Two Sa'ys and the Order of Hajj Actions for the Qarin
Ruling on two sa'ys and order of actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a qarin performing two sa'ys and identify the order of actions (ramy, dhabh, halq) and the Hanafi ikhtilaf on whether reversing the order incurs a dam.

Core Idea
A qarin may perform two sa'ys but does wrong; reversing the sacrifice order incurs a dam according to Abu Hanifa but not according to the Sahibayn.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a qarin who delays the Umrah sa'y and performs two sa'ys, and also addresses the order of the three actions on Yawm al-Nahr: stoning, slaughtering, and shaving. The ruling depends on which view you follow within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing two sa'ys (one for Umrah, one for Hajj) by a qarin. The ruling: permissible (jā'iz) but blameworthy (makruh tanzih) because the Umrah sa'y should be performed immediately after the Umrah tawaf.
2
Understand the prescribed order
On Yawm al-Nahr, the qarin must perform ramy, then dhabh, then halq. This order is required (wajib) according to Abu Hanifa.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on reversing order
If the order is reversed (e.g., shaving before slaughtering), Abu Hanifa holds a dam is required. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold no dam is required. The relied-upon view is of the Sahibayn.
4
Apply to the two sa'ys case
The delay of the Umrah sa'y also involves no penalty (dam), only wrongness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسعى سعيين جاز وأساء، وإذا رمى جمرة العقبة يوم النحر ذبح شاةً أو بدنةً أو سبعها، جاز لأنه أتى بما هو المستحق عليه وأساء بتأخير سعي العمرة وتقديم طواف التحية عليه، ولا يلزمه بذلك شيء. ذبح شاة وجوباً قبل الحلق بشرط أن يقع الذبح في يوم من أيام النحر، فإن حلق قبل الذبح لزمه دم عند الإمام، والذبح قبل الرمي لا يجوز لوجوب الترتيب غير أنه لا يلزمه الدم بعكس الترتيب عندهما، وعنده يجب. وهذا دم القرآن شكراً فيأكل منه. وقوله "أو سبعها" إيماء إلى أن البدنة من الإبل والبقر يمكن أن يشترك فيها سبعة. وقال مالك: لا تجزئ البدنة إلا عن واحد. ولنا: قول جابر: "حججنا مع رسول الله فنحرنا البعير عن سبعة والبقرة عن سبعة" رواه البخاري ومسلم. والجزور أفضل من البقرة والاشتراك في البقرة أفضل من الشاة فيما إذا كانت حصة من البقرة أكثر قيمة من الشاة. والمسألة مقيدة بإرادة الكل للقربة وإن اختلفت جهتها، حتى لو أراد أحدهم اللحم دون القربة لم يجز. وكل دم وجب جبراً لا يكفي فيه سبع البدنة بخلاف دم الشكر.
And he performed two sa'ys: it is permissible but he has done wrong. And when he stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba on Yawm al-Nahr, he slaughters a sheep or a camel (badanah) or its seventh; it is permissible because he has done what is due, but he did wrong by delaying the Umrah sa'y and preferring the tahiyyah tawaf, and nothing is required of him for that. Slaughtering a sheep is obligatory before shaving, provided the slaughter occurs on a day of al-Nahr; if he shaves before slaughtering, a dam is required according to Imam Abu Hanifa. Slaughtering before stoning is not permissible because of the required order, but he does not owe a dam for reversing the order according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), while according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is required. This is the dam of qiran as a thank-offering, so he may eat from it. His saying "or its seventh" indicates that the badanah from camels and cows can be shared by seven. Malik said: a badanah suffices only for one. Our proof: the saying of Jabir: "We performed Hajj with the Messenger of Allah, and we sacrificed a camel for seven and a cow for seven," narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. A camel is better than a cow, and sharing a cow is better than a sheep if the share of the cow is more valuable than the sheep. The matter is conditioned on everyone intending the qurbah even if their specific goals differ, so if one intends only meat without qurbah, it is not valid. Every dam that is obligatory as compensation (jabran) does not suffice with a seventh of a badanah, unlike the dam of shukr.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof for the qarin. The passage states that a qarin performs two sa'ys (one for Umrah and one for Hajj) — it is permissible but Makruh Tanzihan due to delaying the Umrah sa'y. No compensation is required. The sacrifice on Yawm al-Nahr is wajib shukr. The order is: ramy, then dhabh, then halq. If reversed, according to Abu Hanifa a dam is due, but the relied-upon view (Sahibayn) is no dam. The proof for sharing a badanah among seven is the hadith of Jabir. The condition for valid sharing is that all participants intend qurbah. A compensatory dam (e.g., for a violation) cannot be fulfilled with a seventh share, but a thank-offering (dam shukr) can.

Key Terms
سعي (sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah during Hajj or Umrah.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal offered as compensation or thanks.
رمي جمرة العقبة (ramy jamrat al-aqaba): Stoning the largest pillar on Yawm al-Nahr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, if a qarin reverses the order of actions on Yawm al-Nahr (e.g., shaves before slaughtering), what is the ruling?
A) The sacrifice becomes invalid and must be repeated.
B) He owes an additional dam (compensatory sacrifice).
C) No dam is required; his Hajj is valid.
D) He must repeat the Hajj.

Key Takeaway
A qarin may perform two sa'ys but should follow the order of ramy, dhabh, and halq; reversing the order does not incur a dam according to the relied-upon Hanafi view.

The Wajib Sacrifice (Dam al-Qiran) and Sharing a Badanah
Ruling on dam al-qiran and sharing badanah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling on dam al-qiran as a thank-offering, the permissibility of sharing a badanah among seven, and the condition that all participants intend qurbah.

Core Idea
دم القرآن is a thank-offering, not a penalty; sharing a camel or cow among seven is valid if all intend devotion.

This passage continues the discussion of the qarin's sacrifice. It clarifies that the dam al-qiran is a shukr (gratitude) offering, not a compensatory dam. It also addresses the permissibility of sharing a badanah (camel or cow) among seven, citing the hadith of Jabir, and sets the condition that all partners must intend qurbah.

Guided Path
1
Understand the nature of dam al-qiran
It is wajib shukr, not jabr. The qarin may eat from it.
2
Identify the ruling on sharing a badanah
Camels and cows can be shared among seven people for sacrifice. This is based on the practice of the Companions.
3
Examine the condition for valid sharing
All participants must intend qurbah (devotion to Allah). If one intends only to eat meat, the sharing is invalid.
4
Distinguish between dam shukr and dam jabr
A compensatory dam (e.g., for a violation) cannot be fulfilled with a seventh share of a badanah; only a shukr dam can be shared.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسعى سعيين جاز وأساء، وإذا رمى جمرة العقبة يوم النحر ذبح شاةً أو بدنةً أو سبعها، جاز لأنه أتى بما هو المستحق عليه وأساء بتأخير سعي العمرة وتقديم طواف التحية عليه، ولا يلزمه بذلك شيء. ذبح شاة وجوباً قبل الحلق بشرط أن يقع الذبح في يوم من أيام النحر، فإن حلق قبل الذبح لزمه دم عند الإمام، والذبح قبل الرمي لا يجوز لوجوب الترتيب غير أنه لا يلزمه الدم بعكس الترتيب عندهما، وعنده يجب. وهذا دم القرآن شكراً فيأكل منه. وقوله "أو سبعها" إيماء إلى أن البدنة من الإبل والبقر يمكن أن يشترك فيها سبعة. وقال مالك: لا تجزئ البدنة إلا عن واحد. ولنا: قول جابر: "حججنا مع رسول الله فنحرنا البعير عن سبعة والبقرة عن سبعة" رواه البخاري ومسلم. والجزور أفضل من البقرة والاشتراك في البقرة أفضل من الشاة فيما إذا كانت حصة من البقرة أكثر قيمة من الشاة. والمسألة مقيدة بإرادة الكل للقربة وإن اختلفت جهتها، حتى لو أراد أحدهم اللحم دون القربة لم يجز. وكل دم وجب جبراً لا يكفي فيه سبع البدنة بخلاف دم الشكر.
And he performed two sa'ys: it is permissible but he has done wrong. And when he stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba on Yawm al-Nahr, he slaughters a sheep or a camel (badanah) or its seventh; it is permissible because he has done what is due, but he did wrong by delaying the Umrah sa'y and preferring the tahiyyah tawaf, and nothing is required of him for that. Slaughtering before stoning is not permissible because of the required order, but he does not owe a dam for reversing the order according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), while according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is required. This is the dam of qiran as a thank-offering, so he may eat from it. His saying "or its seventh" indicates that the badanah from camels and cows can be shared by seven. Malik said: a badanah suffices only for one. Our proof: the saying of Jabir: "We performed Hajj with the Messenger of Allah, and we sacrificed a camel for seven and a cow for seven," narrated by Bukhari and Muslim. A camel is better than a cow, and sharing a cow is better than a sheep if the share of the cow is more valuable than the sheep. The matter is conditioned on everyone intending the qurbah even if their specific goals differ, so if one intends only meat without qurbah, it is not valid. Every dam that is obligatory as compensation (jabran) does not suffice with a seventh of a badanah, unlike the dam of shukr.

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof for the qarin. The passage states that a qarin performs two sa'ys (one for Umrah and one for Hajj) — it is permissible but Makruh Tanzihan due to delaying the Umrah sa'y. No compensation is required. The sacrifice on Yawm al-Nahr is wajib shukr. The order is: ramy, then dhabh, then halq. If reversed, according to Abu Hanifa a dam is due, but the relied-upon view (Sahibayn) is no dam. The proof for sharing a badanah among seven is the hadith of Jabir. Key Terms
دم القرآن (dam al-qiran): The wajib sacrifice for a qarin as a thank-offering for performing both Hajj and Umrah.
بدنة (badanah): A large sacrificial animal; specifically a camel or cow.
شكر (shukr): Gratitude; the dam al-qiran is a thank-offering.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Fasting as Substitute for Qarin
Ruling on fasting substitute with timing and linguistic dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the fasting substitute for the qarin, explain the preferred timing, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument regarding the interpretation of 'idha raja'tum'.

Core Idea
Fasting for the qarin is a wajib substitute for the sacrifice, with three days ending on Arafah and seven days valid even in Mecca.

This lesson examines the fasting alternative for the qarin (one performing Hajj with combined intentions) who cannot afford the sacrifice. The ruling is derived from the Quran and involves a timing preference as well as a dispute with the Shafi'i school over the interpretation of the phrase 'when you return'. Understanding this ruling clarifies Hanafi methodology in deriving fiqh from the absolute wording of the Qur'an.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled (fasting as a substitute) and its hukm level (wajib) for the qarin unable to sacrifice.
The act is fasting three days during Hajj and seven after completion.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the Quranic verse (Al-Baqarah 2:196) and note its thubut (qat'i) and dalala (zanni) per Hanafi usul.
The verse uses imperative 'fa-siyamu', indicating obligation.
3
Analyze the timing preference
Understand the recommendation to make the last of the three days the day of Arafah, and why earlier fasting suffices due to the absolute wording.
Delaying is preferred to allow ability to get the original sacrifice.
4
Examine the linguistic dispute
Contrast Hanafi interpretation of 'idha raja'tum' (when you finish the rites) with Shafi'i literal 'when you return home'.
Hanafis argue the effect (return) is used for the cause (finishing).
5
Determine the practical effect
Note that Hanafis permit fasting the seven days in Mecca, while Shafi'is require literal return or intention to stay.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العاجز عنه أي الفقير العاجز عن الهدي، صام ثلاثة أيام في الحج وسبعة إذا فرغ بحيث يكون آخر ثلاثة أيام يوم عرفة، وهو الأفضل. والأصل في صوم الأيام العشرة قوله تعالى: {فَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجِّ وَسَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمْ تِلْكَ عَشَرَةٌ كَامِلَةٌ} (البقرة: 196). وإنما شرط أن يكون آخرها يوم عرفة لأن الصوم بدل عن الدم يستحب تأخيره إلى آخر وقته رجاء أن يقدر على الأصل، وهذا بيان الأفضلية، فإن صام قبل ذلك أجزأه لإطلاق النص. وهذه الآية وإن وردت في التمتع فالقران مثله لأنه ترفق بأداء النسكين كالتمتع. فإن قيل: إذا قال تعالى: {فَصِيَامُ ثَلاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجِّ وَسَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمْ} علم أن المجموع عشرة أيام، فأي فائدة في قوله: {تِلْكَ عَشَرَةٌ كَامِلَةٌ}؟ قلنا: الواو قد تستعمل بمعنى "أو" فلو اقتصر على ذكر الثلاثة والسبعة ربما توهم متوهم أنه مخير بين الثلاثة والسبعة، فقال: تلك عشرة كاملة إعلاماً بأن الواجب كلها. وقيل: كان في العرب قلة معرفة بالحساب، وإذا كان الرجل خاطباً صاحبه بأعداد متفرقة جمعها ليسرع فهمه إليها، فالآية من هذا القبيل. و"لو" في قوله "ولو بمكة" متصلة أي وإن كان صام هذه السبعة بمكة متصلة فإنه يجوز. وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز إلا أن ينوي الإقامة فيها، هو يقول: إن المراد بقوله تعالى: {وَسَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمْ} حقيقة الرجوع، ونحن نقول: رجعتم بمعنى فرغتم عن أفعال الحج، والفراغ سبب الرجوع، فأطلق المسبب على السبب. واعلم أن أول وقت الصوم بعد الإحرام بالعمرة في أشهر الحج، وشرط جوازه وجود الإحرام وأن يكون في أشهر الحج؛ لأن كونه متمتعاً شرط بالنص، وقبل الإحرام لا ينعقد سببه.
The one unable: i.e., the poor one unable to afford the hady, he fasts three days during the Hajj and seven when he finishes, such that the last of the three days is the day of Arafah, and that is best. The basis for fasting ten days is the saying of the Most High: 'And whoever cannot find [a sacrifice], then a fast of three days during Hajj and seven when you return; that is ten complete [days]' (al-Baqarah 196). The condition that the last of them be the day of Arafah is because the fast is a substitute for the blood-offering, and it is recommended to delay it to the end of its time hoping to be able to perform the original. This is an explanation of preference; if he fasts before that, it suffices due to the absoluteness of the text. This verse, though revealed for tamattu', applies to qiran as well because it similarly involves ease in performing the two rites. If it is said: when Allah says 'fast of three days during Hajj and seven when you return', it is known that the total is ten days, so what benefit is there in His saying 'that is ten complete'? We reply: the 'waw' is sometimes used in the sense of 'or'; so if He only mentioned the three and the seven, someone might think he has a choice between the three and the seven; so He said 'that is ten complete' to inform that all are obligatory. It was also said that the Arabs had little knowledge of arithmetic, and when a person addresses his companion with separate numbers, he combines them for quick comprehension; thus the verse is of that type. The word 'law' in His saying 'even if in Mecca' is connected, meaning even if he fasts these seven in Mecca continuously, it is permissible. Al-Shafi'i said: it is not permissible unless he intends to stay there; he claims that the meaning of His saying 'when you return' is the literal return. We say: 'return' means 'you have finished the actions of Hajj'; finishing is the cause of return, so the effect is used for the cause. Know that the earliest time for the fast is after assuming ihram for Umrah in the months of Hajj, and the condition for its validity is the existence of ihram and that it be in the months of Hajj, because being mutamatti' is a textual condition; before ihram its cause is not established.
Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This lesson explains the fasting alternative for the qarin who cannot afford the sacrifice. It is a ruling with proof from the Quran. The preferred time for the three days is such that the last is the day of Arafah (9th Dhul Hijjah), but fasting earlier suffices. The verse mentions 'when you return' — the Hanafi view interprets this as 'when you finish the rites', allowing the seven days to be fasted in Mecca. The dispute with Shafi'i is over the interpretation of 'return'; the Hanafi position uses linguistic flexibility. The timing of the fast begins after ihram in the Hajj months.

Key Terms
البدل (al-badal): The fasting substitute for the sacrifice when unable to offer it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if the qarin fasts the three days before the day of Arafah?
A) It is invalid; he must restart.
B) It is valid but Makruh.
C) It is valid and acceptable.
D) It is invalid without repeating.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows the qarin's fasting substitute to be completed even in Mecca, based on interpreting 'return' as finishing the rites.

Dispute on Post-Yawm al-Nahr Fasting for the Qarin
Inter-madhhab dispute on post-Nahr fasting for the qarin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on fasting after Yawm al-Nahr for the qarin and evaluate the Shafi'i and Maliki counter-arguments.

Core Idea
A substitute with a specified time cannot be delayed; once time passes, the obligation reverts to the original.

This passage addresses a critical dispute in Hajj fiqh: what happens if a qarin (one performing Hajj al-Qiran) fails to complete the required fasting before Yawm al-Nahr? The Hanafi school holds that fasting is no longer an option; the hady becomes obligatory. The Shafi'i and Maliki schools disagree, offering alternative solutions. We will examine the proofs and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The qarin had to fast three days during Hajj and seven after, but missed the deadline of Yawm al-Nahr.
2
State the Hanafi position
Fasting after Yawm al-Nahr is invalid; the hady becomes wajib. If unable to sacrifice, two dams are due.
3
Examine the Hanafi dalil
The prohibition of fasting on the days of al-Nahr (11th-13th Dhul Hijjah) and the principle that substitutions are only known from revelation.
The hady is the original substitute; its time-limited replacement (fasting) expired.
4
Compare opposing views
Shafi'i allows qada of the missed fast by analogy with Ramadan; Maliki permits fasting during the days of al-Nahr based on the literal reading of the verse.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Hanafi: must offer hady or two dams; Shafi'i: can fast later; Maliki: fast during al-Nahr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أخرها يوم عرفة، وسبعةً إذا فرغ ولو بمكة، فإن لم يصم إلى يوم النحر تعين الهدي، ولو قدر على الهدي في خلال الصوم أو بعده قبل يوم النحر لزمه الهدي وبطل الصوم إلا أن قدر عليه بعد الحلق قبل صوم السبعة. والقارن بعد الزوال فلا يجوز. تعين الدم أي الهدي ولم يجز الصيام بعده، فإن عجز عن الهدي تحلل وعليه دمان: دم القرآن ودم التحلل قبل الذبح، ولا دم عليه بترك الصوم، ولم يجز الصوم بعده؛ لأن الهدي أصل وقد نقل حكمه، وهو التحلل بعد الذبح إلى بدل موصوف بصفة وقد فات فعاد الحكم إلى الأصل وهو الهدي. وقال الشافعي: يصوم بعد هذه الأيام؛ لأنه صوم مؤقت فيقضي بعد فواته كصوم رمضان. وقال مالك: يصوم في أيام النحر؛ لقوله تعالى: {وَثَلاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجِّ} وهذا وقته. ولنا: النهي المعروف عن صوم هذه الأيام، فجاز تخصيص الآية به؛ لأنه مشهور أو يدخل الصوم نقص لمكان النهي، فلا يتأدى به الكامل كقضاء رمضان والكفارات فإنه لا يجوز فيها. ولو جاز الصوم بعد هذه الأيام لكان بدلا عن الصوم الواجب في أيام الحج، والإبدال لا تعرف إلا شرعاً، وجواز الدم على الأصل.
The last of them is the day of Arafah, and seven when he finishes, even if in Mecca. If he did not fast until the day of al-Nahr, the hady becomes obligatory. And if he becomes able to afford the hady during the fast or after it before the day of al-Nahr, the hady becomes obligatory and the fast is nullified, unless he becomes able after shaving before fasting the seven. The qarin after zawal is not permissible. The blood becomes specified, i.e., the hady, and fasting after it is not valid. If he is unable to afford the hady, he becomes free from ihram (tahallul) and owes two dams: the dam of qiran and the dam of tahallul before slaughtering; but no dam is due for leaving the fast. Fasting after that is not valid because the hady is the original, and its ruling—which is tahallul after slaughter—has been transferred to a substitute described with a quality; that quality has been lost, so the ruling returns to the original, which is the hady. Al-Shafi'i said: he fasts after these days because it is a timed fast, so he makes it up after its time like Ramadan. Malik said: he fasts during the days of al-Nahr because of the verse {and three days during Hajj}, and this is its time. Our proof: the well-known prohibition of fasting on these days, so the verse is specified by it; or the fast is deficient due to the prohibition, so the complete obligation is not fulfilled by it, like making up Ramadan and expiations which are not allowed on those days. And if fasting after these days were allowed, it would be a substitute for the wajib fast during Hajj, but substitutions are only known from revelation, and the permissibility of blood remains on the original.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position: if the qarin has not fasted by Yawm al-Nahr, the sacrifice becomes obligatory and fasting is no longer a valid substitute. If he cannot sacrifice, he performs tahallul and owes two dams (dam al-qiran and dam al-tahallul). The Shafi'i view: he can fast after Yawm al-Nahr as qada like Ramadan fast. The Maliki view: he should fast during the days of al-Nahr. The Hanafi response uses the known prohibition of fasting on the days of al-Nahr (11th, 12th, 13th) as evidence that these are not valid fasting days, and the principle that substitutions are only established by revelation.

Key Terms
دم التحلل (dam al-tahallul): The dam required when a qarin performs tahallul before offering the sacrifice due to inability.
الهدي (al-hady): The sacrificial animal offered by a pilgrim in Hajj al-Qiran or al-Tamattu.
قضاء رمضان (qada' Ramadan): Making up missed fasts of Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a qarin do if he did not fast by Yawm al-Nahr and cannot afford the hady?
A) He must fast after Yawm al-Nahr.
B) He must perform tahallul and offer two dams.
C) He must repeat the Hajj.
D) He owes only one dam.

Key Takeaway
In Hajj al-Qiran, once the deadline for the substitute fasting passes, the obligation reverts to the original hady, and fasting after Yawm al-Nahr is invalid per the Hanafi school.

Rifad of Umrah for Qarin: Dispute with Shafi'i and Internal Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Ruling when qarin abandons Umrah and goes to Arafat, with internal Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on rifad al-umrah for a qarin, distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A qarin who stands at Arafah without completing Umrah owes a dam and must make it up, but intention alone is insufficient.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced ruling within Hajj: what happens when a qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) fails to complete Umrah before proceeding to Arafat. The Hanafi school holds that he becomes a rafid (abandoner) of Umrah and must offer a dam and make up the Umrah. However, there is an internal disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn regarding the precise moment he becomes a rafid. Moreover, Imam al-Shafi'i rejects the entire concept of rifad. By working through the proofs and reasoning, you will gain clarity on thamarah al-khilaf and the tarjih within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act: a qarin who does not enter Mecca or perform Umrah tawaf, and instead goes straight to Arafat and stands there. The ruling: he becomes a rafid (abandoner) of Umrah and must sacrifice a dam (sacrificial animal) and perform the Umrah later (qada). Additionally, the original dam of qiran falls from him.
This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the internal Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the qarin becomes a rafid by merely intending to go to Arafat (even before standing). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that only actual standing at Arafat makes him a rafid. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn.
Compare the analogy: Abu Hanifa analogizes to Friday prayer (salah al-jum'ah) where merely intending to go after praying Zuhr nullifies the Zuhr. The Sahibayn point out that in qiran/tamattu', the intention to go to Arafat is prohibited before completing Umrah, unlike the Friday case where the intention is commanded.
3
Analyse the Shafi'i dispute
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the qarin does not become a rafid because, in his view, the Umrah tawaf is included in the Hajj tawaf. Thus there is no separate obligation to perform Umrah before Hajj, and no penalty for failing to do so. The Hanafi response relies on the hadith of Aisha (RA) who was in qiran or tamattu' and was ordered by the Prophet to abandon her Umrah and do as the pilgrim does.
This hadith provides direct evidence that the Prophet recognized the concept of rifad and commanded it.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under Hanafi law, if a qarin stands at Arafah without completing Umrah, he must sacrifice a dam and later perform a makeup Umrah. The dam of qiran drops. Under Shafi'i, there is no penalty, and he simply completes Hajj without additional obligations.
This affects the muqallid in terms of financial and ritual consequences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن لم يدخل مكة ووقف بعرفة فعليه دم لرفض العمرة وقضاؤها. لأنه لو أداها بعد الوقوف يصير بانيا أفعال العمرة على أفعال الحج وهو خلاف المشروع. لأنه تحلل منها بغير طواف فوجب عليه دم كالمحصر وفيه إيماء إلى سقوط دم القرآن عنه لأنه لم يرفق لأداء النسكين. وقال الشافعي: لا يصير رافضاً بناء على أصله أنه لا يرى الإتيان بأفعال العمرة، وعنده طواف العمرة يدخل في طواف الحج. ولنا أن عائشة ما كانت معتمرة أو قارنة وهو الصحيح، فلما حاضت سرفت قدمت ولم تطف لعمرتها حتى مضت إلى عرفات، فأمرها رسول الله أن ترفض عمرتها وتصنع كما يصنع الحاج. وإنما قيد بالوقوف؛ لأنه بمجرد التوجه لا يصير رافضا لها ما لم يقف بعرفة في الصحيح. وعن أبي حنيفة: يصير رافضا لها بالتوجه إلى عرفات كالسعي إلى الجمعة بعد ما صلى الظهر في منزله؛ فإنه ينتقض به الظهر عنده بمجرد السعي. ووجه قولهما أن الأمر هناك بالتوجه متوجه بعد أداء الظهر، والتوجه في القران والمتعة منهي قبل أداء العمرة فافترقا فلهذا أقيم السعي إلى الجمعة مقامها؛ لكونه مأمورا، بخلاف التوجه إلى عرفة لكونه منهيا عنه قبل أداء العمرة. وقوله "وقضاؤها" مرفوع معطوف على دم، أي فعليه قضاء العمرة؛ لأن الشروع فيها ملزم كالنذر، ويسقط عنه دم القرآن لأنه لم يرفق لأداء النسكين.
If he did not enter Mecca and stood at Arafah, then a dam is due for abandoning the Umrah and its makeup. Because if he were to perform it after standing, he would be building the actions of Umrah upon the actions of Hajj, which is contrary to the prescribed way. Because he exited (tahallul) from it without tawaf, so a dam became obligatory like one obstructed (muhsar). In this there is an indication that the dam of qiran falls away because he did not have the ease to perform the two rites. Al-Shafi'i said: he does not become a rafid (abandoner) based on his principle that he does not see the performance of Umrah actions, and in his view the tawaf of Umrah is included in the tawaf of Hajj. Our proof: Aisha was either performing Umrah or qiran—this is the correct view—and when she menstruated, she entered and did not perform tawaf for her Umrah until she went to Arafat, then the Messenger of Allah ordered her to abandon her Umrah and do as the pilgrim does. The restriction to standing (wuquf) is because mere intention [to go] does not make him a rafid until he actually stands at Arafah in the correct view. According to Abu Hanifa: he becomes a rafid by intending to go to Arafat, like going to Friday prayer after praying Zuhr at home; for that it nullifies the Zuhr by mere intention according to him. The justification of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is that the command there is directed after performing Zuhr, while the intention in qiran and tamattu' is prohibited before performing Umrah, so they differ. Therefore going to Friday prayer is considered a substitute because it is commanded, unlike going to Arafat because it is prohibited before performing Umrah. His saying 'and its makeup' is raised as a conjunct to 'dam', meaning that he must make up the Umrah because starting it is binding like a vow, and the dam of qiran is removed because he did not have ease for performing the two rites.
Source pages p. 280

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute with an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf. The ruling: if a qarin goes to Arafat without completing Umrah (e.g., did not enter Mecca or did not perform Umrah tawaf), he becomes a rafid (abandoner) of Umrah. He owes a dam (like a muhsar) and must make up the Umrah. The dam of qiran falls away. The Shafi'i view: he does not become a rafid because Umrah tawaf is included in Hajj tawaf. The Hanafi proof is from the hadith of Aisha. There is an internal ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn: Abu Hanifa says that merely intending to go to Arafat (even before standing) makes him a rafid, analogy with Friday prayer. The Sahibayn say only actual standing at Arafah makes him a rafid, because intention to go to Arafat is prohibited before Umrah, unlike the Friday case. The relied-upon view is that of the Sahibayn: he is not a rafid until he actually stands at Arafah.

Key Terms
رفض العمرة (rafḍ al-ʿumrah): Abandoning Umrah after having started it in the state of qiran or tamattu'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, when does a qarin become a rafid of Umrah?
A) As soon as he intends to go to Arafat.
B) When he actually stands at Arafah.
C) When he enters Mecca.
D) When he performs tawaf.

Key Takeaway
A qarin who stands at Arafah without completing Umrah must sacrifice a dam and make up the Umrah; mere intention is insufficient per the relied-upon Hanafi view.

Tamattu' Defined and the Obligation of Halq/Taksir in the Hanafi School
Defines tamattu' and discusses obligation of halq/taksir with Malik dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define tamattu', distinguish between the two types (with/without hadi), and state the Hanafi proof for the requirement of halq/taksir for tahallul from 'umrah.

Core Idea
The mutamatti' without hadi must shave or shorten his hair to become halal — the Hanafi proof is the explicit command of the Prophet.

This lesson defines the legal concept of tamattu' (interrupted performance of 'umrah and hajj in one journey). It then focuses on a key ruling: the obligation of halq (shaving) or taqsir (shortening) for the mutamatti' who does not bring a hadi. The passage presents the Hanafi position with its proofs and addresses the opposing view of Imam Malik.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of tamattu'
Identify the two core elements: performing 'umrah in the months of hajj, then becoming halal, then performing hajj in the same year, with a break in between.
The mutamatti' returns to normal life between the two.
2
Distinguish between mutamatti' with and without hadi
The passage states that one who brings a hadi remains in ihram until after hajj; one without is free after halq/taksir.
This distinction is crucial for the ruling on halq.
3
Examine the Hanafi position on halq/taksir
According to Hanafi, halq or taqsir is required for tahallul from 'umrah for the one without hadi. The passage also notes that it may be delayed until Mina.
The ruling is based on the hadith of Ibn Umar.
4
Analyze the dispute with Imam Malik
Malik holds that no halq is needed; tahallul occurs automatically upon completing 'umrah acts. The Hanafi refutation cites Quran and Sunnah.
The thamarah al-khilaf: a Maliki mutamatti' is halal without shaving; a Hanafi is not.
5
Evaluate the evidence
The Hanafi proof includes Quran 48:27 (command to shave) and the explicit command in the hadith of Ibn Umar.
The hadith also shows the distinction between those with and without hadi.

باب التمتع: [من المتاع أو المتعة، وهو الانتفاع أو النفع، وشرعاً ما ذكره المصنف. (ع)] التمتع الترفق بأداء النسكين، وذكره عقب القرآن؛ لاقترانهما في معنى النفع بالنسكين، وقدم القرآن لمزيد فضله، وهو على وجهين: متمتع يسوق الهدي، ومتمتع لا يسوقه، وعرفه الزيلعي بأن يفعل أفعال العمرة الواحدة أو أكثرها في أشهر الحج، ثم عامه ذلك يحج من يلم بأهله إلماماً صحيحاً، والإلمام على نوعين صحيح وفاسد، والصحيح عبارة عن النزول في وطنه من غير بقاء صفة الإحرام، وهذا إنما يكون في التمتع الذي لم يسق الهدي، والفاسد ما يكون على خلافه، وهو إنما يكون فيمن ساق الهدي، وعند محمد ليس من ضرورة صحة الإلمام كونه حلالاً. (فتح)
من الميقات: ليس بشرط للعمرة ولا للتمتع حتى لو أحرم بها من دويرة أهله أو غيرها جازت وصار متمتعاً، وقيل: قيد الميقات للاحتراز عن مكة، فإنه ليس لأهلها تمتع ولا قرآن، وقوله: "فيطوف" ولا بد من كون الطواف أو أكثره في أشهر الحج، وكذا الحلق بعد الفراغ ليس بحتم، بل له الخيار ما لم يسق الهدي، فلو أخر الحلق حتى حج وحلق بمنى كان متمتعاً، وليس من شرط التمتع وجود إحرام العمرة في أشهر الحج بل أداءها فيها أو أكثر أشواطها. وقال مالك: لا حلق على المعتمر؛ بناء على أن التحلل يحصل عند فراغه من العمرة، ساق الهدي أو لم يسق من غير حلق ولا تقصير، ولنا قوله تعالى: مُحَلِّقِينَ رُؤُوسَكُمْ وَمُقَصِّرِينَ (الفتح: ٢٧) نزلت في عمرة القضاء، ولأن النبي عليه هكذا فعل في عمرة القضاء، ولأنها لما كان لها تحريم بالتلبية كان لها تحلل بالحلق أو التقصير. (فتح، مستخلص) فيطوف لها : أي للعمرة سبع أشواط أو أكثر الطواف في أشهر الحج. (ط،ع) وقد حل منها : لأنه لم يبق عليه من أفعالها شيء أي حل منها بالحلق أو التقصير، وهذا إذا لم يسق مع المتعة، أي التخيير بين التحلل أو التقصير وبين أن يبقى محرماً بشرط عدم سوق الهدي، فأما إذا ساق، فإنه لا يتحلل عن إحرام العمرة إلا بعد الفراغ من الحج. وقال مالك: يتحلل عند فراغه من أفعال العمرة ساق الهدي أو لم يسق من غير حلق ولا تقصير، ولنا: حديث ابن عمر لما أنه قال: "تمتع الناس بالعمرة إلى الحج، فلما قدم النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مكة قال للناس: من كان معه هدي، فإنه لا يحل من شيء حرم منه حتى يقضي حجه، ومن لم يكن منكم أهدى فليطف بالبيت وبالصفا والمروة، وليقصر وليتحلل"، متفق عليه [ رمز الحقائق: ١٦٧/١]
Chapter of Tamattu'. It means: that one enters ihram for 'umrah from the miqat, performs tawaf for it, sa'y, and shaves or shortens hair, and has thereby become free from it, and he cuts talbiyah. The commentary: Tamattu' is taking ease in performing the two rites. It follows the discussion of qiran due to their pairing in meaning of benefiting from both rites. It is of two types: one who drives hadi and one who does not. From the miqat: this is not a condition for 'umrah or tamattu'. The tawaf must occur mostly in the months of hajj. Shaving after finishing is not mandatory; he has a choice as long as he does not drive hadi. Malik said: no shaving for the one performing 'umrah. Our proof is the verse and the practice of the Prophet. And we have the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet said: whoever has hadi does not become halal from anything until he completes his hajj; whoever does not have hadi should perform tawaf, sa'y, shorten and become halal.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq defines the legal category of tamattu' (interrupted performance of 'umrah and hajj). It is a ruling statement with proof. The author first gives the lexical and technical definition: performing 'umrah from the miqat, then tawaf, sa'y, and halq/taksir, then becoming halal. The commentator expands that tamattu' is of two types: one who drives hadi (a sacrificial animal) and one who does not. The condition of ihram from miqat is not strict; one can even do it from home and still be a mutamatti'. However, the tawaf must be done in the months of hajj. A key point: halq or taksir is not obligatory for the one without hadi; he may delay it even to Mina if he wishes. This leads to a dispute with Imam Malik, who holds that no shaving or shortening is required at all for 'umrah; the person becomes halal simply by completing the actions. The Hanafi response cites two proofs: Quran 48:27 which commands shaving heads, and the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet distinguished between those with and without hadi, commanding the latter to shorten their hair. This establishes that halq/taksir is an integral part of the tahallul from 'umrah. The commentary also clarifies that if one drives hadi, he remains in ihram until after hajj, a point agreed upon by the hadith.

Key Terms
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Performing 'umrah in the months of hajj, then becoming halal, then performing hajj in the same year, with a break in between (the mutamatti' returns to normal life between 'umrah and hajj).
الحلق (al-halq): Shaving the head; one of the two methods of tahallul (the other being taqsir, shortening hair). Required for the mutamatti' without hadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately upon completing tawaf and sa'y, without any additional act.
B) After performing halq (shaving) or taqsir (shortening) of the hair.
C) Only after completing all acts of hajj.
D) When he returns to his home after 'umrah.

Key Takeaway
The mutamatti' without hadi must shave or shorten his hair to become halal from 'umrah, based on the explicit command in the hadith of Ibn Umar.

Cutting Talbiyah During Umrah
Ruling on cutting talbiyah during 'umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when to cut talbiyah during 'umrah and explain the evidence from the hadith of Ibn Abbas.

Core Idea
Talbiyah ends when tawaf begins — the Black Stone touch marks the moment.

After completing the rituals of 'umrah, a key question arises: when should a mu'tamir stop reciting the talbiyah? This passage establishes the Hanafi position, grounding it in the direct practice of the Prophet, and addresses a competing view from Imam Malik. Understanding this timing ensures that the pilgrim's actions align with the sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is the recitation of talbiyah during 'umrah; the ruling is when to cut it according to Hanafi school.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Ibn Abbas reported by Abu Dawud that the Prophet stopped talbiyah when he touched the Black Stone.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action at that precise moment indicates that this is the prescribed time.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Malik holds various opinions: cutting upon seeing the House or the houses of Mecca.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school adopts the specific hadith as stronger evidence.

(ط)] التقييد به اتفاق؛ لأن المراد أنه إن صام ثلاثة أيام من أشهر الحج، فالحكم لا يختلف إذا صام فيها قبل أن يحرم بالعمرة، وقوله: "لم يجز"؛ لأن سبب وجوب هذا الصوم التمتع؛ لأنه بدل عن الهدي، وهو في هذه الحالة غير متمتع، فلا يجوز أداؤه قبل وجود السبب وقوله: "عن الثلاثة" لم يطلق عدم الجواز؛ لأنه يجوز نفلا. (مسكين، فتح
And he cuts talbiyah: i.e. when he touches the Black Stone in the first circuit. Malik said: he cuts when his sight falls on the House, and in one narration when he sees the houses of Mecca. Our proof is what Abu Dawud narrated from Ibn Abbas that the Prophet would stop talbiyah in 'umrah when he touched the stone, and he said: authentic hadith. Then he enters ihram for hajj on the day of tarwiyah from the sanctuary, performs hajj and sacrifices, and if unable it has passed. It is obligatory because he is mutamatti', i.e. the sacrifice. And before it is better. The commentary explains that the ihram for hajj immediately after 'umrah is not a condition; ihram before tarwiyah is permissible and even better. He does all actions of hajj like the mufrid except he performs raml in tawaf al-ziyarah and sa'y after it because this is his first tawaf in hajj, unlike the mufrid who does raml in tawaf al-qudum.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This passage continues the rulings for the mutamatti' after completing the actions of 'umrah. It covers two issues: cutting talbiyah and the timing of ihram for hajj. Regarding cutting talbiyah, the Hanafi position is that it should be cut when one begins tawaf by touching the Black Stone. This is based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas reported by Abu Dawud. The commentator notes a dispute with Imam Malik, who holds varying views, such as cutting upon seeing the House or the houses of Mecca. The Hanafi rebuttal is the specific practice of the Prophet. After cutting talbiyah and completing 'umrah, the next step is ihram for hajj. The text states that ihram should be on the day of tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah) from the sanctuary (al-Haram). However, the commentary clarifies that it is not a condition to do it immediately after 'umrah; one may do it earlier, which is in fact better due to hastening to good deeds and increased effort. The mutamatti' then performs all the actions of hajj like one who is mufrid (single intention for hajj), except that he performs raml (quick walk with chest out) during tawaf al-ziyarah (the main tawaf of hajj) and sa'y after it, because this is his first tawaf in hajj. In contrast, the mufrid does raml in tawaf al-qudum (arrival tawaf). The passage ends with a note that the ruling for fasting (if unable to sacrifice) is mentioned in the chapter of qiran and will be repeated here.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The chant (Labbayk Allahumma labbayk) recited by someone in ihram; cutting it means stopping the recitation at a specific point.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) As soon as he sees the Kaaba.
B) Upon entering Mecca.
C) When he touches the Black Stone at the beginning of tawaf.
D) After completing sa'y.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi 'umrah: stop talbiyah at the Black Stone — the sunnah is precise.

Timing of Ihram for Hajj for the Mutamatti
Ruling on timing of ihram for hajj for mutamatti'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on when a mutamatti' should enter ihram for hajj and describe the specific actions he performs in tawaf and sa'y.

Core Idea
Ihram for hajj can be earlier than tarwiyah — hastening to good is better.

After completing 'umrah, the mutamatti' must eventually enter ihram for hajj. This lesson clarifies the recommended time (day of tarwiyah) and the flexibility to enter earlier, which is considered superior. It also details how the mutamatti' performs tawaf and sa'y differently from the mufrid.

Guided Path
1
State the recommended time for ihram
Day of tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah), from within the Haram.
2
Explain the permissibility of earlier ihram
It is permissible and even better to enter ihram before tarwiyah.
3
Identify the rationale
Hastening to good deeds and increasing effort (mashaqqah).
4
Note the actions of hajj for the mutamatti'
He avoids tawaf al-qudum but performs raml in tawaf al-ziyarah and sa'y after it.
5
Contrast with mufrid
The mufrid performs raml in tawaf al-qudum, whereas the mutamatti' does it in tawaf al-ziyarah.

Fasting Three Days Before 'Umrah in Tamattu: The Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute on Timing
Ruling on timing of three-day fast in tamattu' and dispute with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school allows fasting the three days of tamattu' after 'umrah and before hajj, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument by analyzing the different interpretations of Quran 2:196.

Core Idea
The cause of the fast (tamattu') permits its performance before hajj actions.

In this lesson, we examine a key inter-madhhab dispute concerning the timing of the optional three-day fast that substitutes for the hadi in tamattu'. The Hanafi school argues that the fast becomes valid as soon as the cause (tamattu') is established, which occurs with the 'umrah in the hajj months. Imam al-Shafi'i, however, insists the fast must be performed after entering ihram for hajj. By analyzing the Quranic verse and the underlying principles, we will see how each school constructs its argument and what practical difference this makes for the pilgrim.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the three-day fast substituted for the hadi in tamattu' is valid as soon as the pilgrim enters ihram for 'umrah within the months of hajj, even before starting the actions of hajj.
This is based on the interpretation that 'fi al-hajj' means 'in the time of hajj'.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees and requires the fast to be performed only after the pilgrim enters ihram for hajj (on 8th Dhul Hijjah or later), because he interprets 'fi al-hajj' as 'during the acts of hajj'.
The Shafi'i position also relies on the principle that bodily worship cannot be advanced before its proper time.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Al-Shafi'i uses the literal wording of the verse 'fasting three days in hajj' and argues that fasting before hajj cannot be considered 'in hajj'. He also draws an analogy: just as monetary expiation can be advanced but bodily acts cannot, the same applies here.
The Hanafi response will address both the linguistic and analogical arguments.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the verse means 'in the season of hajj' because hajj itself is not a proper time for fasting (since the pilgrim is traveling and performing rites). The cause of the fast is tamattu', which is established by 'umrah, so the fast is valid once the cause exists.
They also distinguish between substitution (badal) and expiation (kaffarah): the substitute can follow its cause, while expiation requires the sin to occur first.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Under the Hanafi school, a pilgrim can fast the three days immediately after 'umrah in Shawwal or Dhul Qada, well before hajj begins. Under the Shafi'i school, the same fast must be delayed until after ihram for hajj, which can be several days later.
This affects pilgrims who want to complete the fast early or those who might become able to afford the hadi later.

(مسكين، فتح
الثلاثة التي ذكرت في قوله تعالى: فَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجِّ (البقرة: ١٩٦)؛ لأنه أداء قبل وجود السبب. (ع) وصح أي الصوم من العاجز، ويحسب عن الثلاثة. (ط) قبل أن يطوف أصحابنا جوزوا الصوم قبل أفعال الحج، ولم يجوزوا التكفير قبل الحنث، والشافعي عكس، وقال: الصوم بدني فلا يجوز تقديمه، والتكفير مالي فيجوز تقديمه، وقال: لا يصام إلا بعد الإحرام بالحج؛ لقوله تعالى: فَصِيَامُ ثَلاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجِّ (البقرة: ١٩٦)، وقبل الإحرام بالحج لا يكون صومه في الحج، ولنا أن المراد به وقت الحج؛ لأن الحج لا يصلح ظرفاً للصوم، وهذا قد صام في وقت الحج بعد ما تقرر سببه، وهو التمتع؛ إذ هو طريق إليه فيجوز، وكان ينبغي أن يجوز وإن لم يحرم بالعمرة؛ لأنه وقت الحج، ولكنا شرطنا إحرام العمرة لتحقق السبب، وبقي فيما رواه على الأصل، وقد مر أن الأفضل تأخيره إلى سابع ذي الحجة رجاء القدرة على الهدي. (فتح)
And if he fasts three days from Shawwal and then performs 'umrah, it does not count for the three; but it is valid if he fasts after having entered ihram for 'umrah before tawaf. The commentary: the restriction is agreement; the meaning is that if he fasts three days from the months of hajj, the ruling does not differ if he fasts before ihram for 'umrah. It does not count because the cause of this fasting is tamattu', which is a substitute for the hadi, and in this state he is not a mutamatti', so it is not valid to perform it before the existence of the cause. The three are mentioned in the verse 'fasting three days in hajj'. It is valid if he fasts after having determined the cause, i.e., after ihram for 'umrah. Our companions allowed fasting before the actions of hajj but did not allow expiation before committing an oath, while al-Shafi'i reversed this, saying fasting is bodily so cannot be performed in advance, but monetary expiation can be advanced. He said: one should not fast except after ihram for hajj due to the verse. Our argument: the meaning is the time of hajj, because hajj is not itself a time for fasting. So he has fasted in the time of hajj after the cause was established, i.e., tamattu', which is a way to it, so it is permissible. It would be permissible even without ihram for 'umrah, but we condition ihram for 'umrah to confirm the cause.
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the timing of the three-day fast that substitutes for the hadi (sacrifice) in tamattu'. The verse states 'fasting three days in hajj' (Quran 2:196). The Hanafi position allows fasting these three days after one has entered ihram for 'umrah but before the actions of hajj, as long as it is within the months of hajj. The cause (sabab) of this fast is tamattu' itself, which is established by performing 'umrah in hajj months. Therefore, once the 'umrah is initiated, the cause exists, and the fast can be performed even before hajj actions. However, if one fasts before ihram for 'umrah (e.g., in Shawwal before starting 'umrah), it does not count for the tamattu' obligation, though it may count as nafl (voluntary) fasting. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that fasting is a bodily worship and cannot be performed before its time, so he requires the fast to be after ihram for hajj. He analogizes with monetary expiation, which can be advanced, but fasting cannot. The Hanafi response is that the verse means 'during the time of hajj' (the months), not 'after ihram for hajj'. Since the cause (tamattu') is present after ihram for 'umrah, the fast is valid even before ihram for hajj. The text also notes that it is better to delay the fast until the 7th of Dhul Hijjah in case one can afford the hadi and thus avoid the fast altogether.

Key Terms
فِي الْحَجِّ (fi al-hajj): Interpreted by Hanafis as 'in the time of hajj' (months of hajj: Shawwal, Dhul Qada, first 10 days of Dhul Hijjah).
سبب الصوم (sabab al-sawm): The cause that necessitates the fasting: tamattu' itself, which is established by performing 'umrah in the hajj months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is the three-day fast for tamattu' valid to start?
A) Only after completing all actions of hajj.
B) Only after ihram for hajj (on 8th Dhul Hijjah).
C) After entering ihram for 'umrah within the months of hajj.
D) At any time during the year, even before the umrah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the substitute fast after 'umrah because the cause (tamattu') is established, while Shafi'i requires it after hajj ihram due to a different textual interpretation.

The Obligations of the Mutamatti' Without a Sacrificial Animal
States basic rulings for tamattu' and timing of ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for the mutamatti' who does not bring a hadi, identify the correct time and place for his ihram for hajj, and distinguish his rites from those of the mufrid.

Core Idea
Without a sacrificial animal, the mutamatti' must fast 3 days during hajj and 7 after; his ihram for hajj begins on the day of tarwiyah from within the Haram.

This lesson covers the rulings for a person performing tamattu' (combining umrah and hajj in one journey) who does not bring a sacrificial animal (hadi). The Hanafi school specifies the timing and place of ihram for hajj and the required fasting as a substitute for the sacrifice. These details ensure the pilgrim's rites are valid according to the sunna.

Guided Path
1
Identify the mutamatti' and his obligation regarding the hadi
Define mutamatti' as one who performs umrah during hajj months then hajj in the same year without returning home. He must slaughter an animal; if unable, he must fast 3 days during hajj and 7 after returning home.
The fasting substitute is ten days total.
2
Pinpoint the time and place for ihram for hajj
The primary time is yawm al-tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah) and place is within the Haram. Earlier ihram is permissible and better, as it hastens to good.
Ihram from the masjid is superior.
3
Understand the special rites of the mutamatti' during hajj
The mutamatti' does not perform tawaf al-qudum, but performs ramal (brisk walking) in tawaf al-ziyarah and sa'y after it, because this is his first tawaf in hajj.
The mufrid performs ramal in tawaf al-qudum instead.
4
Apply the fasting substitute correctly
Fasting three days during hajj (any three days before Eid) and seven days after returning home. Fasting three days of Shawwal before umrah does not count.
The fast must be in the same hajj season.

Chapter of Tamattu'. With the first tawaf, then he assumes ihram for hajj on the day of tarwiyah from the Haram, and he performs hajj and slaughters (an animal), and if unable, then it has passed, obligatory because he is mutamatti', i.e., (he slaughters) instead of the animal, and before it is better. And if he fasted three days of Shawwal and then performed umrah, it does not count for the three (days), but it is valid if after he had assumed ihram (for umrah) before performing tawaf. [Commentary continues.]
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on tamattu'. It states the ruling of the mutamatti' who does not bring a sacrificial animal (hadi). The mutamatti' first performs umrah, then on the day of tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah) he assumes ihram for hajj from within the Haram. He then performs hajj and slaughters an animal. If he cannot afford an animal, he fasts three days during hajj and seven after returning home, as previously mentioned. The commentator explains that 'from the Haram' is required because the mutamatti' is like a Makki in that respect. It is better to assume ihram before the day of tarwiyah due to hastening to good. The mutamatti' performs all actions of hajj like a mufrid (one performing hajj only) except that he performs ramal (quick walking) in tawaf al-ziyarah and sa'y after it because that is his first tawaf in hajj, unlike the mufrid who does ramal in tawaf al-qudum.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti'): A person who performs umrah during the months of hajj and then performs hajj in the same year without returning home in between.
يوم التروية (yawm al-tarwiyah): The 8th day of Dhul Hijjah, when pilgrims begin the rites of hajj by heading to Mina.
يرمل (yaramil): To walk briskly with short steps while moving the shoulders, done in the first three circuits of a tawaf in which ramal is prescribed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) On the day of tarwiyah from within the Haram
C) On the day of Eid
D) Before entering Makkah

Key Takeaway
The mutamatti' without hadi must fast ten days, and his ihram for hajj is optimally from the Haram on yawm al-tarwiyah.

Fasting Three Days for Tamattu': Timing and Dispute with Shafi'i
Rules on fasting three days when unable to sacrifice, and a dispute with Shafi'i.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for the validity of the three fasts (after ihram for umrah) and explain the Hanafi proof and response to the Shafi'i argument regarding the timing.

Core Idea
The three fasts for tamattu' are valid only after ihram for umrah, because the cause must precede the substitute.

When a mutamatti' cannot afford a sacrificial animal, he must fast three days during hajj. But when exactly? The Hanafi school holds that these fasts must be performed after assuming ihram for umrah, because the obligation arises from tamattu', which is only realized with umrah. This lesson examines the ruling and the key dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who argues the fasts must be after ihram for hajj. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies how the Hanafi school interprets the Quranic phrase 'fi al-hajj' and its application.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafis rule that the three fasts are valid only after ihram for umrah, during the months of hajj, even before ihram for hajj. Identify the condition: ihram for umrah actualizes the cause (tamattu').
Note the cause: tamattu' requires both umrah and hajj; umrah establishes the cause.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the fasts must be performed after ihram for hajj, not merely during the hajj season. His proof: the verse 'fasting three days during hajj' and the nature of fasting as bodily worship.
Shafi'i interprets 'fi al-hajj' as the rituals of hajj.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i relies on the literal meaning of 'during hajj' (fi al-hajj) and the principle that bodily worship cannot be performed before its time.
He analogizes with other bodily acts like prayer.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Hanafis argue that 'during hajj' refers to the time of hajj, not the rituals, because the rituals themselves are not a valid container for fasting. Moreover, the cause (tamattu') is already present after umrah, making the fast permissible by analogy with financial expiations.
The key usul point: linguistic interpretation + sabab.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: according to Shafi'i, a mutamatti' cannot fast until after he enters ihram for hajj; according to Hanafi, he can fast immediately after his umrah, any time during the hajj months. The Hanafi position allows more flexibility and is relied upon for fatwa.
This difference affects the ease of worship for pilgrims.

Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage deals with the fasting alternative for the mutamatti' who cannot afford a sacrificial animal. The ruling is that the three fasts must be performed during the months of hajj and after assuming ihram for umrah, because the cause of obligation is tamattu' (combining umrah and hajj). Fasting before ihram for umrah does not fulfill the requirement because the cause is not yet present. The commentator notes a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i. The Shafi'i school holds that the three fasts can only be performed after assuming ihram for hajj, citing the verse 'fasting three days during hajj'. The Hanafi response is that 'in hajj' means 'in the time of hajj' (the months of hajj), not literally during the rituals. Since the cause (tamattu') is already established by performing umrah, the fast can be done before the day of tarwiyah. The Hanafis require ihram for umrah for the cause to be actualized. It is recommended to delay the fast until the seventh of Dhul Hijjah in hopes of being able to sacrifice.

Key Terms
تمتع (tamattu'): A type of hajj where one performs umrah during the hajj months and then performs hajj in the same year.
هدي (hadi): A sacrificial animal (usually a sheep or cow) offered by a mutamatti' or qarin, or as a penalty for missing a wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The three fasts for tamattu' are valid only after ihram for umrah, based on the interpretation that 'fi al-hajj' means the time of hajj, not the rituals, as argued by the Hanafi school.

Rulings for the Mutamatti' Who Brings Hadi: Taqlid, Ish'ar, and Tahlul
Rules on taqlid, ish'ar, and prohibition of tahlul for the mutamatti' with hadi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for the mutamatti' who brings hadi regarding taqlid, ish'ar, and tahlul, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on ish'ar.

Core Idea
The mutamatti' with hadi must not do tahlul after umrah; taqlid is recommended, ish'ar is hasan per fatwa.

In this passage, we learn the specific rules for a mutamatti' who brings a sacrificial animal (hadi). The Prophet himself practiced this form of Hajj. The text covers the preferred method of marking the animal (taqlid vs. ish'ar) and the crucial rule that such a pilgrim does not exit ihram after umrah but remains in ihram until Hajj. There is a well-known intra-Hanafi difference on ish'ar between Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling context
Determine who the mutamatti' with hadi is and what key actions are involved: bringing a sacrificial animal, performing umrah, then Hajj without tahlul in between.
This sets the stage for the specific rules.
2
Understand the preference for taqlid over tajlil
Analyze why taqlid (garlanding) is preferred over tajlil (covering). The evidence includes Quranic mention and Prophetic practice as narrated by Aisha.
Taqlid is a confirmed sunnah.
3
Analyze the dispute on ish'ar
Identify ish'ar (marking by cutting the hump) and the three positions: Abu Hanifa (makruh due to muthla), Sahibayn (hasan due to Prophetic practice), Shafi'i (sunnah).
Focus on the reasoning: mutilation vs. following the Prophet.
4
Evaluate the tarjih (weighting) of the dispute
Understand why the fatwa is on the Sahibayn's view: the Prophetic practice outweighs the general prohibition of muthla, and the practice was continued by the Companions.
The fatwa allows ish'ar but it is not mandatory.
5
Apply the rule on tahlul
Learn that bringing the hadi prevents tahlul after umrah. The Prophet's statement 'If I had known... I would not have brought the hadi' indicates that driving the hadi prevents exiting ihram.
This is an exception to the normal tamattu' procedure.

(ع) ولا تمتع إلخ: أما عدم مشروعية التمتع لقوله تعالى: ﴿ذَلِكَ لِمَنْ لَمْ يَكُنْ أَهْلُهُ حَاضِرِي الْمَسْجِدِ الْحَرَامِ ، (البقرة: ١٩٦) بناء على أن اسم الإشارة يعود على التمتع، واللام فيه تدل عليه؛ إذ لو كان عائدا على الهدي والصوم - كما ذهب إليه الشافعي صح للمكي التمتع والقرآن - لقال: على من لم يكن"؛ لأن اللام تستعمل -
If he wants to drive the hadi: explanation of the second type, and it is better following the Prophet... and he garlanded his camel with a waterskin or a sandal, and does not mark (ish'ar), and he does not perform tahlul after his umrah, and he assumes ihram for hajj on the day of tarwiyah, and before it is more beloved. So when he shaves on the day of Nahr, he is released from his two ihrams. And there is no tamattu' or qiran for a Makki...
Source pages p. 282

Commentary
This passage covers additional rulings for the mutamatti' who brings a sacrificial animal (hadi). The Prophet himself performed tamattu' and drove the hadi. The preferred method is to garland (taqlid) the animal with a piece of an old shoe or waterskin, as the Prophet did, and not to mark it by cutting or wounding (ish'ar). However, there is a dispute: Abu Hanifa considers ish'ar makruh (disliked) because it amounts to mutilation (muthla) which is forbidden even on a hostile enemy, so how can it be done on an animal that is sacred? Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it good (hasan) because the Prophet himself did it. The fatwa is according to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that it is hasan. The commentator also notes that the preference for taqlid over tajlil (covering with a cloth) is because taqlid is mentioned in the Quran. Additionally, when one brings the hadi, it is sunnah not to perform tahlul (to exit ihram) after umrah; instead, one remains in ihram until the completion of hajj. This is based on the Prophet's statement: 'If I had known what I know now, I would not have brought the hadi, and I would have made it umrah and performed tahlul.' This indicates that bringing the hadi prevents tahlul. Finally, the passage states that tamattu' and qiran are not valid for a Makki (resident of Makkah) based on the verse: 'That is for him whose family is not present in the Sacred Mosque.'

Key Terms
تقليد (taqlid): Placing a garland (usually of leather or a piece of old shoe) around the neck of the sacrificial animal.
إشعار (ish'ar): Making a small cut on the hump of the camel or cow to let blood flow, marking it as a sacrificial animal.
مثلة (muthla): Mutilation or disfigurement of a living being, which is prohibited in Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi position on ish'ar?
A) It is makruh (disliked)
B) It is haram (forbidden)
C) It is hasan (good, recommended)
D) It is sunnah (emphasized sunnah)

Key Takeaway
The mutamatti' with hadi does not perform tahlul after umrah; taqlid is recommended, and ish'ar is hasan per the fatwa.

Taqlid: Garlanding the Hady
States the ruling on taqlid and its evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on taqlid for the mutamatti' and explain why taqlid is preferred over tajlil using Quranic and hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Taqlid is wajib for the mutamatti' driving a camel hady; it is preferred over covering because it is mentioned in the Quran.

When a mutamatti' drives a sacrificial animal (hady), the Hanafi school requires him to garland it (taqlid) with a leather strap or sandal. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof from the Quran and Sunnah, and the reasoning behind preferring taqlid over covering the animal (tajlil).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act the passage commands (taqlid of the hady) and its legal level (wajib based on the imperative form).
The matn uses the imperative 'ساق وقلد' indicating obligation.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
Find the proofs cited in the commentary: Quran 5:2 (the prohibition of violating the garlands) and the hadith of Aisha.
The Quranic verse is presented as evidence for the virtue of taqlid.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (legal inference)
Understand how the Quranic prohibition of violating garlands (qala'id) implies the legitimacy and commendability of the act of garlanding.
The verse forbids desecrating the garlands, indicating their sanctity.
4
Compare taqlid with tajlil
Note why taqlid is preferred: it has explicit Quranic mention and Prophetic practice, while tajlil (covering) is also permissible but inferior.
The commentary states 'التقليد أحب من التجليل' (taqlid is more beloved than covering).
5
Apply the restriction to camels
Recognize that taqlid is only for the badanah (camel), not for sheep, as indicated by 'الغنم لا تقلد'.
Sheep are not garlanded in the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب التمتع وساق وقلد بدنته بمزادة أو نعل، ولا يُشعر، ولا يتحلل بعد عمرته، ويحرم بالحج يوم التروية، وقبله أحبّ، فإذا حلق يوم النحر حلّ من إحراميه.
المتمتع السائق للهدي في وهو أحب من التجليل؛ لأن له ذكراً في القرآن، قال تعالى: ﴿وَلا الْهَدْيَ وَلا الْقَلائِدَ﴾ (المائدة:٢)، ولحديث عائشة والله ما كنت أقتل قلائد هدايا رسول الله ، ولأن التقليد يراد به التقرب، والتجليل قد يكون لغيره كالزينة وغيرها، وفي التقييد بالبدنة إشارة إلى أن الغنم لا تقلد. (فتح، مستخلص) وساق: هديه وهو أفضل من قوده؛ لأنه عليها أحرم بذي الحليفة وساق الهدي معه. (ط،ع) بمزادة: أي قطعة جلد، والتقليد أحب من التجليل؛ لأنه عليه قلد البدنة. (ع، ط) ولا يشعر الأنه مكروه، وقالا حسن والإشعار أن يضرب بحربة في أحد جانبي سنام البدنة حتى يخرج منه الدم ثم يلطخ سنامها. (ط)] الإشعار مكروه عند أبي حنيفة، وقالا حسن، وقال الشافعي: سنة، وجه الكراهة لما وهي حرام فيمن يجب قتله كالحربي، فكيف من لا تحل عقوبته والفتوى على قولهما: إنه حسن، وإنما لم يكن عندهما سنة مع فعله عليه وفعل أصحابه؛ لأنه عارضه دليل الكراهة وهو كونه مثلة، فقلنا بحسنه، ونقل عن الطحاوي: أنه لا يكره أصل الإشعار عند أبي حنيفة، وهو كيف يكره مع ما ورد فيه من الأخبار؟ إنما كره إشعار أهل زمانه؛ لأنه رآهم يبالغون فيه على وجه يخشى منه السراية ثم الإشعار من جانب اليسار عند أبي يوسف، ومن اليمين عند الشافعي، وكل ذلك مروي عنه عليه، وقيل: إنما كره أبو حنيفة إيثاره على التقليد، كما كره إيثار نكاح الكتابية على نكاح المسلمة رمز الحقائق: ١٦٧/١] (فتح) من المثلة، ولا يتحلل: أي المحرم إذا ساق الهدي فيسن له أن لا يتحلل بعد عمرته؛ لقوله عليها: "لو استقبلت من أمري ما استدبرت لما سقت الهدي ولجعلتها عمرة وتحللت منها"، وهذا ينفي التحلل عند سوق الهدي، وكان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم تمتع وساق الهدي، فلما فرغ من أفعال العمرة أمر أصحابه أن يحلقوا رؤوسهم ويتحللوا، وهم كانوا ينتظرون هل يتحلل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قبل أن يفتح بأفعال الحج، فقال: "لو استقبلت" إلخ يعني لو علمت في ابتداء الشروع في العمرة أن هذه معارض يعرض لي في هذا الوقت، لما سقت الهدي، ولأن لسوق الهدي تأثيراً في إثبات الإحرام ابتداء، فلأن يؤثر في إبقائه عليه أولى بخلاف ما إذا لم يسق الهدي فله أن يتحلل؛ لأنه لا مانع له من التحلل. تبيين الحقائق: ٣٤٣/٢] (مستخلص فتح التروية كما ذكر في الذي لا يسوق الهدي. (ع) وقبله أحب أي إحرام التمتع قبل يوم التروية أحب مطلقا؛ لأن فيه مسابقة إلى الخير وزيادة في المشقة. (ع) إحراميه: أي إحرام العمرة وإحرام الحج؛ لأن الحلق في الحج كالسلام في الصلاة فيتحلل به عنهما. (ع)
Chapter of Tamattu': He drove and garlanded his sacrificial animal with a leather water-skin or sandal, and does not mark it, and does not exit ihram after his 'umrah, and enters ihram for hajj on the day of Tarwiyah, and before it is more beloved. Then when he shaves on the day of Nahr, he becomes free from both his ihrams. The mutamatti' who drives the hady...
Source pages p. 283

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proofs from the Kanz al-Daqaiq. It outlines the obligations and recommendations for someone performing tamattu' while leading a sacrificial animal. The matn commands taqlid (garlanding) with a leather piece or sandal, prohibits ish'ar (marking by cutting the hump), prohibits tahallul after 'umrah, and specifies the time for ihram for hajj on the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah), with ihram before that being mustahabb. The commentary expands each clause: taqlid is preferred over covering (tajlil) because it is mentioned in the Quran (Maidah:2) and in the hadith of Aisha. Ish'ar is makruh according to Abu Hanifa but hasan according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn), while al-Shafi'i considers it sunnah. The fatwa is on the view of the two companions (hasan). The prohibition of tahallul is based on the Prophet's statement 'Had I known what I know now, I would not have driven the hady' which indicates that driving the hady prevents tahallul. Shaving on the day of Nahr completes both ihrams, like the salam in prayer.

Key Terms
التقليد (taqlid): Garlanding the sacrificial animal with a leather strap or sandal to mark it for sacrifice.
التجليل (tajlil): Covering the sacrificial animal with a cloth or covering.
البدنة (badanah): A camel (male or female) used as a sacrificial animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on taqlid for a mutamatti' driving a camel hady?
A) It is sunnah mu'akkadah.
B) It is wajib.
C) It is mubah.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
Taqlid is a wajib act for the mutamatti' who drives a camel hady, based on Quranic and hadith evidence, and it is preferred over covering the animal.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Ish'ar
Explains the intra-Hanafi dispute on ish'ar and the fatwa ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding ish'ar, state the mufta bihi ruling, and explain the reason for the difference.

Core Idea
Ish'ar is a disputed act among the Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa considers it makruh, but the fatwa is on the view of the two companions that it is hasan.

The practice of marking the sacrificial animal by cutting its hump (ish'ar) is a subject of intra-Hanafi disagreement. While Abu Hanifa considers it makruh due to the prohibition of mutilation, his two leading students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regard it as hasan (recommended). The later Hanafi fatwa adopts the view of the two companions. This lesson unpacks the proofs and the reasoning behind the tarjih.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the three opinions: Abu Hanifa (makruh), Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (hasan), and al-Shafi'i (sunnah).
The text clearly records all three views.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Understand the basis for makruh: ish'ar is considered a form of mutilation (muthlah) which is prohibited, even when dealing with enemies.
The commentary states 'وهي حرام فيمن يجب قتله كالحربي' (it is forbidden for even those who must be killed, like a combatant).
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
Their view that it is hasan is based on the Prophetic practice, as the Prophet himself performed ish'ar.
Despite the general prohibition, the act is from the Prophet, so it cannot be makruh; it becomes hasan.
4
Understand the tarjih (preference)
The text explicitly states 'والفتوى على قولهما: إنه حسن' (the fatwa is on their view: it is hasan), because the Prophetic practice takes precedence over the general prohibition.
The later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin) have relied on the Sahibayn's view.
5
Note the cross-madhhab comparison
al-Shafi'i considers it sunnah, which is stronger than hasan. The Hanafi school does not elevate it to sunnah due to the conflicting evidence of mutilation.
The thamarah al-khilaf is that Shafi'is treat ish'ar as a confirmed sunnah, while Hanafis treat it as merely recommended.

Key Terms
الإشعار (ish'ar): Marking the sacrificial animal by making a small incision on one side of its hump until blood flows.
المثلة (muthlah): Mutilation; disfiguring a living being.

Checkpoint
What is the mufta bihi (operative fatwa) ruling on ish'ar in the Hanafi school according to this passage?
A) Makruh tanzihi.

D) Sunnah mu'akkadah.

Prohibition of Tahallul and Timing of Ihram for the Mutamatti' Leading Hady
States the prohibition of tahallul and the timing of ihram for hajj for the mutamatti' with hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a mutamatti' who drives a hady cannot perform tahallul after 'umrah, and state the preferred time for entering ihram for hajj.

Core Idea
Driving a hady prevents a mutamatti' from exiting ihram after 'umrah, and ihram for hajj is best on the day of Tarwiyah or earlier.

The mutamatti' who brings a sacrificial animal (hady) is bound by additional rules that affect his ihram. He may not perform tahallul (exit ihram) after completing 'umrah, unlike a mutamatti' without a hady. Furthermore, the timing of entering ihram for hajj is specified: the day of Tarwiyah (8th of Dhul Hijjah) is the latest, but entering earlier is recommended. This lesson explores the reasoning behind these rules based on the Prophet's practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on tahallul
The text states 'ولا يتحلل بعد عمرته' (he does not exit ihram after his 'umrah). This is the ruling for the mutamatti' driving hady.
Contrast with the mutamatti' without hady, who may do tahallul.
2
Find the dalil from the Prophet's action
The commentary cites the Prophet's statement: 'لو استقبلت من أمري ما استدبرت لما سقت الهدي ولجعلتها عمرة وتحللت منها' (Had I foreseen my situation, I would not have driven the hady and would have made it 'umrah alone). This shows that driving the hady necessitates remaining in ihram.
The Prophet did tamattu' with hady and did not do tahallul.
3
Apply the analogy (qiyas)
The commentary argues that if hady can initiate ihram (as in qiran), it can also prolong it (as in tamattu'). So it prevents tahallul.
Qiyas: The hady has an effect in establishing ihram at the start, so it has an effect in maintaining it.
4
Determine the timing of ihram for hajj
The matn says 'ويحرم بالحج يوم التروية، وقبله أحبّ' (he enters ihram for hajj on the day of Tarwiyah, and before it is more beloved). So there are two times: preferred (before) and permissible (on that day).
The reason given: 'المسابقة إلى الخير' (competing in goodness) and 'زيادة في المشقة' (increase in effort).
5
Understand the final ruling on shaving
When he shaves on the day of Nahr, he becomes free from both ihrams (umrah and hajj) simultaneously, like the salam in prayer.
Shaving is the concluding act that releases him from both.

This passage is a ruling statement with proofs from the Kanz al-Daqaiq. It outlines the obligations and recommendations for someone performing tamattu' while leading a sacrificial animal. The matn commands taqlid (garlanding) with a leather piece or sandal, prohibits ish'ar (marking by cutting the hump), prohibits tahallul after 'umrah, and specifies the time for ihram for hajj on the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah), with ihram before that being mustahabb. The commentary expands each clause: taqlid is preferred over covering (tajlil) because it is mentioned in the Quran (Maidah:2) and in the hadith of Aisha. Ish'ar is makruh according to Abu Hanifa but hasan according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn), while al-Shafi'i considers it sunnah. The fatwa is on the view of the two companions (hasan). The prohibition of tahallul is based on the Prophet's statement 'Had I known what I know now, I would not have driven the hady' which indicates that driving the hady prevents tahallul. Shaving on the day of Nahr completes both ihrams, like the salam in prayer.

Key Terms
التحلل (tahallul): Exiting the state of ihram by shaving or trimming hair.
يوم التروية (Yawm al-Tarwiyah): The 8th day of Dhul Hijjah, when pilgrims traditionally enter ihram for hajj.
يوم النحر (Yawm al-Nahr): The 10th day of Dhul Hijjah, the day of sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it most beloved (أحبّ) for a mutamatti' with hady to enter ihram for hajj?
A) On the day of Tarwiyah.
B) Before the day of Tarwiyah.
C) After the day of Tarwiyah.
D) On the day of Arafah.

Key Takeaway
A mutamatti' who drives a hady must remain in ihram continuously from 'umrah until the day of Nahr, and entering ihram for hajj before the day of Tarwiyah is recommended for additional reward.
