Returning Home After Umrah and Its Effect on Tamattu'
Ruling on returning home after umrah and its effect on tamattu', with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tamattu' when the mutamatti' returns home after umrah and distinguish the effect of driving a hady on the validity of tamattu'.

Core Idea
Returning home after umrah invalidates tamattu' without a hady; with a hady, continuity of ihram preserves it according to the relied-upon view.

A key issue for pilgrims performing tamattu' is whether returning to their hometown after umrah disrupts the continuity between umrah and hajj. The Hanafi school holds that the answer depends on whether the pilgrim drove a sacrificial animal (hady). This lesson unpacks the ruling and the internal Hanafi disagreement on this point, explaining the reasoning of the imams and the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and base ruling
The text begins by stating the case of a mutamatti' who returns to his hometown after completing umrah without driving a hady. Here tamattu' is invalidated (batil). Recognize that this is the undisputed foundation.
2
Distinguish the case with a hady
When the pilgrim does drive a hady, the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) rule that tamattu' remains valid. This is the mufta bihi position. Understand the key difference: the hady preserves the ihram.
3
Analyze the dissent of Muhammad al-Shaybani
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani has a separate transmission holding that tamattu' is invalid even with a hady. His reasoning is that the pilgrim actually visited his family between the two rites, making the journey two separate trips.
4
Trace the proof of the two companions
The two companions argue that the return is not a valid visit because the pilgrim remains in ihram until the hady is sacrificed. Consequently, the return is obligatory, not voluntary, and does not break the continuity of tamattu'.
The text contrasts with the case of a Makkan who drives a hady but is not considered mutamatti' because the return is not obligatory for him.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and cross-madhhab comparison
The relied-upon position is that of the two companions: tamattu' is not invalidated if a hady is driven. Note that Malik and Ahmad side with Muhammad's other opinion, but within the Hanafi school, the fatwa is on the side of the companions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن يليها، فإن عاد المتمتعُ إلى بلده بعد العمرة و لم يَسُق الهدي بطل تمتعه، وإن ساق لا هذا عندهما، وقال محمد يبطل؛ لأنه ألم بأهله بين النسكين وأداهما بسفرين، فصار كمن لم يسق الهدي، والهدي لا يمنع صحة الإلمام ألا ترى أن المكي إذا قدم من الكوفة بعمرة، وساق هدياً لا يكون متمتعاً، ولهما: أن إلمامه غير صحيح؛ لأنه محرم ما لم ينحر عنه الهدي، وكان العود مستحقاً عليه، وذلك يمنع صحة الإلمام بأهله بخلاف ما إذا لم يسق الهدي أو ساق وهو مكي؛ لأن العود غير واجب عليه، وقول مالك وأحمد مثل قول محمد. (عيني، فتح)
And whoever is adjacent to it [Mecca], then if the mutamatti' returns to his town after 'umrah and did not drive the hady, his tamattu' is invalidated. And if he drove it, it is not invalidated according to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani], but Muhammad [al-Shaybani] says it is invalidated because he has visited his family between the two rituals and performed them with two journeys...
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of returning to one's hometown after completing 'umrah on the validity of tamattu'. The matn states that if the mutamatti' returns to his hometown after 'umrah without driving a hady, his tamattu' is invalidated. If he drove a hady, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions), it is not invalidated. However, Muhammad (al-Shaybani) has a separate opinion that even with a hady, tamattu' is invalidated because he genuinely visited his family between the two rituals, making it two separate journeys. The two companions argue that his visit is not valid because he is still in ihram until the hady is sacrificed, so the return is obligatory, not optional. This is contrasted with the case of a Makkan who comes from Kufa with an 'umrah and drives a hady—such a person is not considered a mutamatti' because returning is not obligatory. The opinion of Malik and Ahmad is similar to Muhammad's. The relied-upon fatwa is the view of the two companions.

Key Terms
الإلمام (ilamam): Briefly visiting one's family; if done properly, it breaks the continuity of tamattu'.
الهدي (hady): A sacrificial animal driven by the pilgrim; in this context, it preserves the continuity of ihram when returning home.
تمتع (tamattu'): A type of hajj where one performs umrah first, then hajj in the same journey, with a break in ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is invalidated.
B) It is not invalidated.
C) It is invalidated only if he returns before shaving.
D) It becomes qiran.

Key Takeaway
Driving a hady preserves the continuity of ihram, so returning home after umrah does not invalidate tamattu' according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Partial Tawaf Before Hajj Months: Hanafi Validation of Tamattu'
Ruling on tamattu' with partial tawaf before hajj months

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on tamattu' validity when partial tawaf is performed before the hajj months and distinguish it from the Shafi'i and Maliki views.

Core Idea
The majority of tawaf circuits must occur during the hajj months; ihram can precede them.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in hajj: a person begins umrah before the hajj months but only completes part of the tawaf, then finishes it during the hajj months and performs hajj. Is such a person considered a mutamatti'? The Hanafi school says yes, while the Shafi'i and Maliki schools have different requirements. Understanding this dispute clarifies the conditions of tamattu' and the role of ihram timing.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact Hanafi ruling: if a person performs at least three circuits of tawaf before the hajj months and completes the remaining circuits during the months, then performs hajj, he is a mutamatti'.
The key is that the majority of tawaf (three out of four parts, i.e., three out of seven circuits) must be performed within the hajj months.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their views
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i requires the entire umrah ihram to occur within the hajj months, so he rejects tamattu' in this case. Imam Malik requires all seven circuits to be performed during the hajj months.
Shafi'i considers ihram a rukn; Maliki focuses on completion of actions.
3
Follow the opponents' proofs
Understand the Shafi'i proof: ihram is a rukn, so it must be performed within its designated time. The Maliki proof: the entire tawaf must be in the hajj months.
These proofs stem from different definitions of the conditions for tamattu'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis argue that ihram is a condition (shart), not a rukn, so it can be performed early. What matters is that the majority of the actions (most circuits) occur in the hajj months.
The Hanafi reasoning is based on the principle that conditions can precede their actions.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, tamattu' is valid; under Shafi'i it is invalid; under Maliki it is only valid if all seven circuits are performed during the hajj months.
This affects whether the pilgrim must offer a dam, repeat the umrah, or change the type of hajj.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن طاف أقل أشواط العمرة قبل أشهر الحج وأتمها فيها وحج، كان متمتعاً
أقل أشواط من أربعة بأن طاف ثلاثة أشواط . (ط، ع) وأتمها أي العمرة بأن طاف أربعة أشواط بقية. (ع) وحج أي من أحرم بالحج بعد فراغه من العمرة (ط) كان متمتعاً : أي من أحرم بالعمرة قبل أشهر الحج، وطاف لها ثلاثة أشواط، فتركها حتى دخل أشهر الحج، فأتمها فيها، ثم حج من عامه كان متمتعاً عندنا، وقال الشافعي: إحرام العمرة قبل أشهر الحج لا يجوز، فلا يكون متمتعاً عنده وقال مالك: لو طاف للعمرة سبعة أشواط كان متمتعاً، فالشافعي يعتبر الإحرام بناء على أصله أن الإحرام من الأركان، ومالك يعتبر إتمام العمرة في أشهر الحج، ولنا: أن الإحرام شرط فيصح تقديمه على أشهر الحج وإنما يعتبر أداء الأفعال فيها، وقد وجد الأكثر، وللأكثر -
And whoever performs the minimum number of circumambulations of 'umrah before the months of hajj and completes it during them and performs hajj, he is a mutamatti'. The minimum number of circumambulations is three out of four...

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute about the validity of tamattu' when some tawaf of 'umrah is performed before the hajj months (Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, Dhul Hijjah). The Hanafi position is that it is valid: if one enters ihram for umrah before these months, performs at least three tawaf circuits (considered the minimum part of the umrah), then delays completing the umrah until the hajj months, then completes the remaining circuits and performs hajj in the same year, he is a mutamatti'. Al-Shafi'i holds that ihram for umrah before the hajj months is not valid, so he would not be a mutamatti'. Malik requires that all seven circuits of tawaf be performed during the hajj months. The Hanafi reasoning: ihram is a condition that can be performed early; what matters is that the actions (most of tawaf) occur in the hajj months. Since most of the tawaf (three out of four parts) is done in the weeks? Actually the text says three out of four? The commentary says the minimum is three circuits (out of four parts or out of seven? The matn says 'less than the number of circuits' meaning less than the full four circuits? Actually the wording is 'aqall ashwat min arba'a' meaning less than four circuits, i.e., three circuits. So the majority (three out of four) is done in the months. The last sentence is cut off but the argument is that the majority of the actions suffice.

Key Terms
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-hajj): The months of hajj: Shawwal, Dhul Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis validate tamattu' when the majority of tawaf circuits occur during the hajj months, even if some circuits were done before, distinguishing them from Shafi'i and Maliki.

Returning Home After 'Umrah in Tamattu': The Hady Dispute
Explains the ruling of tamattu' when the pilgrim returns home after 'umrah, with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tamattu' when the pilgrim returns home after 'umrah, and explain the dispute between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the role of the hady.

Core Idea
Returning home invalidates tamattu' unless a hady is brought; the hady preserves continuity.

In this passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq, the author addresses a critical nuance in tamattu': what happens if the mutamatti' returns to his hometown after performing 'umrah? The ruling hinges on whether he brought a sacrificial animal (hady) or not. We will explore the intra-Hanafi disagreement on this point and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its basic ruling
The act is tamattu', where a pilgrim performs 'umrah during Hajj months then performs Hajj in the same year. The basic ruling: if the mutamatti' returns home without a hady, tamattu' becomes invalid.
This ruling is agreed upon within the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the condition of the hady
The hady (sacrificial animal) is normally required of the mutamatti'. The dispute arises when the mutamatti' brings a hady and returns home: does this invalidate tamattu'?
3
Examine the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They hold that tamattu' remains valid if a hady is brought, because the mutamatti' is still in ihram until the hady is sacrificed, so the return is not a valid break.
Their evidence: the obligation to return to Makkah remains.
4
Examine the position of Muhammad al-Shaybani
Muhammad holds that tamattu' is invalid even with a hady, because the mutamatti' performed two separate journeys, and the hady does not prevent the return from being a valid coming to family.
He analogizes to a Makkan returning with a hady, who is not a mutamatti'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as it is the established Zahir al-Riwayah view. This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.
This position is supported by the majority of the Tabi'in and later Hanafi authorities.

Chapter of Tamattu'. And those near [Makkah]: if the mutamatti' returns to his town after 'umrah and did not bring the hady, his tamattu' becomes invalid; and if he brought [the hady], it does not [become invalid]. And whoever circumambulates fewer circuits of 'umrah before the months of Hajj and completes them therein and performs Hajj, he is a mutamatti'. ... His tamattu' is not invalidated by the prohibitions of ihram. = Then he entered these months, 'umrah in the months of Hajj, in what is for us, not in what is against us. And we have the choice in tamattu'. As for the hady, it is obligatory without choice. And as for the lack of permissibility of qiran, it cannot be conceived except with a defect in one of the two rites; because if he combines them in the Haram, he has violated a condition of ihram for 'umrah because its miqat is the hill; and if he enters ihram for both from the hill, he has violated the miqat of Hajj because its miqat is the Haram. Nevertheless, if a Makkan performed tamattu' or qiran, he owes a compensatory dam, he does not eat from it, and fasting does not suffice for him in case of inability. His statement: 'those near' meaning: and not for those who are inside the miqat. These people have only ifrad according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i as previously. Malik said: those who are inside the miqat up to the Haram may do tamattu' and qiran, and Ahmad said likewise, because they are not among the residents of the Sacred Mosque. Our evidence: they are followers of them and in their ruling since their residences are inside the miqat like the people of Makkah. From Ibn 'Umar: there is no tamattu' for the people of Makkah, and similar from Ibn 'Abbas and Ibn al-Zubayr. (Fath) 'And those near' meaning: and not for those near Makkah, who are the people of what is inside the miqat up to the Haram; the pronoun refers to Makkah indicated by 'al-Makki'. ('Ayni) His tamattu' becomes invalid because tamattu' is seeking ease by dropping one of the two journeys; so if he initiates a journey for each one, this meaning is invalidated. Or we say: when he comes to his family with a valid coming, the return is no longer obligatory upon him, so he becomes like the people of Makkah. This is if he shaves [his head]. If he returns to his family before shaving, then performs Hajj in that year before shaving in his family, then he is a mutamatti'. Al-Shafi'i said: it does not invalidate tamattu' because according to him, coming to family does not invalidate tamattu', so he permitted tamattu' for the people of Makkah. Our evidence: invalidation is reported from Ibn 'Umar, Sa'id ibn Jubayr, 'Ata', Ibrahim, and others from the majority of the Tabi'in. (Fath) 'And if he brought [the hady], it does not' – this is according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad? Actually 'inda huma = according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?) No, 'inda huma refers to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf? The text says: 'this is according to the two' and then 'Muhammad said it becomes invalid' because he came to his family between the two rites and performed them with two journeys, so he is like one who did not bring the hady. The hady does not prevent the validity of coming to family. Do you not see that if a Makkan comes from Kufa for 'umrah and brings a hady, he is not a mutamatti'. And for the two: his coming to family is not valid because he is in ihram until the hady is sacrificed, and the return is obligatory upon him, and that prevents the validity of coming to family, unlike the case when he did not bring the hady or brought it while being a Makkan because the return is not obligatory upon him. The statement of Malik and Ahmad is like that of Muhammad.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq with its commentary from al-Fath and al-'Ayni discusses the ruling on tamattu' when the mutamatti' returns to his hometown after performing 'umrah. The passage opens by stating the chapter on tamattu'. The core ruling: if a mutamatti' returns to his home after 'umrah without having brought a sacrificial animal (hady), his tamattu' becomes invalid. If he brought a hady, it does not become invalid. The commentary then explains who is included in 'those near' (man yaliha): people who live inside the miqat, i.e., within the boundaries of the sacred territory but not in Makkah itself. They are treated like the people of Makkah and cannot do tamattu' or qiran; only ifrad is permitted for them. This is the Hanafi position, opposed by al-Shafi'i who permitted tamattu' for them, and by Malik and Ahmad who permitted tamattu' and qiran for them on the grounds that they are not 'residents of the Sacred Mosque'. The Hanafi response relies on the authority of Ibn 'Umar, Ibn 'Abbas, and Ibn al-Zubayr. The passage then delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute: if the mutamatti' brought a hady, does returning home invalidate tamattu'? According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf ('indahuma), it does not. But according to Muhammad al-Shaybani, it does. His reasoning: the mutamatti' has still performed the two rites with separate journeys, and the hady does not prevent the invalidity. He analogizes to a Makkan who comes from Kufa for 'umrah with a hady: such a person is not a mutamatti' because he did not combine the journeys. The counter-argument of the two (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that the mutamatti' is still in ihram until the hady is sacrificed, so his return to his family is not a 'valid coming' (ilmaam saheeh), and thus the obligation to return to Makkah remains. Therefore, he is still considered as having combined the journeys. The passage ends by noting that Malik and Ahmad agree with Muhammad. The relied-upon position for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, as it is the majority view and supported by the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
التمتع (al-tamattu'): Performing 'umrah during the months of Hajj and then performing Hajj in the same year with a break in between, requiring a hady.
الإلمام (al-ilmaam): Coming to one's family, i.e., returning home temporarily between the two rites.
المُتَمَتِّع (al-mutamatti'): One who performs tamattu': performs 'umrah first, then Hajj.
الهَدْي (al-hady): A sacrificial animal brought by the mutamatti' or qarin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, what is the ruling on tamattu' if the mutamatti' returns to his hometown after 'umrah and has brought a hady?
A) It becomes invalid.
B) It remains valid.
C) It becomes invalid unless he shaves his head.
D) It becomes invalid if he stays more than one day.

Key Takeaway
Returning home after 'umrah invalidates tamattu' unless a hady is brought, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Majority of Tawaf Circuits and Tamattu'
Determines when a person is considered mutamatti' based on number of tawaf circuits performed before the months

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a person becomes a mutamatti' based on the number of 'umrah tawaf circuits performed before the months of Hajj, and explain why the majority (three out of four) is sufficient.

Core Idea
Three out of four tawaf circuits before the months are treated as the whole, making tamattu' valid (Hanafi).

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario in Hajj jurisprudence: a person performs 'umrah tawaf partially before and partially during the months of Hajj. The Hanafi school applies the principle 'al-akthar yanazzilu manzilat al-kull' (the majority takes the ruling of the whole) to determine tamattu'. The passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary clarifies the conditions and contrasts with the positions of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is performing 'umrah tawaf partly before and partly within the months of Hajj. The Hanafi ruling: the person becomes a mutamatti' if the majority (three out of four) of the circuits occur within the months.
The majority principle is key.
2
Locate the condition
The condition for valid tamattu' according to Hanafi is that the majority (akthar) of the tawaf circuits must be performed during the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah).
The minimum considered is three out of four circuits.
3
Understand the Hanafi proof
The proof is the usul principle that the majority takes the ruling of the whole (al-akthar yanazzilu manzilat al-kull). Additionally, ihram is a condition (shart), not a pillar (rukn), so it can validly precede the months.
This contrasts with Shafi'i and Maliki.
4
Contrast with opposing schools
Al-Shafi'i requires that ihram for 'umrah occur within the months because he considers ihram a pillar. Malik requires that all seven circuits be within the months.
These differences stem from different usul positions.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: a person who performs three circuits before and one after is mutamatti' in Hanafi, but not in Shafi'i or Maliki. If the majority (e.g., four) are before, he is not mutamatti' in any school.
Also affects the obligation of hadi (sacrifice).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقل أشواط من أربعة بأن طاف ثلاثة أشواط . (ط، ع) وأتمها أي العمرة بأن طاف أربعة أشواط بقية. (ع) وحج أي من أحرم بالحج بعد فراغه من العمرة (ط) كان متمتعاً : أي من أحرم بالعمرة قبل أشهر الحج، وطاف لها ثلاثة أشواط، فتركها حتى دخل أشهر الحج، فأتمها فيها، ثم حج من عامه كان متمتعاً عندنا، وقال الشافعي: إحرام العمرة قبل أشهر الحج لا يجوز، فلا يكون متمتعاً عنده وقال مالك: لو طاف للعمرة سبعة أشواط كان متمتعاً، فالشافعي يعتبر الإحرام بناء على أصله أن الإحرام من الأركان، ومالك يعتبر إتمام العمرة في أشهر الحج، ولنا: أن الإحرام شرط فيصح تقديمه على أشهر الحج وإنما يعتبر أداء الأفعال فيها، وقد وجد الأكثر، وللأكثر -

حكم الكل، وخصت المتعة بأداء أفعال العمرة في أشهر الحج؛ لأنها كانت متعينة للحج قبل الإسلام فأدخل الله سبحانه العمرة فيها؛ إسقاطاً للسفر الجديد عن الغرباء، فكان اجتماعهما في وقت واحد في سفر واحد رخصة وتمتعاً. (فتح، مستخلص)
وبعكسه لا: أي لو طاف العمرة أربعة أشواط قبل الأشهر، ثم أتمها فيها لم يكن متمتعاً؛ لأن للأكثر حكم الكل، وكان أكثر أشواط العمرة قبل الأشهر، فلم يجتمع له الحج والعمرة فيها لا حقيقة ولا حكماً، أما الحقيقة؛ فلأنه لم يوجد فيها إلا بعضها وكذا حكماً؛ لأنها فرغت تقديراً؛ لأنها صارت بحال لا تحتمل الفساد بالجماع، والحاصل: أنه إن وجد أكثر طواف العمرة في أشهر الحج، فقد اجتمع له الحج والعمرة فيها، فيصير متمتعاً، وإن كان الأكثر قبلها لم يجتمعا ، ولا يكون متمتعاً. (فتح، مستخلص)
The minimum circuits [needed] from four is that he performed three circuits. (T, 'A) And completed it, i.e., the 'umrah, by performing the remaining four circuits. ('A) And performed Hajj, i.e., he entered ihram for Hajj after finishing the 'umrah. (T) He is a mutamatti': meaning, he who entered ihram for 'umrah before the months of Hajj, performed three circuits of tawaf for it, then left it until the months of Hajj entered, then completed it therein, then performed Hajj in that year — he is a mutamatti' according to us. Al-Shafi'i said: entering ihram for 'umrah before the months of Hajj is not permissible, so according to him he is not a mutamatti'. And Malik said: if he performed seven circuits for 'umrah, he is a mutamatti'. So al-Shafi'i considers ihram, based on his principle that ihram is a pillar; Malik considers completing the 'umrah within the months of Hajj. Our evidence: ihram is a condition, so it is valid to perform it before the months of Hajj; rather, the performance of actions is considered within them, and the majority [of circuits] has occurred. And for the majority - Book of Hajj, Chapter of Tamattu' - and its opposite is not. They are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and ten [days] of Dhu al-Hijjah. And it is valid to enter ihram for Hajj before them. The months of Hajj i.e., for Hajj are the months of Hajj. The ruling of the whole is that tamattu' is specified by performing the actions of 'umrah within the months of Hajj; because they were designated for Hajj before Islam, so Allah included 'umrah in them, to drop the new journey for the strangers, so their coming together in one time and one journey was a concession and a tamattu'. (Fath, Mustakhlas) And its opposite is not: meaning, if he performed four circuits of 'umrah before the months, then completed it therein, he is not a mutamatti'; because the majority has the ruling of the whole, and the majority of the circuits of 'umrah were before the months, so Hajj and 'umrah are not combined for him therein, neither in reality nor in ruling. As for reality: because only some of it existed therein; likewise in ruling: because it is considered completed by estimation, since it became such that it does not admit of invalidation by intercourse. The conclusion: if the majority of the tawaf of 'umrah occurs in the months of Hajj, then Hajj and 'umrah are combined for him therein, so he becomes a mutamatti'; if the majority was before them, they are not combined, and he is not a mutamatti'. (Fath, Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage discusses the condition for tamattu' regarding the timing of tawaf for 'umrah. The core issue: if a person enters ihram for 'umrah before the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah), and performs some circuits of tawaf before the months, and completes the rest within the months, then performs Hajj in the same year, is he validly a mutamatti'? The Hanafi ruling: yes, if he performed at least three circuits (the majority of the four required circuits) before the months, and completes the remaining four within the months, he is a mutamatti'. This is because the majority (three out of four) has the ruling of the whole. Al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding that ihram for 'umrah cannot precede the months of Hajj because for him ihram is a pillar. Malik holds that all seven circuits must be within the months. The commentary then explains the rationale: the purpose of tamattu' is to combine the two rites in one journey, dropping the second journey. If the majority of the 'umrah tawaf is within the months, the combination is achieved. The passage also clarifies that if the majority of circuits were before the months (e.g., he performed four circuits before and three after), then he is not a mutamatti'. The relied-upon Hanafi position uses the principle 'al-akthar yanazzilu manzilat al-kull' (the majority takes the ruling of the whole).

Key Terms
الأكثر (al-akthar): The majority; here, three out of four circuits of tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person performs three circuits of 'umrah tawaf before the months of Hajj and the remaining one circuit within the months, then performs Hajj, what is his status?
A) He is a mutamatti'.
B) He is not a mutamatti'.
C) He is a qarin.
D) His 'umrah is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school applies the principle that the majority of 'umrah tawaf circuits determines the validity of tamattu' when circuits are split before and during the months of Hajj.

Definition of the Months of Hajj and Ruling on Ihram Before Them
Defines months and rules on early ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the months of Hajj, explain why ihram before them is valid but disliked, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i and Maliki views.

Core Idea
Ihram before the months of Hajj is valid but disliked; it is a condition, not a pillar.

This passage defines the months of Hajj and explores the permissibility of entering ihram before those months. The Hanafi school holds that ihram is a condition, not a pillar, so it may precede the time, though doing so is disliked. We will examine the evidence for this position and compare it with the views of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik.

Guided Path
1
Identify the months of Hajj according to the Hanafi school
From the text, extract the three components: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. Note the minor intra-Hanafi difference from Abu Yusuf (ten nights and nine days).
The plural 'months' can refer to less than three, as in the Quranic inheritance verse.
2
Understand the ruling on ihram before the months
The Hanafi position is that such ihram is valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh tanzihan). Validity is because ihram is a condition (shart), similar to purification before prayer. Dislike arises from fear of violating prohibitions over a prolonged period.
The condition- vs pillar-based reasoning is central to the dispute.
3
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Al-Shafi'i argues that ihram is a pillar, so it cannot precede the time; if done, it becomes 'umrah. The Hanafi response: (a) ihram is not a pillar but a condition, and (b) one intention cannot produce two distinct obligations.
The thamarah al-khilaf: a Shafi'i would need to complete 'umrah and re-enter ihram for Hajj.
4
Evaluate the Maliki position on the months
Malik holds that the entire month of Dhu al-Hijjah is included. The Hanafi refutation uses the hadith 'The greatest day of Hajj is the Day of Sacrifice' to show that the Day of Sacrifice is part of the month, and that the plural can be applied to less than three.
The benefit of specifying these months: no Hajj actions are valid outside them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي شوال: لما ذكر أن المتمتع يترفق بأداء النسكين في أشهر الحج احتاج إلى أن يبين الأشهر، فقال: هي شوال وذو القعدة وعشر ذي الحجة بكسر الحاء أي عشرة أيام منها، فإنه إذا حذف التمييز جاز التذكير، وعن أبي يوسف: أنها عشر ليال وتسعة أيام من ذي الحجة؛ لأن الحج يفوت بطلوع الفجر من يوم النحر، ولو كان وقته باقياً لما فات، قلنا: روي عن النبي له الا الله أنه قال: "يوم الحج الأكبر يوم النحر" فكيف يكون يوم الحج الأكبر ولا يكون من شهره؟ ولأن وقت الركن وهو طواف الزيارة - يدخل وقته بطلوع الفجر من يوم النحر، فكيف يدخل وقت ركن الحج بعد ما خرج وقت الحج؟ وفوات الوقوف بطلوع الفجر من يوم النحر؛ لكونه مؤقتاً به بالنص، فلا يجوز في غيره، ألا ترى أن يوم التروية من أشهر الحج ولا يجوز الوقوف فيه؛ لما قلنا. وقال مالك: ذو الحجة كلها من أشهر الحج؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿الْحَجِّ أَشْهُرٌ مَعْلُومَاتٌ (البقرة: ١٩٧) بلفظ الجمع، وأقله ثلاثة، قلنا: يجوز إطلاق لفظ الجمع على ما دون الثلاث، كقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنْ كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ (النساء: ۱۱)، فالأخوان يحجبانها من الثلث إلى السدس، ويجوز أن ينزل البعض منزلة الكل يقال: "رأيت زيداً سنة كذا"، وإنما رآه في ساعة منها، وفائدة التوقيت بهذه الأشهر: أن شيئاً من أفعال الحج لا يجوز إلا فيها، حتى إذا صام المتمتع أو القارن ثلاثة أيام قبل أشهر الحج لا يجوز، وكذا السعي بين الصفا والمروة عقب طواف القدوم لا يجوز إلا فيها عيني، فتح) ذي الحجة: كذا روي عن العبادلة الثلاثة وعبد الله بن الزبير . (ع) وصح الإحرام به إلخ لأنه شرط فأشبه الطهارة في حق جواز التقديم على الوقت لا مطلقاً، قوله: "وكره" وجه الكراهة خوف الوقوع في محظورات الإحرام بطول الزمان، أو نقول له شبه بالركن، فصحة الإحرام قبلها بالنظر لكونه شرطا والكراهة بالنظر لكونه أشبه الركن وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز الإحرام قبلها، وينعقد عمرة؛ لأن الإحرام للحج ركن عنده، فلا يجوز قبل الوقت، واستشكل على قوله : ينعقد عمرة"؛ لأن العمرة فرض كالحج، فكيف ينعقد بتحريمة فرض الحج فرض آخر؟ هذا خلف. (عيني، فتح)
And they are Shawwal: when it was mentioned that the mutamatti' seeks ease by performing the two rites in the months of Hajj, he needed to clarify the months, so he said: they are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and ten [days] of Dhu al-Hijjah – with kasra on the ha' – meaning ten days from it, because when the specification is omitted, it is permissible to use the masculine. And from Abu Yusuf: that they are ten nights and nine days of Dhu al-Hijjah because Hajj is missed with the dawn of the Day of Sacrifice, and if its time were remaining it would not be missed. We say: it is narrated from the Prophet ﷺ that he said: 'The greatest day of Hajj is the Day of Sacrifice.' So how can the greatest day of Hajj be and not be from its month? And because the time of the pillar, which is Tawaf al-Ziyarah, enters with the dawn of the Day of Sacrifice, so how can the time of the pillar of Hajj enter after the time of Hajj has exited? And the deficiency of 'Arafah is by the dawn of the Day of Sacrifice because it is time-bound by the text, so it is not permissible in other times. Do you not see that the Day of Tarwiyah is from the months of Hajj and it is not permissible to stand at 'Arafah on it, due to what we said. And Malik said: Dhu al-Hijjah in its entirety is from the months of Hajj, based on His statement: 'The Hajj is [during] well-known months' (al-Baqarah 2:197) in the plural form, and its minimum is three. We say: it is permissible to apply the plural to less than three, like His statement: 'But if he has brothers, then for his mother the sixth' (al-Nisa' 4:11), so two brothers exclude her from the third to the sixth. And it is permissible to treat the part as the whole. It is said: 'I saw Zayd in such-and-such a year,' even though he saw him only in an hour of it. And the benefit of specifying these months is that nothing of the actions of Hajj is permissible except in them, such that if the mutamatti' or qarin fasts three days before the months of Hajj, it is not permissible. Likewise, the sa'y between al-Safa and al-Marwah after the tawaf of arrival is not permissible except in them. ( 'Ayni, Fath) Dhu al-Hijjah: Thus narrated from the three 'Abdullahs and 'Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr. ('Ayni) And it is valid to enter ihram for Hajj before them, etc. because it is a condition, so it resembles purification in terms of permissibility of preceding the time, not absolutely. His statement: 'and it is disliked' – the reason for dislike is fear of falling into the prohibitions of ihram due to the length of time, or we say: it resembles a pillar. So the validity of ihram before them is with consideration to its being a condition, and the dislike is with consideration to its resemblance to a pillar. Al-Shafi'i said: it is not permissible to enter ihram before them, and it becomes 'umrah because ihram for Hajj is a pillar according to him, so it is not permissible before the time. And it is problematic that his statement 'it becomes 'umrah' because 'umrah is an obligation like Hajj, so how can it become another obligation by the intention of the obligation of Hajj? That is contradictory. ( 'Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage defines the months of Hajj (ashhur al-hajj) and discusses the ruling on ihram for Hajj before these months. The text states that the months are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. There is a slight difference from Abu Yusuf, who said it is ten nights and nine days (i.e., up to the dawn of the Day of Sacrifice). The commentary refutes Malik's view that the entire month of Dhu al-Hijjah is included, by using the principle that the plural can apply to less than three, as in the Quranic inheritance verse. The key proof is the hadith 'The greatest day of Hajj is the Day of Sacrifice', which shows that the Day of Sacrifice is part of the months. The passage then explains that ihram for Hajj before these months is valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh). This is because ihram is a condition (shart) for Hajj, and conditions can precede their act (like purification before prayer). However, it is disliked because it resembles a pillar (rukn) in time-specificity, and entering ihram too early risks violations. Al-Shafi'i holds that ihram cannot precede the months at all; if one does so, it becomes 'umrah, not Hajj. The Hanafi response: ihram is not a pillar but a condition, so it can precede. The objection to Shafi'i's view is that one intention cannot make two different obligations (Hajj and 'umrah).

Key Terms
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-hajj): The months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah.
الإحرام (al-ihram): The intention to enter the state of consecration for Hajj or 'umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) The ihram becomes 'umrah automatically.
D) The ihram is valid and recommended.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ihram for Hajj before the months is valid but disliked, because ihram is a condition, not a pillar.

Definition of the Months of Hajj: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the First Ten Days of Dhu al-Hijjah
Defining the months of Hajj and the dispute with Imam Malik

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of the months of Hajj and explain the proofs used against the Maliki position.

Core Idea
The months of Hajj are three, but Dhu al-Hijjah is only partial—the first ten days.

The timing of Hajj is critical: actions performed outside the designated months are invalid. The Hanafi school defines these months precisely, drawing on the Quran, hadith, and linguistic reasoning. This passage presents the definition and defends it against both an internal (Abu Yusuf) and an external (Maliki) challenge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The author states that the months of Hajj are three: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. Note that 'ten' here means the first ten days, not the entire month.
The wording 'عشر ذي الحجة' uses the masculine 'عشر' because the noun it modifies (أيام) is implied.
2
Examine the intra-Hanafi disagreement (Abu Yusuf)
Abu Yusuf holds that the months include ten nights and nine days of Dhu al-Hijjah, arguing that Hajj is missed by dawn of the day of Nahr. The author responds with the hadith 'The greater day of Hajj is the day of Nahr' and the fact that Tawaf al-Ziyarah begins at dawn, proving the day of Nahr is within the months.
The majority Hanafi position (mufta bihi) includes the day of Nahr as part of the months.
3
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Malik
Imam Malik argues that all of Dhu al-Hijjah is from the months because the Quran says 'known months' (plural, implying at least three). The Hanafi response uses linguistic examples (e.g., 'brothers' in inheritance verse for two) and the convention of using a part to represent the whole.
The practical difference: Malik allows Sa'y on 11th and 12th; Hanafis restrict to first ten days.
4
Understand the legal benefit (thamarah al-khilaf)
The timing affects the validity of Hajj actions. For example, fasting for tamattu' or performing Sa'y after Tawaf al-Qudum are only valid within these months. If done outside, they must be repeated or are invalid.
This underscores the importance of precise definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهي شوّال وذو القعدة وعشر ذي الحجة بكسر الحاء أي عشرة أيام منها، فإنه إذا حذف التمييز جاز التذكير، وعن أبي يوسف: أنها عشر ليال وتسعة أيام من ذي الحجة؛ لأن الحج يفوت بطلوع الفجر من يوم النحر، ولو كان وقته باقياً لما فات، قلنا: روي عن النبي له الا الله أنه قال: "يوم الحج الأكبر يوم النحر" فكيف يكون يوم الحج الأكبر ولا يكون من شهره؟ ولأن وقت الركن وهو طواف الزيارة - يدخل وقته بطلوع الفجر من يوم النحر، فكيف يدخل وقت ركن الحج بعد ما خرج وقت الحج؟ وفوات الوقوف بطلوع الفجر من يوم النحر؛ لكونه مؤقتاً به بالنص، فلا يجوز في غيره، ألا ترى أن يوم التروية من أشهر الحج ولا يجوز الوقوف فيه؛ لما قلنا. وقال مالك: ذو الحجة كلها من أشهر الحج؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿الْحَجِّ أَشْهُرٌ مَعْلُومَاتٌ (البقرة: ١٩٧) بلفظ الجمع، وأقله ثلاثة، قلنا: يجوز إطلاق لفظ الجمع على ما دون الثلاث، كقوله تعالى: ﴿فَإِنْ كَانَ لَهُ إِخْوَةٌ فَلِأُمِّهِ السُّدُسُ (النساء: ۱۱)، فالأخوان يحجبانها من الثلث إلى السدس، ويجوز أن ينزل البعض منزلة الكل يقال: "رأيت زيداً سنة كذا"، وإنما رآه في ساعة منها، وفائدة التوقيت بهذه الأشهر: أن شيئاً من أفعال الحج لا يجوز إلا فيها، حتى إذا صام المتمتع أو القارن ثلاثة أيام قبل أشهر الحج لا يجوز، وكذا السعي بين الصفا والمروة عقب طواف القدوم لا يجوز إلا فيها عيني
They are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and ten of Dhu al-Hijjah - with kasrah of the ha (i.e., ten days from it), because when the specification is omitted, masculine gender is permissible. From Abu Yusuf: they are ten nights and nine days of Dhu al-Hijjah, because Hajj is missed by the dawn of the day of Nahr, and if its time were still remaining, it would not be missed. We said: It is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he said: 'The greater day of Hajj is the day of Nahr.' So how could the greater day of Hajj not be from its month? And because the time of the pillar, which is Tawaf al-Ziyarah, enters with the dawn of the day of Nahr, so how could the time of a pillar of Hajj enter after the time of Hajj has exited? And the missing of Wuquf occurs by dawn of the day of Nahr because it is time-bound by text, so it is not permissible at other times. Do you not see that the day of Tarwiyah is from the months of Hajj, yet Wuquf is not permissible on it, for what we said. Malik said: All of Dhu al-Hijjah is from the months of Hajj, due to His (exalted) saying: 'The Hajj is (in) known months' (Al-Baqarah: 197) in the plural form, and the minimum of that is three. We said: It is permissible to use the plural for less than three, as in His saying: 'But if he has brothers, then for his mother is the sixth' (An-Nisa: 11), so two brothers prevent her from the third to the sixth. And it is permissible to consider a part as the whole; it is said: 'I saw Zaid in such-and-such a year,' though he only saw him in a portion of it. And the benefit of timing these months is that none of the actions of Hajj are permissible except in them, such that if a mutamatti' or qarin fasts three days before the months of Hajj, it is not permissible. Similarly, Sa'y between Safa and Marwah after Tawaf al-Qudum is not permissible except in them. (Ayni)
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof defining the months of Hajj. The author states that the months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah. He clarifies that 'ten' means ten days, and the word 'ten' is masculine because the specified noun is omitted. He then reports a narration from Abu Yusuf that the months are ten nights and nine days of Dhu al-Hijjah, reasoning that Hajj is missed by dawn of the day of Nahr, so if the month included the whole day, it would not be missed. The Hanafi response is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) called the day of Nahr 'the greater day of Hajj', so it must be from the months. Also, the time for Tawaf al-Ziyarah, a pillar of Hajj, begins at dawn of Nahr, so the time of the pillar cannot begin after the time of Hajj has ended. Wuquf is missed by dawn of Nahr because it is textually tied to that time; thus the day of Tarwiyah is from the months but Wuquf is not performed on it. Imam Malik's position is that all of Dhu al-Hijjah is from the months, citing the Quranic phrase 'known months' in the plural, implying at least three. The Hanafi rebuttal is that the plural can be used for less than three, as in the verse on inheritance where 'brothers' (plural) refers to two. Also, it is common to speak of a whole year when only a part is meant. The practical benefit of this timing is that actions of Hajj, such as fasting for tamattu' or sa'y, are only valid within these months.

Key Terms
أشهر الحج (ashhur al-hajj): The specific months in which Hajj actions are valid: Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah.
عشر ذي الحجة (ashr dhi al-hijjah): The first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah, including the day of Nahr (10th).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many days of Dhu al-Hijjah are part of the months of Hajj?
A) The entire month
B) The first ten days
C) Nine days
D) Ten nights and nine days

Key Takeaway
The months of Hajj are Shawwal, Dhu al-Qa'dah, and the first ten days of Dhu al-Hijjah; actions performed outside are invalid.

The Majority Principle in ‘Umrah Tawaf for Tamattu‘
Ruling on whether most of ‘umrah tawaf occurs before or within the months

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that the majority (al-akthar) determines whether ‘umrah tawaf occurred within the months of Hajj, and state the resulting ruling on tamattu‘.

Core Idea
The majority of tawaf circuits decides the time of ‘umrah: four out of seven determines tamattu‘ validity.

This lesson examines a key rule in the Hanafi school regarding tamattu‘ in Hajj. The question arises when a person performs some circuits of ‘umrah tawaf before the months of Hajj and the rest within them. The Hanafi school uses the principle that the majority takes the ruling of the whole (al-akthar yanzilu manzilat al-kull) to decide whether the ‘umrah occurred within the months. Understanding this principle helps you correctly determine when tamattu‘ is established.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is performing ‘umrah tawaf partially before and partially within the months of Hajj. The question is whether this qualifies as tamattu‘ (combining ‘umrah and Hajj in the same journey).
2
State the Hanafi ruling
If the majority (four or more) of the seven circuits occur within the months of Hajj (Shawwal, Dhu al-Qi‘dah, and first ten of Dhu al-Hijjah), the ‘umrah is considered within and tamattu‘ is established. If the majority is before, tamattu‘ is not established.
The principle: al-akthar yanzilu manzilat al-kull.
3
Apply the majority principle
Count the circuits: exactly four or more within months? If yes, the tawaf is legally treated as having occurred entirely within the months. If three or fewer, it is as if performed before.
4
Understand the reasoning
The text explains that once a certain stage is reached (majority performed), the ‘umrah becomes binding and cannot be invalidated by intercourse. Hence, it is considered completed before the months if the majority was before, or within the months if the majority is during.
5
Identify the practical consequence
If tamattu‘ is established, the pilgrim becomes a mutamatti‘ and must offer a sacrificial animal (dam) as required by Hajj tamattu‘. If not, he performs Hajj ifrad (separate ‘umrah and Hajj) without dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبعكسه لا: أي لو طاف العمرة أربعة أشواط قبل الأشهر، ثم أتمها فيها لم يكن متمتعاً؛ لأن للأكثر حكم الكل، وكان أكثر أشواط العمرة قبل الأشهر، فلم يجتمع له الحج والعمرة فيها لا حقيقة ولا حكماً، أما الحقيقة؛ فلأنه لم يوجد فيها إلا بعضها وكذا حكماً؛ لأنها فرغت تقديراً؛ لأنها صارت بحال لا تحتمل الفساد بالجماع، والحاصل: أنه إن وجد أكثر طواف العمرة في أشهر الحج، فقد اجتمع له الحج والعمرة فيها، فيصير متمتعاً، وإن كان الأكثر قبلها لم يجتمعا ، ولا يكون متمتعاً. (فتح، مستخلص)
And its opposite is not [valid]: i.e., if he performed four circuits of ‘umrah tawaf before the months, then completed them in the months, he is not a mutamatti‘ because the majority has the ruling of the whole. Since most of the circuits of ‘umrah were before the months, Hajj and ‘umrah did not combine for him therein, neither in reality nor in legal effect. As for reality, because only part of them occurred in the months. And likewise in legal effect, because it is considered as if completed, since it reached a state where it cannot be invalidated by intercourse. The conclusion: if most of the ‘umrah tawaf occurred in the months of Hajj, then Hajj and ‘umrah combined for him, so he becomes a mutamatti‘. If the majority was before them, they did not combine, and he is not a mutamatti‘.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement followed by legal reasoning. It clarifies the criterion for tamattu‘: the combination of ‘umrah and Hajj in the months of Hajj. If a person performs four out of seven circuits of tawaf for ‘umrah before the months begin (e.g., in Ramadan), then completes the remaining three after Shawwal starts, he is not considered a mutamatti‘. The principle is that the majority takes the ruling of the whole. Since more than half the circuits were outside the months, the tawaf is legally considered as having occurred before the months. Thus, the ‘umrah is not deemed to have taken place within the months, so no tamattu‘. The reasoning mentions that once a certain stage is reached, the ‘umrah cannot be invalidated by intercourse (i.e., it becomes binding), so it is as if completed before the months. Conversely, if most circuits (four or more) occur after the months begin, tamattu‘ is established.

Key Terms
الأكثر (al-akthar): Majority: more than half of the tawaf circuits (four out of seven).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performs three circuits of ‘umrah tawaf before the months of Hajj and four within the months, is he a mutamatti‘?
A) Yes
B) No
C) Only if he completes all seven within the months
D) Only if he intends tamattu‘

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the majority of tawaf circuits determines whether ‘umrah occurred within the months of Hajj for tamattu‘.

Ihram for Hajj Before the Months: Validity and Dislike
Ruling on early Hajj ihram with proof and criticism of Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on early ihram for Hajj, distinguish between shart and rukn, and evaluate the Shafi'i objection using qiyas.

Core Idea
Ihram is a condition, not a pillar — advancing it is valid but disliked.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies a key difference between Hanafi and Shafi’i schools: the nature of ihram. The Hanafis treat ihram as a condition (shart) for Hajj, allowing it before the prescribed months, while the Shafi’is view it as a pillar (rukn), invalidating early ihram. Understanding this distinction reveals how madhhab principles shape rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school rules that ihram for Hajj before the months is valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh). The act is not invalid; the person remains in ihram for Hajj.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi‘i holds that ihram before the months is invalid and automatically becomes an ‘umrah.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi‘i proof: ihram is a rukn (pillar), and a pillar cannot be performed before its time. Therefore, the intention changes from Hajj to ‘umrah.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis respond: ihram is a shart (condition), analogous to ritual purity (taharah) which can be performed before prayer. Hence advancing is permissible. The dislike arises from the risk of violating prohibitions during the prolonged state, not from any invalidity.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: A Hanafi who enters ihram in Ramadan remains in ihram for Hajj and must avoid prohibitions until completing Hajj. According to Shafi‘i, the same person would perform ‘umrah and must exit ihram after ‘umrah, then re-enter ihram for Hajj at the proper time.
The Hanafi ruling is based on qiyas with taharah and careful distinction between shart and rukn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصح الإحرام به إلخ لأنه شرط فأشبه الطهارة في حق جواز التقديم على الوقت لا مطلقاً، قوله: "وكره" وجه الكراهة خوف الوقوع في محظورات الإحرام بطول الزمان، أو نقول له شبه بالركن، فصحة الإحرام قبلها بالنظر لكونه شرطا والكراهة بالنظر لكونه أشبه الركن وقال الشافعي: لا يجوز الإحرام قبلها، وينعقد عمرة؛ لأن الإحرام للحج ركن عنده، فلا يجوز قبل الوقت، واستشكل على قوله : ينعقد عمرة"؛ لأن العمرة فرض كالحج، فكيف ينعقد بتحريمة فرض الحج فرض آخر؟ هذا خلف. (عيني، فتح)
And ihram for Hajj before them is valid, etc., because it is a condition, so it resembles purity regarding the permissibility of advancing it before the time, not absolutely. His statement: 'And it is disliked' – the reason for dislike is fear of falling into prohibitions of ihram due to the length of time. Or we say: it resembles a pillar. So the validity of ihram before them is from the perspective that it is a condition, and the dislike is from the perspective that it resembles a pillar. Al-Shafi‘i said: Ihram before them is not valid, and it becomes an ‘umrah, because ihram for Hajj is a pillar in his view, so it is not permissible before the time. An objection is raised against his statement: it becomes an ‘umrah, because ‘umrah is obligatory like Hajj, so how can the tahrimah of the obligation of Hajj initiate another obligation? This is contradictory. (Ayni, Fath)
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi ruling with a proof and a dispute with Imam al-Shafi‘i. The Hanafi position is that ihram for Hajj before the months of Hajj is valid (sahih) but disliked (makruh). The reasoning: ihram is a condition for Hajj, not a pillar, so it can be performed before its time, just as ritual purity (taharah) can be performed before the time of prayer. However, it is disliked because prolonging the state of ihram increases the risk of violating its prohibitions, or because it resembles a pillar (since in other schools it is considered a pillar). Imam al-Shafi‘i holds that ihram before the months is invalid; instead it becomes an ‘umrah because in his school ihram is a pillar, and a pillar cannot be before its time. The Hanafi commentator objects that this would mean the intention of Hajj (tahrimah) creates a different obligation (‘umrah), which is illogical since both are obligatory.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition that must be present for the validity of the act but is not part of the act itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on ihram for Hajj before the month of Shawwal?
A) It is invalid and becomes ‘umrah
B) It is valid and mustahabb
C) It is valid but makruh
D) It is invalid and must be repeated

Key Takeaway
Ihram is a condition, not a pillar — advancing it is valid but disliked, distinguishing the Hanafi school from the Shafi‘i.

Tamattu’ of a Non-Makki Who Resides Away
Ruling on tamattu‘ with residence away from home

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tamattu‘ for a non-Makki who resides away after ‘umrah, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the condition of journey continuity to determine whether dam is wajib.

Core Idea
Tamattu‘ stands as long as your journey continues – even a long stay away from home does not break it.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq examines a critical nuance: what happens when a non-Makki performs ‘umrah but then resides in a place like Basra (with no family) before performing Hajj? The ruling hinges on whether the journey is considered a single, continuous trip. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that it is, while his two disciples Sahibayn disagree. Let’s explore the reasoning and the practical consequence in terms of the obligatory sacrifice (dam).

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for tamattu‘
The ‘umrah and Hajj must be performed in a single journey without returning to one’s homeland. This is the core condition for tamattu‘ in the Hanafi school.
The term 'tamattu‘' literally means 'enjoyment' – the pilgrim enjoys a single trip for both rituals.
2
Apply it to the scenarios
Consider an Iraqi (non-Makki) who does ‘umrah then stays in Makkah or Basra (a place without family) before performing Hajj. Has he returned home? No. So according to Imam Abu Hanifa, the journey continues and tamattu‘ is valid.
3
Compare the views
Imam says the journey continues; Sahibayn say if he stays in a place like Basra where he has no family, he becomes like a resident and the journey is broken. This is the crux of the dispute.
Sahibayn consider his ‘umrah as miqati (from the miqat) and his Hajj as Makki (since he resides in the miqat area), so they are not combined in a single travel.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: For Imam, the dam (sacrificial blood) is wajib because he is a mutamatti‘; for Sahibayn, no dam is due.
This shows how a conceptual difference leads to a different obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كوفي: أراد به الآفاقي لا خصوص المنسوب إلى الكوفة وقيد به؛ لأن المكي لا تمتع له، وقوله: "أقام بمكة" أي داخل المواقيت، وقوله: "أو بصرة" بضم الباء وكسرها، وأراد بها مكاناً لا أهل له فيه، وقوله: "صح تمتعه" قال العيني: أما إذا أقام بمكة؛ فلأنه أدى نسكين وترفق بإسقاط أحد السفرين، وهو حقيقة المتعة، وأما إذا أقام ببصرة فصحة التمتع فيها عند الإمام؛ لأن سفره قائم ما لم يعد إلى وطنه، وعندهما لا يصير متمتعا في هذه الصورة؛ لأن كانت عمرته ميقاتية وحجته مكية ونسكا هذا الرجل ميقاتيان كما إذا . رجع إلى أهله، وثمرة الخلاف في وجوب الدم فإنه يجب عنده؛ لأنه متمتع وعندهما لا يجب. (عيني، فتح) فيها : أي في أشهر الحج وفرغ منها وحلق أو قصر بمكة ليس بقيد والمراد موضع لا أهل له فيه، دل على ذلك قوله: "إلا أن يعود". (فتح) وحج :لا أي وإن أفسد تلك العمرة وفرغ منها وقصر، ثم أقام بمكة، ثم قضى تلك العمرة والحج مع القضاء لا يكون متمتعاً بالاتفاق؛ لأنه صار بمنزلة المكي، ولا تمتع لأهل مكة، ولو اتخذ داراً في البصرة بعد إفساد العمرة، ثم قضى وحج لا يكون متمتعاً عنده؛ لأن حكم السفرة الأولى باق ما لم يرجع إلى أهله، فصار كأنه لم يخرج من مكة، عندهما؛ لأن . ويصير متمتعاً. عوده من البصرة إنشاء سفر، وقد ترفق في هذا السفر بأداء النسكين، فالمذكور في المتن المسألة الاتفاقية، ولهذا قيد بقوله : "فأقام بمكة". (مستخلص) إلا أن يعود وهذا استثناء من قوله : "لا" أي لا يكون في صورة الإفساد والقضاء متمتعا، إلا أن يعود إلى أهله؛ لأنه لما ألم بأهله، ثم رجع وأتى بالعمرة والحج كان هذا إنشاء سفر؛ لأن السفرة الأولى قد انتهت بالإلمام الصحيح، فاجتمع نسكان في السفرة الثانية فيكون متمتعا؛ لأن عمرته ميقاتية وحجته مكية، وهو من أهل الآفاق فيكون متمتعا. (عيني، مستخلص) إلى أهله ثم اعتمر في الأشهر وحج من عامه ذلك، فإنه يكون متمتعا اتفاقاً. (ط) أفسد: أي الكوفي الذي يريد التمتع. مضى فيه: أي من اعتمر في أشهر الحج وحج من عامه ذلك فهو متمتع، وعليه دم التمتع، ثم إن أفسد أحدهما مضى فيه ولا دم عليه، أما المضي؛ فلأنه لا يمكنه الخروج عن عهدة الإحرام إلا بالأفعال، وأما سقوط الدم؛ فلأنه لم يبق متمتعاً، ولزمه مه دم جبر للتضاد (مستخلص فتح) ولا دم عليه أي دم التمتع؛ لأنه لم يترفق بأداء النسكين الصحيحين في سفر واحد. (ع) فضحى: أي ذبح أضحيته يوم النحر. (ع)
Kufi: he means a non-Makki, not specifically one from Kufa; it is specified because a Makki has no tamattu‘. His statement 'he stayed in Makkah' means inside the miqat. 'Or Basra' with dammah or kasrah of the ba, and he meant a place where he has no family. His statement 'his tamattu‘ is valid' – al-Ayni said: if he stayed in Makkah, because he performed two rituals and is granted ease by cancelling one journey, which is the reality of tamattu‘. If he stayed in Basra, tamattu‘ is valid according to Imam Abu Hanifa because his journey continues as long as he has not returned to his homeland. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he does not become a mutamatti‘ in this case because his ‘umrah was miqati and his Hajj was Makki, and the two rituals of this man are both miqati, just as if he returned to his family. The consequence of the difference is in the necessity of blood: according to Imam, it is obligatory because he is a mutamatti‘; according to the two, it is not obligatory. (Ayni, Fath) 'In them' means in the months of Hajj. He completed them and shaved or trimmed in Makkah – this is not a condition, and what is meant is a place where he has no family, as indicated by his statement 'unless he returns'. (Fath) 'And Hajj: no' i.e., if he spoiled that ‘umrah, completed it and trimmed, then stayed in Makkah, then made it up (qada) and performed Hajj along with the makeup, he is not a mutamatti‘ by agreement, because he becomes like a Makki, and there is no tamattu‘ for the people of Makkah. If he took a house in Basra after spoiling the ‘umrah, then made it up and performed Hajj, he is not a mutamatti‘ according to Imam because the ruling of the first journey remains as long as he has not returned to his family, so it is as if he never left Makkah; according to the two, he becomes a mutamatti‘ because his return from Basra is a new journey, and he has gained ease in this journey by performing the two rituals. So what is mentioned in the text is the agreed-upon case, hence he specified by saying 'so he stayed in Makkah'. (Mustakhlas) 'Unless he returns' – this is an exception from his statement 'no'. i.e., in the case of spoiling and makeup, he is not a mutamatti‘ unless he returns to his family, because when he returns to his family, then comes back and performs ‘umrah and Hajj, this constitutes a new journey, because the first journey ended with a valid return home. So the two rituals combine in the second journey, and he becomes a mutamatti‘ because his ‘umrah is miqati and his Hajj is Makki, and he is from the afaq, so he becomes a mutamatti‘. (Ayni, Mustakhlas) 'To his family, then he performed ‘umrah in the months and Hajj in the same year, then he is a mutamatti‘ by agreement.' (T) 'He spoiled': i.e., the Kufi who intends tamattu‘. 'He continues with it': i.e., whoever performs ‘umrah in the months of Hajj and Hajj in the same year, he is a mutamatti‘ and owes the dam of tamattu‘. Then if he spoils one of them, he continues with it and no dam is due upon him. As for continuing, because he cannot exit the responsibility of ihram except by the actions. As for the dropping of the blood, because he no longer remains a mutamatti‘, and a compensatory blood becomes necessary? (Mustakhlas, Fath) 'And no dam upon him' i.e., the dam of tamattu‘, because he did not gain ease by performing both correct rituals in one journey. (A) 'Then he sacrificed': i.e., he slaughtered his udhiyah on the day of Nahr. (A)
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the tamattu‘ of a non-Makki (person from outside Makkah) who performs ‘umrah during the months of Hajj, then resides in Makkah or in a place like Basra (where he has no family), and then performs Hajj. The key point: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, his tamattu‘ is valid because his journey is considered ongoing unless he returns to his homeland. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree when he resides in Basra, considering his ‘umrah and Hajj both as miqati, so no tamattu‘. The practical consequence: whether the dam (sacrificial blood) is obligatory. Imam says yes (since he is mutamatti‘); Sahibayn say no. The text then discusses the case where he spoils (ifsad) the ‘umrah, makes it up, and performs Hajj: here there is agreement that he is not a mutamatti‘ because he becomes like a Makki. However, if he returns to his family first and then comes back, he is a mutamatti‘ by agreement. The passage also notes that if a mutamatti‘ spoils either the ‘umrah or the Hajj, he continues with the spoiled one (no way out of ihram) but the dam of tamattu‘ is dropped because he no longer has the ease of two correct rituals. The final phrase 'then he sacrificed' simply notes that if a mutamatti‘ slaughters an udhiyah, it is permissible.

Key Terms
متمتع (mutamatti‘): A person who performs ‘umrah during the months of Hajj and then performs Hajj in the same year, benefiting from a single journey.
أفاقي (afaqi): A person whose home is outside the miqat (i.e., not a Makki).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if a non-Makki performs ‘umrah in the months of Hajj, then resides in Basra (with no family) and performs Hajj, is he a mutamatti‘?
A) Yes, and he owes dam
B) No, because his ‘umrah and Hajj are both miqati
C) Yes, but no dam required
D) No, because he is like a Makki

Key Takeaway
The continuity of the journey is decisive for tamattu‘: a non-Makki who does not return home remains a mutamatti‘ even if he stays elsewhere, and must offer the dam.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Tamattu' Dam for the Traveller
Ruling on tamattu' for a non-Makki and the ikhtilaf between Imam and Sahibayn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute on the tamattu' dam for a non-Makki who stays away from home before Hajj and apply the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa rules dam wajib; Sahibayn rule no dam; the school follows Sahibayn.

The matn declares tamattu' valid for a Kufi who stays in Mecca or a place like Basra, but the commentary reveals a key split within the Hanafi school. Understanding this dispute – and which position is operative for fatwa – is essential for correctly applying the rules of tamattu' in Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
The matn states: 'his tamattu' is valid' for a Kufi who performs umrah, stays in Mecca or Basra, and then does Hajj. Note that 'Kufi' means any afaqi (person from beyond the miqat).
The term excludes a Makki, who has no tamattu'.
2
Recognise the two scenarios
The commentary separates two cases: staying in Mecca (inside the miqat) and staying in a place like Basra (outside the miqat but without family). The ikhtilaf applies only to the second scenario.
Both cases are considered tamattu' by the matn initially.
3
Analyse the ikhtilaf – Imam vs Sahibayn
Imam Abu Hanifa: tamattu' valid because travel status persists until return home. Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad): not mutamatti' because both rites become miqati as if he returned home.
The key point is the concept of 'travel' and 'miqat'.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is the obligation of the dam. Imam says dam wajib; Sahibayn say no dam. This difference affects whether the pilgrim must sacrifice an animal.
The fruit of the dispute is purely the dam, not the validity of the Hajj itself.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
Later Hanafi authorities prefer the Sahibayn view, so the operative ruling for fatwa is: no dam required for a Kufi who stays in a place without family.
Always check later tarjih when facing intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو اعتمر كوفي فيها وأقام بمكة أو بصرة وحج صح تمتعه. كوفي: أراد به الآفاقي لا خصوص المنسوب إلى الكوفة وقيد به؛ لأن المكي لا تمتع له، وقوله: "أقام بمكة" أي داخل المواقيت، وقوله: "أو بصرة" بضم الباء وكسرها، وأراد بها مكاناً لا أهل له فيه، وقوله: "صح تمتعه" قال العيني: أما إذا أقام بمكة؛ فلأنه أدى نسكين وترفق بإسقاط أحد السفرين، وهو حقيقة المتعة، وأما إذا أقام ببصرة فصحة التمتع فيها عند الإمام؛ لأن سفره قائم ما لم يعد إلى وطنه، وعندهما لا يصير متمتعا في هذه الصورة؛ لأن كانت عمرته ميقاتية وحجته مكية ونسكا هذا الرجل ميقاتيان كما إذا . رجع إلى أهله، وثمرة الخلاف في وجوب الدم فإنه يجب عنده؛ لأنه متمتع وعندهما لا يجب.
And if a Kufi performs umrah in [the Hajj months] and stays in Mecca or Basra and performs Hajj, his tamattu' is valid. 'Kufi': intended meaning is the afaqi (one from beyond the miqat), not specifically attributed to Kufa, and it is qualified with this because the Makki has no tamattu'. And his statement: 'stayed in Mecca' means inside the miqat, and his statement: 'or Basra' with damm on the ba' and with kasr, and he intended by it a place where he has no family there. And his statement: 'his tamattu' is valid' - al-Ayni said: As for if he stayed in Mecca, because he performed two rites and had ease by dropping one of the two journeys, and that is the reality of tamattu'. And as for if he stayed in Basra, the validity of tamattu' in it is according to Imam Abu Hanifa because his travel remains as long as he does not return to his homeland. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he does not become mutamatti' in this situation because his umrah was miqati (from the miqat) and his Hajj was Makki, and the two rites of this man are both miqati, as if he returned to his family. The fruit of the difference is in the obligation of the dam: it is obligatory according to him because he is mutamatti', and according to them it is not obligatory.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage addresses tamattu' for a person from the miqat (afaqi) who performs umrah in the Hajj months and then stays in Mecca or in a place like Basra where he has no family, and then performs Hajj. The matn states that his tamattu' is valid. The sharh explains that 'Kufi' here means any afaqi, not only someone from Kufa; the term is used because the Makki has no tamattu' (since tamattu' requires two journeys, and the Makki has only one). The commentary clarifies the ikhtilaf between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students (Sahibayn). According to Imam, if the person stays in a place where he has no family (like Basra), his tamattu' is valid because his travel status persists until he returns to his homeland. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, he is not considered mutamatti' in this case because both his umrah and Hajj become miqati (since his residence is now within the miqat area), similar to if he had returned home. The practical consequence (thamarah) is the obligation of the dam: Imam Abu Hanifa requires the dam because he is mutamatti', while the Sahibayn do not. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the Sahibayn in the Hanafi school, as indicated in later commentaries.

Key Terms
كوفي (Kufi): Here means any person from the afaq (beyond the miqat), not specifically from Kufa.
متمتع (mutamatti'): One who performs umrah in the Hajj months and then performs Hajj in the same year with a break, benefiting from a single journey.
ميقاتي (miqati): A rite performed from the miqat boundary; here it describes the umrah as being done from the miqat, not from beyond.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because both his umrah and Hajj become miqati, as if he were a Makki.
C) Because he does not perform umrah in the Hajj months.
D) Because he stays in a place with family.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that a Kufi who stays in a place without family before Hajj is not mutamatti' and owes no dam.

Ruling on Corrupting Either Umrah or Hajj
Ruling that one who corrupts either rite must complete it and no dam is due

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a mutamatti' corrupts one of the two rites and explain why the tamattu' dam is not due.

Core Idea
If you corrupt one rite in tamattu', you must complete it, but you lose the dam — because the ease is gone.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq delivers a concise ruling every Hanafi student must memorize: what happens when a pilgrim performing tamattu' corrupts either the umrah or hajj. The ruling has two parts: an obligation to continue the corrupted rite, and the dropping of the tamattu' compensation. Understanding the legal reasoning behind both parts is essential for applying the rule correctly.

Guided Path
1
Define tamattu' and its two rites
Clarify that tamattu' involves performing umrah first, then after a break, performing hajj in the same journey. Both rites are distinct obligations.
The dam for tamattu' compensates for the ease of combining the two journeys.
2
State the two consequences of corruption
The matn says 'mada fihi' meaning the pilgrim must proceed with the corrupted rite to completion, and 'la dam' meaning no tamattu' dam is due.
He cannot exit ihram except by completing the actions of that rite.
3
Explain why the dam is dropped
The tamattu' dam is a compensation for the benefit of performing both rites correctly in one journey. If one rite is corrupted, that benefit is lost, so the dam is waived.
This ruling applies only if he was validly in tamattu' before corruption.
4
Identify the hukm level
Completing the corrupted rite is wajib (obligatory). There is no ikhtilaf among the Hanafi imams on this point.
The obligation stems from the general rule that once ihram is entered, it cannot be abandoned except by completing the rites.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيهما أفسد مضى فيه، ولا دم
And whichever of them he corrupts, he must proceed with it, and no dam (for tamattu') is due.
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This is a brief ruling from the matn. When a person is performing tamattu' and corrupts either the umrah or the Hajj (by invalidating it, e.g., through sexual intercourse), he must continue with that rite until completion (mada fihi) because he cannot exit the ihram except by completing the actions. However, no dam is due for the tamattu' because the person is no longer considered mutamatti' (since he corrupted one of the rites). The dam for tamattu' is a compensation for the ease of combining two journeys; if one rite is corrupted, that ease is lost, so the dam drops. The commentary explains: 'As for proceeding, because he cannot exit the obligation of ihram except by actions; and as for the dropping of the dam, because he has not benefited from performing both correct rites in one journey.'

Key Terms
تَمَتُّع (tamattu'): A form of pilgrimage where one performs umrah first, then after a break performs hajj in the same journey, requiring a dam.
دَم (dam): An animal sacrifice required as compensation for certain acts in hajj, here specifically the tamattu' dam.
مَضَى فِيهِ (mada fihi): The ruling that one must continue with the corrupted rite to completion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, if a mutamatti' corrupts either his umrah or Hajj, what is due?
A) He must start over.
B) He must proceed with it and no tamattu' dam is due.
C) He must proceed with it and still pay the tamattu' dam.
D) He may abandon the rite and pay a dam.

Key Takeaway
In tamattu', corrupting one rite obligates completing it but waives the tamattu' dam.

Tamattu' After Corrupting Umrah: The Exception of Returning Home
Ruling with intra-Hanafi dispute on tamattu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on tamattu' for a person who corrupts his umrah, stays in Mecca, performs qada and Hajj, and distinguish the agreed-upon case from the disputed case based on returning to his homeland.

Core Idea
Corrupting umrah and staying in Mecca ends tamattu'—only returning home restores it.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hajj jurisprudence: a pilgrim intending tamattu' corrupts his umrah (e.g., by sexual intercourse), then stays in Mecca, performs a replacement umrah (qada), and completes Hajj. The key question is whether he becomes a mutamatti' and owes a dam. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling with an important exception, and there is a subtle internal disagreement on what counts as 'returning home.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The passage describes a person who corrupts his umrah intentionally, then remains in Mecca (within the miqat), performs qada of the umrah, and then performs Hajj in the same year.
Corruption here typically means sexual intercourse while in ihram, making the umrah invalid and requiring qada.
2
State the agreed ruling
In this situation, the person is NOT a mutamatti' by agreement of the Hanafi imams. The reason is that staying in Mecca changes his status to that of a Makki, and residents of Mecca do not have tamattu'.
The matn says 'لا' (he is not mutamatti'), and this is the agreed position.
3
Identify the exception
The exception is 'إلا أن يعود إلى أهله' — unless he returns to his homeland. If he goes back home and then returns to perform umrah and Hajj in the same year, he becomes mutamatti' by consensus because the first journey is considered ended and a new journey begins.
This exception applies when the return is to his actual home, not merely to another city like Basra.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
The passage mentions a difference: if after corruption he takes up residence in Basra (not his home), then according to Imam Abu Hanifa he is still not mutamatti' (the journey remains), but according to the Sahibayn he becomes mutamatti' because moving to Basra constitutes a new journey.
The matn's wording 'أقام بمكة' restricts the agreed case to staying in Mecca; the Basra case is disputed.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The practical difference (thamarah) is the obligation of the dam for tamattu': according to Imam, no dam; according to Sahibayn, dam is wajib. Later fatwa prefers the Sahibayn's view.
The mufta bihi position is that moving to a place where one has no family (like Basra) triggers tamattu'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(مستخلص) إلا أن يعود وهذا استثناء من قوله : "لا" أي لا يكون في صورة الإفساد والقضاء متمتعا، إلا أن يعود إلى أهله؛ لأنه لما ألم بأهله، ثم رجع وأتى بالعمرة والحج كان هذا إنشاء سفر؛ لأن السفرة الأولى قد انتهت بالإلمام الصحيح، فاجتمع نسكان في السفرة الثانية فيكون متمتعا ؛ لأن عمرته ميقاتية وحجته مكية، وهو من أهل الآفاق فيكون متمتعا . (عيني، مستخلص إلى أهله ثم اعتمر في الأشهر وحج من عامه ذلك، فإنه يكون متمتعا اتفاقاً. (ط)
And if he corrupts it (the umrah) intentionally, and then stays in Mecca and performs qada (repeats the umrah) and performs Hajj, he is not (a mutamatti'), unless he returns to his homeland. And whichever of them he corrupts, he must proceed with it, and no dam (for tamattu') is due. His corrupt umrah in the months (of Hajj)... (commentary continues about the anology).
Source pages p. 286

Commentary
This passage deals with the case where a person who intended tamattu' corrupts his umrah (e.g., by having sexual intercourse) intentionally. He then stays in Mecca, performs a qada (replacement) umrah, and then performs Hajj. The ruling is that he does not become a mutamatti' by agreement of the scholars, because his prolonged stay in Mecca makes him like a Makki, and the Makki has no tamattu'. However, if he first returns to his homeland and then comes back to perform umrah and Hajj in the same year, he becomes mutamatti' by consensus. The commentary also discusses the scenario where he takes up residence in Basra after corrupting the umrah: according to Imam Abu Hanifa, he is still not mutamatti' because the ruling of the first journey remains (he has not returned home), but according to the Sahibayn, his return from Basra constitutes a new journey and he becomes mutamatti'. The matn's wording 'stayed in Mecca' indicates the agreed-upon case.

Key Terms
أفسد (afsada): He corrupted the umrah intentionally, generally by sexual intercourse.
قضى (qada): He performed the replacement of the corrupted umrah (repeating it).
متمتع (mutamatti'): A person who performs tamattu' Hajj, i.e., performs umrah and then Hajj in the same year with a break in ihram.
ميقاتي (miqati): Relating to the miqat (the boundary for entering ihram).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He is a mutamatti' and must offer a dam.
B) He is not a mutamatti' and owes no dam for tamattu'.
C) He is a mutamatti' but no dam is required.
D) The ruling depends on whether he stays more than a month.

Key Takeaway
If a pilgrim corrupts his umrah and stays in Mecca before Hajj, he loses tamattu' status unless he first returns to his homeland, which restores the possibility of tamattu' by consensus.
