Udhiya Does Not Suffice for Tamattu' Dam
Ruling with rational proof and additional scenario

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that udhiya does not suffice for tamattu' dam and explain the two-fold reasoning: (1) the mutamatti' is a traveler and udhiya is not wajib on him, and (2) even if it were wajib, the intentions differ because they are separate acts.

Core Idea
Udhiya cannot replace tamattu' dam — they are separate wajib acts with distinct conditions and intentions.

A common practical issue arises when a pilgrim performing tamattu' hajj assumes that the sacrificial animal he slaughters for Eid al-Adha (udhiya) can also fulfill the required tamattu' dam. The Hanafi school, supported by sound reasoning, clarifies that this is not the case. In this lesson, we examine the ruling, its rational proof, and an additional scenario involving a woman that reinforces the principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text rules that a sacrificial animal intended as udhiya does not suffice for the tamattu' dam. Recognize that the ruling is a negative one—it does not count.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The text provides two reasons: first, the mutamatti' is a traveler (safar), and udhiya is not wajib on a traveler; second, even if udhiya were wajib (e.g., due to residency), the two are different acts with separate intentions, so one cannot substitute for the other.
The proof is aqli (rational) based on the principles of obligation and intent.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the reasoning leads to the ruling: because udhiya is not wajib on the mutamatti' (traveler), the act he performed is not the wajib act required. Even if it were wajib, the divergence of intent (niyyah) means the act belongs to one obligation and cannot cover another.
This is a clear case of applying the maxim that each ibadah requires its own intention.
4
Note the additional scenario
The text mentions a woman who enters ihram and then menstruates. She must perform all rites except tawaf and can postpone tawaf. But the udhiya she slaughters still does not cover the tamattu' dam, reinforcing that they are distinct.
This scenario, recorded by Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir, illustrates the ruling in a practical context where ignorance is more common.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence is that a mutamatti' must perform two separate slaughters (or their equivalents): one for udhiya (if resident) and one for the tamattu' dam. Failure to do so leaves the dam obligation unfulfilled, potentially requiring compensation.
There is no ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لم تجز عن المتعة، ولو حاضت عند الإحرام أتت بغير الطواف، ولو عند الصدر تركته تلك الأضحية. لم تجز: لأنه أتى بغير الواجب؛ ولأن المتمتع يكون مسافراً؛ ولهذا لا تمتع للمكي، والأضحية غير واجبة على المسافر، و لم ينب عن دم المتعة، والأضحية إنما تجب بالشراء بنيتها أو الإقامة و لم يوجد واحد منهما، وعلى فرض وجوبها لم تجز أيضاً؛ لأنهما غيران، فإذا نوى أحدهما لم يجز عن الآخر، ولو تخلل يجب عليه دمان: دم التحلل قبل أوانه سوى الدم الذي ذبح، وذكر محمد هذه المسألة "الجامع الصغير" في المرأة؛ لأن الجهل عليهن أغلب، أو كانت واقعة امرأة نقلها أبو يوسف عن أبي حنيفة لمحمد كما سمعها منه، ووضعها محمد لما سمعها من أبي يوسف. (مستخلص، عيني) عن المتعة: أي عن دمها؛ لأنه أتى بغير ما عليه؛ لأن دم التمتع غير الأضحية فلا أحدهما ينوب عن الآخر.
It (the udhiya) does not suffice for the tamattu' (dam). That udhiya does not suffice because he performed something other than the wajib; and because the mutamatti' is a traveler, and for that reason there is no tamattu' for the Makki, and the udhiya is not wajib upon the traveler, and it does not stand in place of the tamattu' dam. The udhiya only becomes wajib by purchasing with the intention or by residency, and neither of those existed. Even if it were wajib, it would not suffice because they are two different things; if one intends one, it does not count for the other...
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage addresses a common practical problem: a pilgrim performing tamattu' may think that the udhiya (the sacrificial animal he slaughters on Eid al-Adha) can also fulfill the requirement of the tamattu' dam. The text clearly states that it does not. The reasons are: (1) The mutamatti' is a traveler, and udhiya is not wajib on a traveler (it is only wajib on a resident). (2) Even if udhiya were wajib on him (for example, if he has taken up residence or purchased an animal with the intention of udhiya), it is a different act of worship with its own purpose, so intending one does not fulfill the other. The commentary mentions that Imam Muhammad recorded this issue in al-Jami' al-Saghir specifically regarding a woman, as women are more often ignorant of these details. The ruling is that the dam for tamattu' is distinct from udhiya, and they cannot substitute for each other.

Key Terms
أضحية (udhiya): The sacrificial animal slaughtered on the days of Eid al-Adha.
دم المتعة (dam al-tamattu'): The sacrificial animal (or its value) required from a mutamatti' as compensation for combining umrah and Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the mutamatti' is a traveler and udhiya is not wajib on him.
B) Because the udhiya must be slaughtered before the dam.
C) Because the tamattu' dam is only for the poor.
D) Because the udhiya is a sunnah, not wajib.

Key Takeaway
Udhiya and tamattu' dam are separate wajib acts; one cannot fulfill the other by mere intention.

Menstruating Woman in Hajj: Exempt from Tawaf
Ruling with proof for menstruating woman's exemption from tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a menstruating woman regarding tawaf and identify the evidence from the Sunnah.

Core Idea
A menstruating woman does all Hajj acts except tawaf.

A common concern for women performing Hajj is the interruption of rituals due to menstruation. This passage, based on a clear prophetic directive, clarifies that a menstruating woman may continue with all Hajj rites except circumambulation of the Ka'bah. The ruling is grounded in the well-known hadith of Aisha (radiyallahu 'anha) at Sarif, and it applies equally to postpartum women.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Scope
Read the passage to determine what acts a menstruating woman is permitted to perform and which she must avoid. Note the two timeframes: menstruation at ihram (early) and after tawaf al-ziyarah (later).
The exemption applies only to tawaf, not to any other ritual.
2
Locate the Primary Evidence (Dalil)
Find the hadith cited: the Prophet's instruction to Aisha. Identify the exact wording and its source (Sahih Bukhari and Muslim).
The hadith is an explicit command: 'Do what the pilgrim does, except do not circumambulate the House.'
3
Analyse the Wajh al-Dalalah (How the Proof Yields the Ruling)
Examine how the hadith proves the ruling. The exception (‘illa) clarifies that all other rituals are permitted. The imperative 'ifa'li' indicates obligation (wujub) for the general acts, but the exemption from tawaf shows it is not required at that time.
The general command includes all acts; the exception removes only tawaf.
4
Identify the Concession for Tawaf al-Sadr
Note the separate case: a woman who menstruates after completing tawaf al-ziyarah is excused from tawaf al-sadr (farewell tawaf). The evidence is the incident of Hafsa and the general concession mentioned by Ibn Abbas.
If she becomes pure before leaving Mecca, the exemption no longer applies.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi (Operative Ruling)
Confirm that this is the established Hanafi position, with no intra-madhhab disagreement noted. The ruling applies identically to postpartum women (nufasa').
The authority weight is zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ع) أتت بغير الطواف [ أي اغتسلت له وأحرمت وفعلت (ط)]. وفي بعض النسخ: "أتت الجميع بغير الطواف"، وذكر السيد الحموي أن هذا المزج قبيح أورث المتن ركاكة والمراد بـ"غير" "الطواف" الوقوفان ورمي الجمار ونحوهما، والأصل في ذلك حديث عائشة لهما حين حاضت بسرف"، رواه البخاري ومسلم. (عيني، فتح) الطواف بالبيت؛ لقوله عليها لعائشة حين حاضت بـ"سرف": "افعلي ما يفعل الحاج غير أن لا تطوفي بالبيت"، فإن طهرت بعد مضي أيام النحر طافت للزيارة، ولا شيء عليها، وعليها طواف الصدر؛ لأنها طاهرة عنده. (ط،ع) تركته أي لو حاضت بعد الوقوف وطواف الزيارة انصرفت وتركت طواف الصدر ؛ لما روي: أن حفصة لها حاضت بعد طواف الزيارة، فرخصها النبي له في ترك طواف الصدر؛ لقول ابن عباس : "إنه عليه أمر الناس أن يكون آخر عهدهم بالبيت إلا أنه خفف عن المرأة الحائض، متفق عليه ولو طهرت قبل أن تخرج منها يلزمها للأهلية حينئذ، وإن جاوزت بيوت مكة ثم طهرت لا تعود وكذا لو انقطع دمها فلم تغتسل و لم يذهب وقت صلاة حتى خرجت منها والنفساء كالحائض
And if she menstruates at the time of ihram, she performs all except tawaf; and if at the time of departure (sadr), she leaves it (tawaf al-sadr). That is her dam. ...
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage deals with the rulings specific to a menstruating woman during hajj. It is based on the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) when she menstruated at Sarif: the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'Do what the pilgrim does, except do not circumambulate the House.' So if she menstruates at the time of ihram, she may still perform all other rituals such as standing at Arafat, Muzdalifah, stoning the jamarat, etc. If she menstruates after the standing and the tawaf al-ziyarah (the obligatory tawaf during the days of Eid), she may leave the farewell tawaf (tawaf al-sadr) due to the hadith of Hafsa and the general concession for the menstruating woman. However, if she becomes pure before leaving Mecca, she must perform the farewell tawaf. The passage also mentions that the postpartum woman (nufasa') has the same ruling as the menstruating woman. The dam mentioned refers to the dam that may be due for leaving the tawaf, but the text indicates that if she leaves it due to menstruation, no dam is required (as per the hadith).

Key Terms
حائض (ha'id): A menstruating woman; during hajj, she is exempt from tawaf but not other rituals.
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed upon leaving Mecca, also called tawaf al-wada'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) To do all that a pilgrim does except circumambulate the House.
C) To perform only the tawaf and leave the other rituals.
D) To send someone to perform the tawaf on her behalf.

Key Takeaway
A menstruating woman is exempted only from tawaf; all other Hajj rituals are valid and she need not compensate for the farewell tawaf if missed due to menstruation.

Rulings on Dam al-Tamattu', Menstruation, and Tawaf al-Sadr
Commentary on matn rulings for tamattu' hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the non-substitution of udhiyah for dam al-tamattu', the exemptions for a menstruating woman during hajj, and the obligation of tawaf al-sadr for residents, and apply them to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
A menstruating woman performs all hajj acts except tawaf; udhiyah does not substitute dam al-tamattu'; tawaf al-sadr is waived for residents and menstruating women.

This lesson covers three distinct rulings from the Hanafi school related to tamattu' hajj. First, the compulsory sacrifice (dam al-tamattu') cannot be replaced by an udhiyah sacrifice. Second, a woman experiencing menstruation is exempt from all forms of tawaf but must perform every other hajj rite. Third, a resident of Makkah is not required to perform tawaf al-sadr (farewell tawaf) if they intend residence before the first departure. These rulings are supported by hadith and reasoning from the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
Locate the three main rulings in the passage: (1) udhiyah does not suffice for dam al-tamattu', (2) a menstruating woman performs all hajj acts except tawaf, (3) a resident of Makkah is exempt from tawaf al-sadr.
2
Examine the evidence for each
For the menstruating woman, the hadith of Aisha at Sarif and Hafsa. For the resident, the principle that tawaf al-sadr is for departing pilgrims.
3
Understand the rationale
Dam al-tamattu' and udhiyah are distinct acts of worship; one cannot substitute the other. Menstruating women are excused from tawaf due to impurity. Residents are not departing, so tawaf al-sadr is not required.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Abu Yusuf holds that if a resident intends residence after the time for tawaf al-sadr has entered, it drops. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold it remains obligatory.
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.
5
Apply to a scenario
Given a hypothetical: a woman on tamattu' menstruates after tawaf al-ziyarah but before leaving Makkah. She leaves without tawaf al-sadr – valid per Hanafi. If she becomes pure before leaving, she must perform it.

(مستخلص، عيني)
Chapter of Tamattu'. It does not suffice for tamattu', and if she menstruates at the time of ihram, she performs [all acts] except tawaf, and if at the time of departure she leaves it, that udhiyah is like one who resides in Makkah. Its blood (i.e., of the woman), tawaf al-sadr, tamattu', and blood. 'It does not suffice' because he performed other than what was obligatory; and because the mutamatti' is a traveler, hence there is no tamattu' for a Makkan, and udhiyah is not obligatory on a traveler, and it does not substitute for the blood of tamattu'. Udhiyah is only obligatory by purchase with its intention or residence, and neither existed. On the assumption of its obligation, it also does not suffice because they are different; if he intends one, it does not count for the other. And if intermediate, two bloods are obligatory: the blood of tahallul before its time besides the blood sacrificed. Muhammad mentioned this issue in al-Jami' al-Saghir concerning the woman because ignorance is more prevalent among them, or it was an incident of a woman reported by Abu Yusuf from Abu Hanifa to Muhammad as he heard it from him, and Muhammad placed it when he heard it from Abu Yusuf. (Mukhtasar, 'Ayni) 'About tamattu'': i.e., about its blood; because he performed other than what was upon him; because tamattu''s blood is other than udhiyah, so neither substitutes for the other. ('Ayni) 'She performs except tawaf' [i.e., she bathes for it and enters ihram and performs (T).] In some copies: 'She performs all except tawaf', and al-Sayyid al-Hamawi said that this mixture is ugly, making the matn weak, and by 'except tawaf' is meant the two standings and throwing the pebbles and the like. The basis for this is the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) when she menstruated at Sarif, reported by Bukhari and Muslim. ('Ayni, Fath) Tawaf of the House; because of his saying (peace be upon him) to Aisha when she menstruated at Sarif: 'Do what the pilgrim does except do not circumambulate the House.' If she becomes pure after the days of Nahr have passed, she performs tawaf al-ziyarah and nothing is upon her, and she must perform tawaf al-sadr because she is pure at that time. (T, 'A) 'She leaves it' i.e., if she menstruates after the standing and tawaf al-ziyarah, she departs and leaves tawaf al-sadr; because it is narrated that Hafsa (may Allah be pleased with her) menstruated after tawaf al-ziyarah, and the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave her concession to leave tawaf al-sadr; due to the saying of Ibn Abbas: 'He (peace be upon him) ordered people that the last of their covenant be with the House, except that he made it light for the menstruating woman.' Agreed upon. And if she becomes pure before she leaves it, it is obligatory on her due to eligibility at that time; and if she passes the houses of Makkah and then becomes pure, she does not return. Likewise, if her blood stops and she does not bathe and no time for prayer passes until she leaves it. And the woman in postnatal bleeding is like the menstruating woman. Ramz al-Haqa'iq 169/1 (Mukhtasar) 'Like one who resides in Makkah': [in the accusative case as a description of a deleted verbal noun, i.e., she leaves it with a leaving like the leaving of one who resides in Makkah of tawaf al-sadr; because he has become one of its people. ('A)] i.e., whoever takes a house in Makkah is not required to perform tawaf al-sadr because it is upon the departing one. This is if the intention of residence is before the first departure, which is the third of the day of Nahr. If it is after, then he must perform tawaf al-sadr according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]; because it became obligatory by the entry of its time before the intention of residence, so it does not drop from him, just as if she menstruates after the time of prayer has exited, that prayer is not dropped from her. Abu Yusuf said: it drops from him, and it is not required unless he begins it; because the cause is the departure, and the time is a condition, and hence it is not obligatory on her if she menstruates after the [time of] halal (exit from ihram). (Mukhtasar, 'Ayni)
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage from Bab al-Tamattu' of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, with its commentary, covers several rulings related to tamattu' hajj. The matn states that a woman's udhiyah sacrifice does not suffice for the required dam al-tamattu' if she is performing tamattu'. The reason is that the mutamatti' is a traveler and not required to sacrifice an udhiyah; the udhiyah is only obligatory on a resident by purchase with intention or by residence. Even if it were obligatory, it would not substitute because the two sacrifices are distinct acts of worship with different purposes. The commentator notes that Imam Muhammad recorded this issue in al-Jami' al-Saghir regarding women due to their common ignorance. The matn then covers a menstruating woman: if she menstruates at the time of ihram, she performs all acts of hajj except tawaf, based on the hadith of Aisha at Sarif. She must bathe for ihram and enter ihram, doing everything except circumambulation. If she menstruates after the standing at Arafat and tawaf al-ziyarah, she may depart without tawaf al-sadr, as the Prophet gave concession to Hafsa. However, if she becomes pure before leaving, tawaf al-sadr becomes obligatory. The ruling for a woman in postnatal bleeding is the same as for menstruation. The final part discusses a resident of Makkah: one who takes up residence in Makkah before the first departure (third day of Nahr) is not required to perform tawaf al-sadr, as it is only obligatory on departing pilgrims. If the intention of residence is after that, the obligation remains, except according to Abu Yusuf, who holds that it drops once the time has passed.

Key Terms
دم المتعة (dam al-tamattu'): The sacrificial blood required of a mutamatti' pilgrim who performs umrah before hajj.
طواف الصدر (tawaf al-sadr): The farewell tawaf performed before departing Makkah after completing hajj.
الحائض (al-ha'id): A woman experiencing menstrual bleeding during hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman menstruates after tawaf al-ziyarah but before tawaf al-sadr, what must she do according to the Hanafi school?
A) She must perform tawaf al-sadr after becoming pure.
B) She may leave without tawaf al-sadr permanently.
C) She must send a proxy for tawaf al-sadr.
D) She must repeat the entire hajj.

Key Takeaway
A menstruating woman is exempt from tawaf but must perform all other hajj acts; udhiyah does not substitute dam al-tamattu'; and residents of Makkah may be exempt from tawaf al-sadr depending on the timing of their intention to reside.

Perfume in Ihram: Sheep or Charity?
Definition and ruling on applying perfume while in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on applying perfume in ihram and identify when a sheep (dam) vs. charity (sadaqah) is required, including the intra-Hanafi differences on proportional penalty.

Core Idea
Perfuming a whole limb in ihram requires a sheep; less requires charity.

In this lesson, we explore the rulings on applying perfume while in the state of ihram. The Hanafi school holds that deliberately perfuming a limb is a jinaayah (ihram violation) that incurs a sacrificial sheep. However, if less than a whole limb is perfumed, or if the amount is small, only charity is due. We will unpack the definitions, conditions, and differences among the Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states: 'A sheep is obligatory if a muhrim perfumes a limb; otherwise, he gives charity.' Determine the act (perfuming) and the ruling (obligation of sheep for whole limb, charity for less).
The commentary clarifies that 'limb' means a large limb like head or leg.
2
Distinguish whole limb vs. partial limb
Note that for a full limb, a sheep is wajib; for less than a limb (e.g., half limb, quarter limb), the ruling is sadaqah according to the mainstream view. However, Imam Muhammad holds proportional penalty (e.g., half sheep for half limb).
The text also mentions a reconciliation view based on quantity of perfume.
3
Examine intra-Hanafi differences on 'eating perfume' and washing with soap
Abu Hanifa rules that washing the head with khitmi (soap) or eating much perfume requires a sheep, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say only charity. Understand the basis: Abu Hanifa considers it analogous to direct application; the Sahibayn see consumption as different.
This illustrates how the same act can be classified differently within the school.
4
Apply the reconciliation principle
The preferred view reconciles between limb size and perfume quantity: if the perfume is little, consider the limb; if much, consider the perfume. Practice applying this to scenarios like a few drops on a large limb vs. a handful on a small limb.
This reconciliation is cited as 'the correct one' in the commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الجنايات
أي في بيان أحكامها
تجب شاة إن طيب محرم عضواً، وإلا تصدق
باب الجنايات [هو جمع جناية وهو اسم لفعل محرم شرعا، وفي اصطلاح الفقهاء يطلق على ما يكون في النفوس والأطراف. (ع)] لما بين أحكام المحرمين شرع فيما يعتري الإحرام والجنايات جمع جناية، وهي ما يجنيه من شيء أي يحدثه، أعم من أن يكون الشيء المجنى مباحاً أو محظوراً إلا أنه خص بما يحرم من الفعل. وأصله من "جني الثمر" أخذه وهو من الشجر وهو مصدر وأريد به الحاصل بالمصدر لا المعنى المصدري بدليل جمعها، والمصدر لا يجمع إذا لم يقصد به العدد أو التنويع. (مسكين، فتح)
عليه
محرم عضوا بالغ فلو طيب الحلال عضوا فأحرم فانتقل منه إلى عضو آخر فلا شيء عليه. (ط)] المراد بالعضو أن يكون كبيراً مثل الرأس والساق وغيرهما حتى لو طيب مثل الأذن والأنف وأعضاء العورة لا شيء عليه، وقصد التطيب ليس بشرط، حتى لو أصاب الطيب يده أو فمه عند استلام الركن من غير قصد وكان كثيراً وجب الدم، وفي القليل الصدقة، وقيد بالمحرم؛ لأن الحلال لو طيب عضواً ثم أحرم فانتقل من العضو المطيب إلى عضو آخر لا شيء عليه، وأن يكون عضواً من أعضائه؛ لأنه لو طيب عضو غيره أو ألبسه المخيط لا شيء . إجماعاً، وكذا يجب الشاة لو غسل رأسه بخطمي، أو أكل طيباً كثيراً بأن يلتزق بأكثر فمه عنده. وعندهما: لا يجب شيء في هاتين الصورتين سوى الصدقة؛ لأن الأكل استهلاك لا استعمال، والتقييد بالبالغ؛ لأن فعل الصبي لا يوصف بالجناية؛ لكونه غير مخاطب، وعند الشافعي: إذا ارتكب الصبي محظور الإحرام فيلزمه ما يلزم البالغ، وقيد بالعضو؛ لأنه لو طيب عضوين أو البدن كله نظر إن طيب في مجلس واحد فكذلك يجب دم واحد؛ لأن البدن كله في حكم عضو واحد، وإن طيب كل عضو من الأعضاء في مجلس على حدة يجب لكل عضو دم، سواء طيب العضو الثاني بعد ما ذبح للأول أو قبله عندهما، وكذا عند محمد فيما ذبح للأول، وإن لم يذبح يجب عليه دم واحد. (فتح، مسكين)
ماء
وإلا تصدق القصور الجناية سواء كان العضو ربعا أو أقل، وإن شمّ طيبا كره ولا شيء عليه. (ط)] مطلقا سواء كان ربعا أو أقل منه، وقال محمد: يجب بقدره من الدم حتى إن طيب نصف عضو يتصدق بنصف الشاة أي نصف قيمتها، وقيل: إن طيب ربع العضو يجب الدم أيضاً اعتبارا للتطيب بالحلق، وإن كان دونه تجب الصدقة، وذكر الفقيه أبو جعفر أن الكثرة تعتبر في نفس الطيب لا في العضو، فإن كان كثيراً مثل كفين من الورد، وكف من الغالية، وبقدر ما يستكثره الناس من المسك يكون كثيراً وإن كان قليلاً في نفسه، والقليل ما يستقله الناس وإن كان في نفسه كثيراً، وقيل: بالتوفيق بينهما وهو الصحيح، إن كان الطيب قليلاً فالعبرة للعضو، وإن كان كثيراً فللطيب، ثم اعلم أن في كل موضع وجب فيه الدم تجزئه الشاة إلا من جامع بعد الوقوف بعرفة =
Chapter of Jinayat. i.e., in explanation of its rulings. A sheep is obligatory if a muhrim perfumes a limb; otherwise, he gives charity. Chapter of Jinayat [it is the plural of jinaayah, which is a name for an act forbidden by sharia, and in the terminology of the fuqaha' it is applied to what pertains to lives and limbs. ('A)] After he explained the rulings of the muhrimun, he began with what affects ihram. Jinayat is plural of jinaayah, which is what one commits of something, i.e., what he initiates, general whether the committed thing is permissible or prohibited, except that it is specified to what is forbidden of action. Its origin is from 'janiy al-thamar' (picking fruit), taking it from the tree, and it is a masdar, and what is intended is the product of the masdar, not the masdar meaning, as indicated by its pluralization, and the masdar is not pluralized unless number or diversity is intended. (Miskin, Fath) Upon him: a muhrim, an adult limb; so if a non-muhrim perfumes a limb then enters ihram and transfers from it to another limb, then nothing is upon him. (T) The intended meaning of 'limb' is that it be large such as the head, leg, and others, such that if he perfumes like the ear, nose, or private parts, nothing is upon him. Intent to apply perfume is not a condition, such that if perfume touches his hand or mouth when touching the corner (of the Kaaba) unintentionally and it is much, the blood (sacrifice) is obligatory, and for little, charity. It is restricted to a muhrim because if a non-muhrim perfumes a limb then enters ihram and transfers from the perfumed limb to another limb, nothing is upon him. And that it be a limb of his own; because if he perfumes another's limb or clothes him with stitched clothing, nothing is upon him by consensus. Likewise, a sheep is obligatory if he washes his head with khitmi (soap) or eats much perfume such that it sticks to most of his mouth according to him (Abu Hanifa). According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), nothing is obligatory in these two images except charity, because eating is consumption, not use. The restriction to an adult is because the action of a minor is not described as jinaayah, as he is not addressed. According to al-Shafi'i: if a minor commits a prohibition of ihram, he is liable for what the adult is liable. The restriction to the limb is because if he perfumes two limbs or the whole body, consider: if he perfumed in one sitting, then one blood is obligatory because the whole body is in the rule of one limb; and if he perfumed each limb in a separate sitting, a blood is obligatory for each limb, whether he perfumed the second limb after sacrificing for the first or before it according to the two. Likewise according to Muhammad regarding what he sacrificed for the first, and if he did not sacrifice, one blood is obligatory. (Fath, Miskin) Water: else he gives charity for the deficiency of the jinaayah, whether the limb is a quarter or less. And if he smells perfume, it is disliked and nothing is upon him. (T) Absolutely, whether a quarter or less. And Muhammad said: It is obligatory according to its measure, such that if he perfumes half a limb, he gives charity of half a sheep, i.e., half its value. And it was said: If he perfumes a quarter of a limb, the blood is also obligatory by analogy with shaving; and if less, charity is obligatory. Al-Faqih Abu Ja'far mentioned that abundance is considered in the perfume itself, not the limb; so if it is much, like two handfuls of rose, a handful of ghaliyah, and an amount that people consider much of musk, it is much even if little in itself; and little is what people consider little even if much in itself. And it was said: reconciliation between them is correct: if the perfume is little, the consideration is for the limb; if much, then for the perfume. Then know that wherever blood is obligatory, a sheep suffices, except for one who has intercourse after standing at Arafah =
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage from Bab al-Jinaayat defines jinaayah as an act forbidden in ihram. The matn states that a muhrim who applies perfume to a limb must sacrifice a sheep; if less than a limb, he gives charity. The commentary clarifies that 'limb' means a large limb like the head or leg; small parts like ear, nose, private parts incur no penalty. Intent is not required: if perfume touches unintentionally, the same rule applies based on quantity. The ruling is restricted to an adult muhrim; a child is not liable, though Shafi'i disagrees. If a muhrim perfumes multiple limbs in one sitting, one sheep suffices; if in separate sittings, multiple sheep are required. The commentary also discusses differences: according to Abu Hanifa, washing head with soap or eating much perfume requires a sheep; according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, only charity. For less than a whole limb, Muhammad holds that the penalty is proportional (e.g., half limb = half sheep value). Another view considers perfume quantity: if much, blood; if little, charity regardless of limb size. The preferred view reconciles: if perfume is little, the limb size matters; if much, the quantity matters. Finally, in all cases where a sheep is obligatory, one sheep suffices except for intercourse after standing at Arafah, which requires a camel.

Key Terms
جناية (ج: جنايات) (jinaayah (pl. jinayaat)): An act forbidden by sharia committed during ihram, requiring compensation.
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for hajj or umrah.
شاة (shaat): A sheep or goat, the required sacrificial animal for certain ihram violations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what is required if a muhrim perfumes half a limb?
A) A full sheep
B) Half the value of a sheep as charity
C) Nothing
D) A full sheep plus charity

Key Takeaway
The key ruling: a whole limb perfumed in ihram requires a sheep; less requires charity, with a reconciliation based on perfume quantity.

Rulings on Offenses (Jinayat) During Ihram: Perfume, Wearing Stitched Garments, and Covering Head
Explains rulings for muhrim committing offenses: perfume, dye, oil, clothes, covering head, shaving

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on perfuming a limb during ihram, differentiate when a sheep (shah) versus charity (sadaqah) is required, and apply the day-condition for wearing stitched garments.

Core Idea
Perfuming a large limb during ihram requires a sheep; lesser amounts or small limbs require charity.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq with its commentary establishes the legal framework for offenses (jinayat) during ihram. The key principle is proportionality: the penalty depends on the extent of the benefit derived from the prohibited act. You will learn the exact thresholds for perfume, clothing, and covering the head, and understand why the Hanafi school differs from others on the requirement of a full day for wearing stitched garments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The main ruling: if a muhrim (adult) perfumes a large limb (e.g., head, leg), a sheep (shah) is wajib; if less, charity (sadaqah) is due. Note that intention is not required; accidental application of much perfume also requires blood.
Large limb excludes small parts like ear, nose, private parts.
2
Locate the evidence (dalil)
The hadith: the Prophet (PBUH) said, 'Upon him is blood if he wears it for a day' – this is cited for the day-condition for wearing stitched garments. For perfume, the ruling is based on qiyas (analogy) and general prohibition.
The hadith is the primary proof for the day-condition.
3
Trace the 'illa (effective cause)
The 'illa for requiring a full day is complete benefit: repelling heat and cold requires continuity. A single instant does not achieve this benefit. Similarly, perfume on a large limb achieves significant benefit.
This 'illa explains why Shafi'i's view (immediate blood) is rejected.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa requires blood for washing head with khatmi or eating much perfume; Sahibayn only require charity because eating is consumption, not use. For oiling with pure oil (intended as perfume), Abu Hanifa says blood; Sahibayn say charity because it is like food with some benefit.
The mufta bihi for oil is the Sahibayn's view (charity).
5
Apply the tarjih (preponderance)
For the day-condition, the Hanafi position is based on the explicit hadith and is mufta bihi. For perfume quantity, the correct view is reconciliation: if perfume is little, consider the limb; if much, consider the perfume itself.
This ensures justice: minor offenses require minor penalties.

Book of Hajj, Chapter of Offenses: meaning in explanation of its rulings. A sheep becomes obligatory if a muhrim perfumes a limb, otherwise he gives charity. Chapter of Offenses: it is a plural of 'jinaya', which is a name for an act forbidden by law, and in the terminology of jurists it is applied to what pertains to lives and limbs. (Ayni) After explaining the rulings of muhrims, he discusses what affects ihram. Offenses plural of jinaya, which is what one commits (i.e., brings about) – general whether the thing committed is permissible or prohibited, but it is specified to what is forbidden of action. Its root is from 'jani al-thamar' (picking fruit), taking it from the tree, and it is a masdar but intended is the product of the masdar not the masdar meaning, evidenced by its pluralization; the masdar is not pluralized unless number or variety is intended. (Miskin, Fath). Upon him: a muhrim (who is) an adult limb. If a halal person perfumes a limb then enters ihram, then it transfers to another limb, nothing upon him. (T.) The meaning of limb is that it be large like the head, leg etc. such that if he perfumes like the ear, nose, private parts, nothing upon him. Intention of perfuming is not a condition, even if perfume touches his hand or mouth when touching the corner (of the Kaaba) unintentionally and it is much, blood (i.e., sacrifice) is obligatory; for little, charity. Restricted to muhrim because if a halal person perfumed a limb then entered ihram and the perfume transferred to another limb, nothing upon him. And that it be from his own limbs because if he perfumed another's limb or dressed him in stitched garment, nothing by consensus. Similarly, a sheep becomes obligatory if he washes his head with a plant (khatmi) or eats much perfume such that it sticks to most of his mouth, according to him (Abu Hanifa). According to both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), nothing is obligatory in these two cases except charity, because eating is consumption not usage. The restriction to adult because the act of a child is not described as an offense due to being not addressed (by commandments). According to al-Shafi'i, if a child commits a prohibition of ihram, what is incumbent on an adult becomes incumbent on him. Restricted to limb because if he perfumed two limbs or the entire body, then if he perfumed in one sitting, one blood (sacrifice) is obligatory because the entire body is considered one limb. If he perfumed each limb separately in distinct sittings, for each limb a blood (sacrifice) is obligatory, whether he perfumed the second limb after slaughtering for the first or before according to both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Similarly according to Muhammad if he had slaughtered for the first; if he did not slaughter, one blood becomes obligatory (Fath, Miskin). [Water] And otherwise he gives charity due to the inadequacy of the offense, whether the limb be a quarter or less. And if he smells perfume it is disliked and nothing upon him (T). Absolutely whether it is a quarter or less. Muhammad said: proportional to it from the blood (sacrifice) such that if he perfumed half a limb, he gives charity half of a sheep i.e., half its value. It is said: if he perfumed a quarter of a limb, blood becomes obligatory as well considering perfuming like shaving; if less, charity becomes obligatory. Faqih Abu Ja'far mentioned that quantity is considered in the perfume itself, not the limb. Then if it is much, like two handfuls of rose, one handful of ghaliya, and as much as people consider much of musk, it is much even if it is little in itself. The little is what people consider little even if it is much in itself. And it is said: reconciliation between them is the correct view: if the perfume is little, the consideration is for the limb; if much, then for the perfume. Then know that in every place where blood (sacrifice) is obligatory, a sheep suffices, except for one who has intercourse after standing at Arafah: [page break] Book of Hajj, page 288, Chapter of Offenses. Or he dyes his head with henna, or oils with oil, or wears a stitched garment, or covers his head for a day, otherwise a complete [day] or a complete night; he gives charity, or shaves, due to inadequacy of the offense. And he performs Tawaf al-Ziyarah while junub, menstruating, or postpartum; then only a camel (badanah) suffices. And every place where charity is obligatory, it is half a sa' of wheat or a sa' of dates or a sa' of barley, except what is obligatory for killing a locust or louse or removing a few hairs, then he gives charity as he wishes. (Ramz al-Haqaiq: 170/1) Or dyes: conjuncted to his statement 'perfumed', i.e., a sheep becomes obligatory if he dyes (Ayni) his head with henna – with lengthened alif and nunation, declinable; because of his (PBUH) statement: 'Henna is a perfume.' He mentioned both henna and head separately, although they are included under perfume and limb, because it is hidden that henna is perfume, and to specify that the head is an independent limb. Similarly, if she dyes her hand with henna. This when the henna is liquid; if it is clotted, then another (obligation) upon him for covering the head. Restricted to henna because if he dyes his head with wasma (a plant), nothing upon him because it is not a perfume (Miskin, Ayni). Or oils with oil: i.e., also obligatory if he oils (Ayni). Similarly if he oils with vinegar, unlike fat and ghee where nothing is obligatory. This when intending perfuming. As for if he treats his wound or cracks in his feet or puts drops in his ear, nothing upon him by consensus, because it is not a perfume in itself; rather it is the origin of perfume, so its use is conditional upon the manner of perfuming, whether used on hair or other. Obligation of blood according to Abu Hanifa, and both (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said charity is obligatory because it is from the edibles except that there is a kind of benefit meaning killing insects and removing dishevelment, so it is a deficient offense. Al-Shafi'i said: if he uses it on hair, blood is obligatory; otherwise nothing upon him, because on hair it removes dishevelment unlike other hair. This difference is for pure oil, i.e., pure that is not mixed with perfume. As for perfumed with violet, lily, ban, etc., blood is obligatory by consensus (Miskin, Ayni). Stitched garment: i.e., a stitched garment for a complete day even if he cannot find other, unlike if he puts on a shirt or wraps a sarong, no harm (T). Or covers his head for a day: this is a restriction for wearing; covering for a complete night like a day. Al-Shafi'i said: blood is obligatory by the very act of wearing because it is a prohibition of ihram. We say: complete benefit is not achieved except by continuity, because the purpose is repelling heat and cold, and the day encompasses both, so it is measure by it. From Abu Yusuf: if he wears more than half a day, blood is obligatory. And we have: he (PBUH) was asked about a muhrim wearing stitched garment, so he said: 'Upon him is blood if he wears it for a day.' From Muhammad: if he wears it for part of a day, blood is obligatory proportionally. And if the garments are all of shirt, cloak, trousers, and socks for a complete day, one blood suffices because they are of one type. Similarly if he continues for days. Similarly if he removes it at night and wears during the day, except if he removes with intention to abandon then wears again, then another blood becomes obligatory (Fath, Ayni). His head: with what is customarily used to cover, like a turban; if with something like a basin, nothing upon him (T). And otherwise he gives charity: meaning if he did not wear or cover for a complete day, but less than a day (Ramz al-Haqaiq: 170/1). Or shaves: conjuncted to what preceded that which requires blood, i.e., blood becomes obligatory if he shaves (Ayni).
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This is an expansion (sharh) of the matn of Kanz al-Daqaiq on the chapter of jinayat (offenses) during ihram. The author first defines jinayat linguistically and technically. The main ruling: a muhrim who perfumes a large limb with perfume must sacrifice a sheep; if the limb is smaller or the perfume little, he gives charity (sadaqah). The commentary discusses details: what constitutes a limb (head, leg, etc., not small parts like ear, nose, private parts); intention is not necessary—accidental application of much perfume requires blood; if perfume transfers from a halal state to ihram, nothing is due. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding washing head with khatmi or eating perfume: Abu Hanifa requires a sheep, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) only require charity, because eating is consumption not use. The passage also addresses a child's offense: according to Shafi'i a child's prohibited act incurs the same as an adult, but Hanafis hold no offense because a child is not legally accountable. If multiple limbs are perfumed in one sitting, one blood suffices; if in separate sittings, multiple bloods are due. The commentary also discusses quantity: Muhammad requires proportional charity for half a limb; other opinions consider a quarter limb sufficient for blood; the correct view reconciles by looking at the perfume quantity—if little, consider limb; if much, consider perfume. Exceptions: for intercourse after Arafah, a camel (badanah) is required instead of sheep. The passage then lists other offenses: dyeing hair with henna (requires blood because henna is a perfume); oiling with pure oil (if intended as perfume, blood according to Abu Hanifa, charity according to Sahibayn because it is like food with some benefit); wearing a stitched garment for a full day (blood required; if less, charity); covering the head for a full day (like wearing); shaving (blood). The hadith regarding wearing a stitched garment for a day is cited as proof for the day requirement. The commentary also notes that wearing multiple stitched garments of different types in one day still requires only one blood because they are of one category. If one continues wearing for multiple days, no additional blood unless there is an interruption with intention to abandon. Finally, the measure of charity: generally half a sa' of wheat, one sa' of dates or barley, except for killing a locust or louse or removing few hairs where charity is discretionary.

Key Terms
جناية (jināyah): An offense committed during ihram, whether by a permissible or prohibited act, but specifically what is forbidden. Technically, it refers to acts that are prohibited for a muhrim.
محرم (muḥrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, and is thus subject to its prohibitions.
شاة (shāh): A sheep or goat; the animal required to be sacrificed as penalty (dam) for certain offenses during ihram.
صدقة (ṣadaqah): Charity given as a lesser penalty for minor offenses during ihram. The amount is generally half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates/barley.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a muhrim wears a stitched shirt for half a day, what penalty is required?
A) No penalty
B) Charity (sadaqah)
C) A sheep (shah)
D) A camel (badanah)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes a clear quantitative threshold for jinayat during ihram: a complete day for wearing stitched garments, a full large limb for perfume, and distinguishes between blood and charity based on the extent of the benefit derived from the offense.

Rulings on Dyeing with Henna and Oiling During Ihram
Explains when dam or sadaqah is due for using henna or oil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on using henna and oil during ihram and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding oil.

Core Idea
Henna as perfume obligates a dam; oil's ruling divides Abu Hanifa (dam) from Sahibayn (sadaqah).

In this passage, the commentator expands on the matn that any perfume applied during ihram requires a sacrificial animal (dam). Two specific cases are examined: dyeing with henna and anointing with pure oil. Understanding the classification of these substances as perfume or not, and the intent behind their use, determines when compensation is due. The passage also highlights an intra-Hanafi disagreement on the severity of using oil.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling for henna
The text states that if a person dyes his head with henna during ihram, a sheep (dam) is obligatory. The proof is the hadith: 'Henna is a perfume.'
Henna is considered a perfume, therefore its use triggers the prohibition of perfume during ihram.
2
Understand the conditions for henna
The ruling applies only when henna is liquid; if it is clumped (muthalbid), it becomes covering the head, requiring another dam for covering. Also, it is specific to henna; other dyes like wasma (indigo) do not obligate anything.
The commentator explains that the head is specified as an independent limb, so dyeing other limbs like the hand also obligates dam.
3
Analyze the ruling for oil
Anointing with pure oil (zayt) with the intention of perfuming obligates dam according to Abu Hanifa. If used for medicinal purposes (wound, cracked feet, ear drops), nothing is due by consensus.
The same applies to vinegar. Fat (shahm) and ghee (samn) do not obligate anything even if used for perfume.
4
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute on oil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that only sadaqah (charity) is required, not dam, because oil is not a pure perfume; it has benefits like killing insects and removing dishevelment, making it a deficient offense (jinaayah qaasirah).
The text presents this difference without explicit tarjih.
5
Compare with the Shafi'i position
Al-Shafi'i differentiates: if oil is used on hair, dam is obligatory; if used on other parts, nothing is due. This disagreement is limited to pure oil; scented oils (with violet, lily, etc.) require dam by consensus.
This shows the importance of texture and the origin of perfume in determining the ruling.

أو خضب عطف على قوله: "طيب" أي تجب شاة إن خضب. (ع) رأسه بحناء بالمد والتنوين منصرف؛ لقوله عليه: "الحناء طيب"، وأفرد كلا من الحناء والرأس بالذكر وإن كانا داخلين تحت الطيب والعضو؛ لخفاء كون الحناء طيبا دم وتنصيصا على أن الرأس عضو مستقل، وكذا لو خضبت يدها بالحناء، وهذا إذا كان الحناء مائعاً، فإن كان متلبداً فعليه آخر؛ لتغطية الرأس، وقيد بالحناء؛ لأنه إن خضب رأسه بالوسمة لا شيء عليه؛ لأنها ليست بطيب. (مسكين، عيني)
Or dyed: it is conjuncted to his saying: "perfume", i.e., a sheep is obligatory if he dyes. His head with henna (with madd and tanwin, fully declinable); due to his statement (peace be upon him): "Henna is a perfume." He mentioned both henna and head separately, although both are included under perfume and limb, because it is hidden that henna is perfume, and to specify that the head is an independent limb. Similarly if she dyes her hand with henna. This is when the henna is liquid; if it is clumped, then on him is another (dam) for covering the head. He restricted it to henna because if he dyes his head with wasma, nothing is on him because it is not perfume. Or anointed with oil: i.e., it is obligatory also if he anoints. This is when it is with the intention of perfuming; as for if he treated a wound or cracks in his feet or drops it in his ear, nothing is on him by consensus, because it is not perfume itself, rather it is the origin of perfume, so its use is conditioned on the manner of perfuming, whether used on hair or other. Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding two specific acts during ihram: dyeing the head with henna and anointing with oil. The author, commenting on the matn, states that dyeing with henna obligates a sheep (dam) because the Prophet (peace be upon him) declared henna a perfume. The head is specified as an independent limb. Henna must be liquid; if clumped, it becomes covering the head, requiring another dam. If dyeing with wasma (indigo), nothing is due. For oiling, if done with intent to perfume, dam is obligatory according to Abu Hanifa; the Sahibayn say sadaqah (half sa' of wheat, etc.) is due because it is a deficient offense (jinaayah qaasirah). Shafi'i differentiates between hair and other body parts. Scented oils (mukhallat) obligate dam by consensus.

Key Terms
الحناء (al-hinna'): A plant used for dyeing; considered a perfume (tib) in this context.
الزيت (al-zayt): Oil, specifically olive oil or other pure oils; used for anointing.
الدم (al-dam): A sacrificial animal (sheep or goat) required as compensation for certain ihram violations.

Henna and oil used with perfuming intent obligate compensation; the Sahibayn view oil as a lesser offense requiring only sadaqah.

Rulings on Wearing Sewn Clothes and Covering Head
Explains when dam is due for wearing sewn clothes or covering head fully

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when dam is due for wearing sewn clothes during ihram and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A full day's use triggers dam — duration matters because benefit requires continuity.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq clarifies the precise conditions under which a muhrim incurs a dam for wearing sewn garments or covering the head. While the prohibition is clear, the Hanafi school uniquely ties the obligation of dam to the duration of use, a principle supported by hadith and legal reasoning. Understanding this condition prevents unnecessary expiation and prepares you for more advanced rulings on ihram violations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited acts and their default ruling
The text covers two prohibited acts: wearing sewn clothes (makhit) and covering the head (taghtiya) during ihram. Both are prohibited, but the dam is conditional. First, note what constitutes sewn clothes (any tailored garment) and head covering (customary items like a turban).
An act like wrapping a sheet is not considered sewn clothes.
2
Determine the condition for dam: full day (or night)
The matn explicitly ties the dam to a full day (yawman kamilan) or a full night. This is the key condition. Understand that the reasoning behind this duration is that the complete benefit of the garment (repelling heat/cold) is only achieved over a full day.
A partial day, even if it is most of it, does not trigger dam according to the relied-upon position.
3
Examine the proof: hadith and its implication
The commentator cites a hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) said, 'عليه دم إذا لبس يوما' (He must give a dam if he wears for a day). This explicitly states the day condition. In Hanafi usul, a general command is binding, and the qualifying phrase 'a day' sets a threshold.
The hadith is ahad, thus zanni in thubut, but its meaning is clear (zanni dalala).
4
Compare intra-Hanafi views and the relied position
Two other Hanafi imams differ on the threshold: Abu Yusuf says dam for more than half a day; Muhammad says proportionate dam for any part. The relied position (mufta bihi) is the Zahir al-Riwayah: only a full day (or night) requires dam; less requires sadaqah.
The preferred view is based on the explicit hadith and the principle that the benefit of a garment is complete only over a full cycle of day and night.
5
Analyze the Shafi'i dispute and the Hanafi response
Al-Shafi'i holds that dam is due immediately upon wearing because the prohibition is instant. The Hanafi response is that the hadith conditions the dam on duration, and the underlying reason (repelling extremes) requires continuity. This shows how textual evidence and reasoning (ta'lil) together determine the ruling.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf): Shafi'i: dam for any wearing; Hanafi: dam only after a full day, otherwise sadaqah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مخيطاً: أي ثوباً مخيطا يوما كاملا وإن لم يجد غيره، بخلاف ما لو ارتدى بقميص أو اتزر بالسراويل فلا بأس به. (ط) أو غطى رأسه يوماً : هو قيد في اللبس، والتغطية الليلة الكاملة كاليوم، وقال الشافعي: يجب الدم بنفس اللبس؛ لأنه محظور إحرامه قلنا الارتفاق الكامل لا يحصل إلا بالدوام؛ لأن المقصود منه دفع الحر والبرد، واليوم يشملهما فقدر به، وعن أبي يوسف إذا لبس أكثر من نصف يوم فعليه دم ولنا: أنه عليها سئل عن محرم يلبس مخيطا، فقال عليه : عليه دم إذا لبس يوما"، وعن محمد: إن لبسه في بعض اليوم يجب عليه من الدم ،بحسابه ولو كان اللباس كلها من قميص وقباء وسراويل وخفين يوماً كاملاً لزمه دم واحد؛ لأنها من جنس واحد، وكذا لو دام أياماً، وكذا لو نزعه بالليل ولبسه بالنهار إلا إذا نزعه على عزم الترك ثم لبسه فإنه يجب عليه دم آخر. (فتح، عيني) رأسه: بما يغطى به عادة كالعمامة، فلو بنحو طست فلا شيء عليه. (ط) وإلا تصدق أي وإن لم يلبس ولم يغط يوماً كاملاً، بل أقل من يوم.
Sewn: i.e., a sewn garment for a complete day, even if he does not find other than it, unlike if he wraps a shirt or loincloth with trousers, there is no harm. Or covered his head for a day: this is a condition in wearing, and covering for a complete night is like a day. Al-Shafi'i said: Dam is obligatory by the mere wearing because it is a prohibition of ihram. We said: Complete benefit is only obtained by continuity, because the purpose is to repel heat and cold, and the day encompasses both so it is estimated by it. From Abu Yusuf: if he wears more than half a day, dam is due. And we have: that he (peace be upon him) was asked about a muhrim wearing sewn clothes, so he said: 'He must give a dam if he wears for a day.' And from Muhammad: if he wears for part of a day, on him is dam proportionately. And if the entire clothing is a shirt, cloak, trousers, and socks for a full day, one dam is incumbent because they are of one type; similarly if he continues days; similarly if he removes at night and wears during the day, except if he removes with intention to abandon then wears, then another dam is due. His head: with what is customarily used to cover, like a turban; if with something like a basin, nothing is on him. Commentary
This passage details the ruling on wearing sewn clothes (makhit) and covering the head during ihram. The matn states these require a dam if done for a full day (or night). The commentator explains that the condition of a full day is based on the purpose of benefit: to repel heat and cold, which the day encompasses. Shafi'i holds that merely wearing obligates dam, but the author refutes by citing a hadith that specifies 'a day' and by reasoning that complete benefit requires duration. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad have different views on partial duration. If one wears multiple garments, only one dam is due unless there is a clear break with intent to abandon. Covering the head applies only to customary coverings like a turban; unconventional objects like a basin incur nothing. If less than a full day, sadaqah is due.

Key Terms
المخيط (al-makhit): A sewn garment; specifically any garment tailored to fit the body, like a shirt or trousers.
التغطية (al-taghtiya): Covering the head with something customarily used, like a turban or hat.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a full day (or night) of wearing sewn clothes or covering the head during ihram before a dam becomes obligatory; less than that only requires sadaqah.

The Quarter Rule for Shaving in Ihram: Hanafi Threshold for Dam
Explains the quarter threshold for dam and rebuts other schools.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi threshold (quarter) for dam when shaving head or beard during ihram and explain the proof based on custom.

Core Idea
A quarter of head or beard is the minimum for dam; less requires sadaqah.

This lesson addresses a key dispute among madhhabs: how much hair must be shaved during ihram to obligate a dam? The Hanafi school, relying on custom, sets the threshold at one quarter. We will examine the proofs and counter-arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The author states: shaving a quarter of head or beard requires a dam; less requires sadaqah. Note the ruling categories.
The ruling distinguishes between dam (compulsory) and sadaqah (charity).
2
Understand the dispute with Malik
Malik required shaving the entire head for dam. The Hanafi response: a quarter achieves complete benefit and is customary.
Malik's position is stricter.
3
Understand the dispute with Shafi'i
Shafi'i held that even three hairs obligate a dam. The Hanafi response: that would make it too easy to violate the prohibition.
Shafi'i's position is more lenient.
4
Examine the Hanafi proof
The proof is based on custom ('urf): shaving a quarter is common among Alawites and Iraqis, and provides complete benefit (izalat al-tafath).
Qiyas jaliy: quarter is like the whole in achieving benefit.
5
Apply the ruling
Given a scenario of shaving less than a quarter, state the compensation: sadaqah of half a sa'.
The text specifies sadaqah for less than a quarter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو حلق عطف على ما قبله من الذي فيه الدم أي يجب دم إن حلق. (ع) ربع رأسه أو لحيته وإلا تصدق كالخالق، أو رقبته أو إبطيه أو أحدهما أو محجمه، وإن لم يكن قدر الربع أي حلقها أي حلق ربع رأسه أو لحيته وقال مالك: لا يجب الدم إلا بحلق الكل، وقال الشافعي: يجب بحلق القليل؛ لأن الشعر استفاد أمناً بالإحرام، فيجب بنتف ثلاث شعرات دمّ، وفي واحدة ثلث ،دم ولنا أن حلق ربع الرأس فيه ارتفاق كامل، لأنه معتاد؛ لأن بعض العلوية يحلقون نواصيهم وأخذ الربع من اللحية معتاد بأراضي العراق والعرب، فلهذا كان حلق الربع ملحقاً بحلق الكل، بخلاف ما دون الربع. (فتح) وإلا تصدق: لقصور الجناية، أي وإن لم يكن قدر الربع بل أقل منه (ط، ع) كالحالق: [ أي كتصدق الحالق شعر رأس غيره سواء كان الغير محرماً أو لا. (ط، ع)] اعلم أن المسألة بالقسمة العقلية على أربعة أقسام: الأول: أن يكونا محرمين فيجب على الحالق الصدقة وعلى المحلوق الدم، والثاني: أن يكون الحالق حلالاً والمحلوق محرماً فكذلك الحكم فيه، والثالث: أن يكون الحالق محرماً والمحلوق حلالاً فيجب على الحالق الصدقة لا غير، وهو المذكور في المتن، والرابع: أن يكونا حلالين فلا يجب عليهما شيء، والصدقة مقدرة بنصف صاع إلا في الوجه الثالث، وقال الشافعي: لا شيء على الحالق؛ لحصول الارتفاق للمحلوق دون الحالق؛ لأن فعله إرفاق ليس بارتفاق ولكن يأثم. قلنا: إن الارتفاق حصل له أيضاً من وجه؛ إذ الإنسان يتأذى بتفث غيره كتأذيته بتفث نفسه، لكن لما كملت الجناية بإزالة تفث نفسه لزمه دم بخلاف إزالة تفت غيره لقصورها، فلهذا اكتفى فيه بالصدقة، ويجب دم على المحلوق المحرم مطلقاً سواء كان الحلق بأمره أو لا، بأن كان نائماً أو مكرهاً أو ناسياً، ولا رجوع له على الحالق عندنا، وقال الشافعي: لا يجب إذا كان بغير أمره؛ لأنه إن كان مكرهاً رجع حكم الفعل على المكره، وكذا إن كان نائماً حكم فعله على الحالق بالطريق الأولى؛ لأنه لا اختيار له أصلاً، قلنا: إن أثر الفعل الذي هو الارتفاق حصل للمحلوق فيلزمه الجزاء، وبالإكراه ينتفي الإثم دون الحكم، كما إذا وطئ مكرهاً يلزمه الاغتسال. (مسكين، فتح)
Or shaved: conjuncted to what preceded of that which has dam, i.e., dam is obligatory if he shaves. A quarter of his head or beard, and if not, he gives sadaqah like the one who shaves. Or his neck, or armpits, or one of them, or the place of cupping. If it is not the amount of a quarter, i.e., he shaved less than a quarter of his head or beard. Malik said: Dam is not obligatory except by shaving the whole. Al-Shafi'i said: Dam is obligatory by shaving a little, because the hair gained security by ihram; so by pulling out three hairs a dam is due, and for one hair a third of a dam. And we (Hanafi) hold that shaving a quarter of the head contains complete benefit because it is customary; since some of the Alawites shave their forelocks, and taking a quarter of the beard is customary in the lands of Iraq and the Arabs, so shaving a quarter is joined to shaving the whole, unlike less than a quarter. Otherwise give sadaqah: due to the deficiency of the offense, i.e., if it is not the amount of a quarter but less. Like the shaver: i.e., like the sadaqah of the one who shaves someone else's hair, whether the other is muhrim or not. Know that the issue in rational division is four categories: First: both are muhrim — then on the shaver is sadaqah and on the one shaved is dam. Second: the shaver is non-muhrim and the one shaved is muhrim — the same ruling. Third: the shaver is muhrim and the one shaved is non-muhrim — on the shaver is sadaqah only, which is mentioned in the matn. Fourth: both are non-muhrim — nothing is due. The sadaqah is measured as half a sa' except in the third case. Al-Shafi'i said: Nothing is on the shaver because the benefit goes to the one shaved, not the shaver; his action is assistance, not benefit, but he sins. We said: Benefit also occurs to him in a way, because a person is harmed by the untidiness of others as he is harmed by his own untidiness. But since the offense is complete by removing his own untidiness, dam is due; by removing another's untidiness it is deficient, so sadaqah suffices. And dam is obligatory on the shaved muhrim absolutely, whether the shaving was by his order or not, even if he was sleeping, coerced, or forgetful; and he has no recourse against the shaver according to us. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not obligatory if it is without his order, because if coerced, the ruling of the act returns to the coercer, similarly if sleeping, the ruling goes to the shaver a fortiori because he has no choice at all. We said: The effect of the act, which is benefit, occurred to the shaved, so compensation is due; coercion removes sin but not the legal effect, as in the case of one who is coerced into intercourse, he must perform ghusl.
Source pages p. 289

Commentary
This passage covers the rulings for shaving during ihram. The matn states that shaving a quarter of the head or beard requires a dam; less requires sadaqah. The commentator refutes Malik (requires full head) and Shafi'i (requires dam even for three hairs) on the basis of custom: a quarter is customary and constitutes complete benefit. The text then discusses shaving by another person, dividing cases into four categories based on the ihram status of shaver and shaved. The shaver always gives sadaqah if he is muhrim or if the shaved is muhrim; the shaved muhrim always gives dam, even if coerced or sleeping. The dispute with Shafi'i on whether the shaved owes dam without consent is resolved by analogy to coerced intercourse where ghusl is still obligatory.

Key Terms
الربع (al-rub'): A quarter of the head or beard; the threshold for dam.
الصدقة (al-sadaqah): Charity (half a sa') given as compensation for shaving less than a quarter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the minimum amount of hair that must be shaved from the head during ihram to require a dam?
A) Any amount
B) Half the head
C) One quarter of the head
D) The entire head

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, shaving a quarter or more of the head or beard during ihram requires a dam; less requires sadaqah.

Shaving Another's Hair in Ihram: Four Cases and Obligations
Expands the shaver ruling into a four-case analysis with proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on compensation when one person shaves another's hair during ihram, distinguishing the four cases based on ihram status.

Core Idea
The shaved muhrim always owes dam; the shaver owes sadaqah except when both are non-muhrim.

The matn briefly mentions the shaver's ruling, but the commentary expands it into a detailed four-case analysis. This lesson clarifies the obligations for both parties involved in shaving during ihram, including disputes with Shafi'i.

Guided Path
1
List the four cases
The commentator divides the scenario into four cases based on whether the shaver and the one shaved are muhrim or not.
Case 1: both muhrim; Case 2: shaver non-muhrim, shaved muhrim; Case 3: shaver muhrim, shaved non-muhrim; Case 4: both non-muhrim.
2
Identify the ruling for each case
For cases 1 and 2: shaver gives sadaqah, shaved gives dam. For case 3: shaver gives sadaqah only. For case 4: nothing.
The shaved muhrim always gives dam. The shaver only gives sadaqah if he is muhrim or the other is muhrim.
3
Examine the dispute with Shafi'i
Shafi'i argued that the shaver owes nothing because benefit goes to the shaved. The Hanafi response: the shaver also benefits indirectly by removing the other's untidiness.
The dispute focuses on whether the shaver obtains any benefit (irtifaq).
4
Understand the ruling for the shaved muhrim
The shaved muhrim owes dam absolutely, even if coerced, asleep, or forgetful. The Hanafi proof: the effect (benefit) occurred to him, so compensation is due; coercion only removes sin.
Analogy: a person coerced into intercourse must still perform ghusl.
5
Apply the ruling to a new scenario
Given a situation where a non-muhrim shaves a muhrim's hair without his consent, state the obligations of each.
Shaver: sadaqah. Shaved: dam (absolutely).

Rulings on Shaving Neck, Armpits, and Cupping Site during Ihram
Explains that shaving these body parts requires dam, with partial shaving requiring sadaqah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for shaving various body parts during ihram and explain the Hanafi position on cupping-related shaving, including the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Shaving a complete limb in ihram requires a dam; shaving part requires sadaqah; for cupping, ruling depends on intention.

This passage continues the discussion on shaving during ihram, now covering the neck, armpits, chest, and the cupping site. It establishes that shaving an entire limb obligates a dam, while shaving only part requires sadaqah. The text also addresses a dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding shaving for cupping, a subtle case of qiyas khafi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
List the body parts mentioned (neck, pubes, chest, leg, armpits, mahjam) and note that shaving the entire limb requires a dam (sheep), while shaving part requires sadaqah.
The ruling applies to each listed limb individually.
2
Understand the principle for multiple similar offenses
If shaving both armpits, only one dam is due because all shaving offenses from one jenis (type) are lumped together into one penalty.
This answers the hypothetical objection about two armpits.
3
Examine the cupping scenario
Shaving the cupping site is a means to cupping. If the person shaves and then performs cupping, it is considered intentional and a dam is due. If he shaves without cupping, only sadaqah is due because it is not intended.
This is Abu Hanifa's position.
4
Contrast Sahibayn's view
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that no compensation is due for shaving related to cupping because the Prophet (peace be upon him) underwent cupping while in ihram without paying compensation.
They also argue that the amount of hair is minimal.
5
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The author (al-Marghinani) responds that the Prophet's action may have been due to an excuse or that the cupping was in a hairless area; thus it does not prove that cupping-related shaving is exempt. The Hanafi view is preferred because the shaving is intended as a means.
This is a classic case of qiyas khafi (subtle analogy).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو رقبته بالنصب عطف على قوله: ربع رأسه أي حلق رقبته كلها أو عانته أو صدره أو ساقه. (ط) أو محجمه بفتح الجيم موضع الحجامة، وبالكسر قارورة الحجام، أي يجب دم في حلق أحد هذه الأشياء، وإن حلق بعض واحد يجب صدقة، فإن قلت: كان ينبغي في حلق الإبطين أن يجب دمان؛ إذ كل إبط عضو مقصود بالحلق؟ قلت: الأصل في جنايات الإحرام إذا كانت من جنس واحد أن يجب دم واحد، وحلق المحجم مقيد إذا كان الحلق وسيلة إلى الحجامة أي حلق ،واحتجم فلو حلق و لم يحتجم لزمه صدقة؛ لأنه غير مقصود، وقالا: لا تحب الصدقة في الحجامة؛ لأنه عليه احتجم وهو محرم ، ولو كان يوجب الدم لما باشره؛ ولأنه قليل فلا يوجب الدم كما إذا حلقه بغير الحجامة وللإمام أن حلقه لمن يحتجم مقصود وهو المعتبر بخلاف الحلق لغيرها، ولا حجة لهما في ما رويا؛ لأنه يحتمل أن يكون لعذر ، ألا ترى أنه عليها لا يباشر ما يوجب الصدقة علينا أيضاً، ويحتمل أنه لم يحلق، بل احتجم في موضع لا شعر فيه، ولم يعتبر الربع في هذه الأعضاء؛ لعدم جريان العادة فيها للاقتصار على البعض،
Or his neck, in accusative, conjuncted to his saying: quarter of his head, i.e., shaving all of his neck, or pubes, or chest, or leg. Or his mahjam (place of cupping) with fatha on jim, and with kasra meaning the cupping glass. I.e., a dam is obligatory for shaving one of these things; if he shaves part of one, sadaqah is obligatory. If you say: It should be that for shaving both armpits, two dams are required, since each armpit is a limb intended for shaving? I say: The principle in ihram offenses when they are of one type is that one dam is obligatory. And shaving the place of cupping is conditioned when the shaving is a means to cupping, i.e., he shaved and then performed cupping. So if he shaved and did not perform cupping, sadaqah is due because it is not intended. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Sadaqah is not obligatory in cupping because he (peace be upon him) performed cupping while in ihram, and if it required a dam he would not have done it; and because it is little, so it does not require dam as if he shaved without cupping. But for the Imam (Abu Hanifa) that shaving for one who is cupped is intended and thus considered, unlike shaving for other purposes. And there is no proof for them (the two) in what they narrated because it is possible that was due to an excuse. Do you not see that he (peace be upon him) did not do what requires sadaqah for us as well? And it is possible that he did not shave but rather was cupped in a place without hair. And the quarter rule is not considered in these limbs because there is no custom of limiting to part of them.
Source pages p. 290

Commentary
This passage completes the discussion of shaving during ihram, now focusing on other body parts: neck, pubes, chest, leg, armpits, and the cupping site (mahjam). Shaving the entire limb requires a dam; shaving part requires sadaqah. The author addresses a potential objection: why is only one dam due for shaving both armpits? The answer is that all parts are considered one type of offense. For cupping, the shaving is only a means to cupping; if one shaves without cupping, sadaqah is due because it is unintended. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argue that cupping itself never requires sadaqah because the Prophet (peace be upon him) underwent cupping during ihram. The author rebuts that the Prophet's case may have been due to an excuse or that the cupping was in a hairless area. The quarter rule (rub') does not apply to these limbs because there is no customary portion.

Key Terms
المحجم (al-mahjam): The place where cupping is performed, usually on the back or shoulder.
الحجامة (al-hijama): Cupping; a medical procedure that may involve shaving the area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the ruling if a person in ihram shaves his neck completely?
A) No compensation
B) Sadaqah
C) A dam (sheep)
D) Invalidates ihram

Key Takeaway
Shaving a complete limb during ihram incurs a dam; shaving part incurs sadaqah; for cupping, the intention determines the compensation.

Quarter Threshold for Shaving in Ihram: Hanafi Position and Dispute
Ruling with inter-madhhab dispute and expansion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shaving part of the head/beard in ihram and explain the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the threshold for a blood penalty.

Core Idea
Shaving a quarter of head/beard in ihram requires dam; less than quarter requires charity.

This lesson tackles a common ihram violation: shaving hair. The Hanafi school, relying on custom (urf), sets a clear threshold—a quarter of the head or beard—for a full blood penalty. Anything less triggers only charity. We will examine the reasoning behind this ruling and how it differs from the Shafi'i position, which imposes a penalty for even a few strands.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling from the text: shaving a quarter of the head or beard requires a blood penalty (dam); less than a quarter requires charity (sadaqah). Note that the text also covers shaving another's hair.
The matn says: 'ربع رأسه أو لحيته وإلا تصدق'
2
Identify the opposing schools and their proofs
Malik requires shaving all; Shafi'i requires dam for any amount (e.g., three hairs). Understand their dalil: Shafi'i says hair gains security from ihram, so removing any amount violates that security.
Shafi'i analogy is with other ihram restrictions where any violation triggers penalty.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response argues that complete relief (irtifaq) is achieved with a quarter due to custom. Shaving a quarter is treated as shaving the whole. Less than that is deficient, so only charity suffices.
The rebuttal also addresses the shaver's liability by considering the effect on both parties.
4
Examine the four-case rational division
The text expands the ruling into four scenarios based on the ihram status of shaver and shaved. Work through each: (1) both muhrim, (2) shaver halal/shawed muhrim, (3) shaver muhrim/shawed halal, (4) both halal. Note the differing obligations.
Only case (3) is explicitly in the matn; the commentary adds the others.
5
Apply the ruling to the issue of coercion
A muhrim who is shaved against his will still owes dam because the relief (irtifaq) occurs. Coercion removes sin but not the legal consequence, analogized to coerced intercourse requiring ghusl.
This shows Hanafi focus on objective effect rather than subjective intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
